Brave's silent-failure-on-Add-to-Home-Screen is the same Brave-heuristic shape the FU-6 entry forewarned about — install affordance not surfacing until engagement signals trip. **Heroes (Test B) surfaced a NEW finding:** the install attempt returned "this app is already installed" because portal-web's installed scope (`/`, implicit default) transitively includes `/heroes/`. Uninstalling portal first then attempting heroes installation produced a clean install with gold-gradient + deep-gold "H" icon, splash showing the icon image, standalone chrome — heroes structurally installable when no other PWA on the origin holds an overlapping scope. The shared-origin two-PWA coexistence question is real and was not fully resolved by FU-6's manifest hardening — heroes-web's manifest already carries explicit `id`/`scope`/`start_url` of `/heroes/`, but portal-web's manifest declares neither `id` nor `scope`, so its scope defaults to the manifest URL's directory (`/`) which Chrome treats as covering every URL on the origin including `/heroes/`. Lifted to FU-10 below for the structural fix; row 3 closes with "install paths structurally verified in isolation; shared-origin coexistence requires the manifest-scope rewrite tracked as FU-10".
  - **Acceptance for CP11 (met 2026-05-13):** all three rows resolved — row 1 deferred to FU-9 with the contract-gate-orthogonality recording, row 2 closed green with the p50/p95 numbers (cold p50 ~788ms server-wait / ~1370ms DCL; cold p95 ~1290ms server-wait / ~1800ms DCL; warm indistinguishable from cold across 5 samples each — the architectural shape per ADR 0005 + Phase 5, no recorded baseline to validate "flat-or-faster" against beyond the absolute-numbers-within-expected-range reading), row 3 closed with the architectural finding lifted to FU-10. CP11's contract-gate sections (§§ 1–9 + 11–14) are satisfied by the chrome + auth + admin-load + manifest-correctness + install-path verifications done in-session and across the operator window.
  - **Out of scope:** any deeper perf instrumentation (flame graphs, OpenTelemetry traces, Cloud Trace dashboards). The post-Phase-5 expectation is comparison against the baseline; deeper investigation is only warranted if the headline number regresses. Tracking the deeper perf surface would belong in a Spec 03 (Integration Test Kit) or a perf-observability spec; it is not gating CP11.
  - **Related:** T47 (the chrome-parity smoke that closed in-session); T48 (the perf row whose scope folded here); FU-6 (the PWA installability fix that closed in-session); ADR 0005 (the "zero DB roundtrips for session validation" promise this verifies in practice); the manual-apply rationale in standing-principle-5 of `tasks/plan.md` (the same "operator hand work where it belongs" reasoning that kept `tofu apply` on the laptop).

- [~] **FU-9: Sheet-sync trigger silent-fail — IaC drift on env vars + fire-and-forget handler swallows the throw (T47 Finding 6)** — code + IaC source landed; `tofu apply` ran 2026-05-13 at commit `06ae55c`; **operator-click verification deliberately deferred** — heroes-side runtime verification deprioritised so the next session opens Spec 05 (fast integration); the structural fix is live and the 503 surfacing means any operator who eventually clicks Sync Now gets honest feedback either way
  - **Surfaced 2026-05-13** during the FU-8 row 1 attempt against post-`5878c2d` deploy. Operator clicked "Sync Now" on `/heroes/admin/sheet-sync`; UI showed the success toast (with the wrong copy — see §3 below); Sync History showed no new entry at today's date; Last sync timestamp remained `08 Mei 2026 11.33`.
  - **Three interlocking layers:**
    1. **IaC drift (root cause).** `infra/heroes/cloud-run.tf:244-258` only sets `GOOGLE_SHEET_ID_POINTS` + `GOOGLE_SHEET_ID_EMPLOYEES` (+ four `SHEET_TAB_*` companions) inside a `dynamic "env"` block gated on `var.sheet_id_points != ""`. `infra/heroes/variables.tf:42` defaults the variable to `""`. `infra/heroes/terraform.tfvars` does not exist; no operator-passed `-var` ever populated it. So every `tofu apply` since the variables landed has silently dropped the env vars. The May 8 `coms-heroes-api-00015-mxv` predecessor revision that ran the successful sync must have been edited out-of-band (`gcloud run services update --set-env-vars=...` or console). Every subsequent revision — including today's `coms-heroes-api-00015-mxv` from `5878c2d` — inherits the empty state. **Confirmed by `gcloud run services describe coms-heroes-api --format=yaml` — env vars present: `GOOGLE_SHEETS_SA_KEY` (secret), `PORTAL_*`, `NODE_ENV`, `DATABASE_URL` (secret), `SELF_PUBLIC_URL`, `PUBLIC_APP_ORIGIN`, `GCS_BUCKET`, `PUBLIC_PORTAL_ORIGIN`, `PORTAL_ORIGIN`. Notably absent: any `GOOGLE_SHEET_ID_*` or `SHEET_TAB_*`.**
    2. **Silent-fail in the trigger handler.** `apps/heroes-api/src/services/sheet-sync-scheduler.ts:106-110` — `triggerSyncInBackground` is fire-and-forget by design. The route at `apps/heroes-api/src/routes/sheet-sync.ts:104-118` returns 200 + `{ started: true }` immediately. The async `triggerManualSync` runs, hits the `if (!config.sheetIds.points && !config.sheetIds.employees) throw new Error('GOOGLE_SHEET_ID_POINTS/EMPLOYEES env vars not set')` check at `sheet-sync-scheduler.ts:94-95`, throws — but the throw is caught by the `void triggerManualSync(...).catch(() => {})` on line 108. Logged to `console.error('[sheet-sync] sync error:', err)` (line 99), invisible to the UI. No `failed` row gets written to `sheet_sync_jobs` because the validation throws BEFORE `runFullSync(...)` (which is where job rows are created).
    3. **Wrong i18n key in heroes-web (cosmetic — fixed in this session 2026-05-13).** `apps/heroes-web/src/routes/(authed)/admin/sheet-sync/+page.svelte:216` previously rendered `{m.settings_saved()}` ("Settings saved successfully.") for sync-trigger success — wrong key copied from the settings page. Fixed to `{m.sheet_sync_triggered()}` with a new i18n entry across en/id/th locales: "Sync started. New rows appear here when it finishes." (and Indonesian + Thai equivalents). One-line page edit + three message-catalog additions. The cosmetic fix lands here because it's a single-locale-set change with no infra dependency; the structural bugs (1) and (2) wait for the proper Secret Manager + Tofu rewrite.
  - **Proper structural fix — what landed in this session:**
    - **Secret Manager intentionally bypassed.** Operator decision 2026-05-13: sheet IDs identify the canonical spreadsheets but are no leakier than the Drive sharing model (anyone with sheet access has the ID in their browser URL). The original §1 proposed Secret Manager + `secret_key_ref` + a runtime SA accessor grant — three moving parts to maintain for a value class that doesn't earn the secrecy. Replaced with a committed `infra/heroes/terraform.tfvars` carrying the two IDs.
    - **§1 (IaC drift, root cause) — closed in code; awaits operator `tofu apply`.** `infra/heroes/cloud-run.tf` no longer wraps the env vars in a `dynamic "env"` block gated on `var.sheet_id_points != ""`. Two unconditional `env { … }` blocks set `GOOGLE_SHEET_ID_POINTS` + `GOOGLE_SHEET_ID_EMPLOYEES` directly from `var.sheet_id_points` / `var.sheet_id_employees`. The four `SHEET_TAB_*` env vars are removed entirely (their values duplicate the app defaults in `apps/heroes-api/src/services/sheet-sync-scheduler.ts:buildConfigFromEnv` exactly — a single source of truth in the app is cleaner than a two-place duplication). `infra/heroes/variables.tf` drops the empty `default = ""` and gains a Tofu `validation` block requiring non-empty values; the FU-9 lesson is recorded in the validation `error_message` so a future operator hitting the same wall sees the explanation inline. `infra/heroes/terraform.tfvars` lands with the actual sheet IDs + an explanatory header naming the FU-9 decision so the next reader understands why a "tfvars file with what look like committed secrets" exists. `infra/README.md`'s heroes-vars section rewritten to point at the new tfvars file.
    - **§2 (Silent-fail in trigger handler) — closed.** `apps/heroes-api/src/services/sheet-sync-scheduler.ts` gains:
      - A `MISSING_CONFIG_MESSAGE` constant (real human-readable English explaining the IaC fix path, not the original cryptic "env vars not set" string).
      - An exported `getSyncConfigError(): string | null` for synchronous boundary validation.
      - An internal `recordFailedJob(direction, error, startedBy)` that writes a `failed` row to `sheet_sync_jobs` with `errorLog: [{ tab: 'scheduler', row: 0, name: '', error: errorMessage }]` and its own try/catch so a failure to record the failure can't crash the scheduler.
      - The inner validation in `triggerManualSync` + the resync inner block tightened from `&&` to `||` (one ID missing is enough to fail; the prior `&&` meant only "both missing" tripped it) and the error message switched to `MISSING_CONFIG_MESSAGE`.
      - The `.catch` on both `triggerSyncInBackground` and `triggerResyncInBackground` now calls `recordFailedJob('import' | 'resync', err, startedBy)` instead of `() => {}`.
      `apps/heroes-api/src/routes/sheet-sync.ts` gains a `getSyncConfigError()` check before every `triggerSyncInBackground` / `triggerResyncInBackground` call — on all three paths (Cloud Scheduler OIDC, public-route admin session, protected-route admin trigger, protected-route admin resync). When the check returns non-null, the handler sets `status = 503` and returns `{ success: false, data: null, error: { code: 'SYNC_NOT_CONFIGURED', message: configError } }`. The UI at `apps/heroes-web/src/routes/(authed)/admin/sheet-sync/+page.svelte` already extracts `json.error.message` for the destructive-toast pattern (`syncError = json?.error?.message ?? ...`), so the 503 surfaces as a real on-page error message without further UI work. `bun test src/services/__tests__/sheet-sync-pending.test.ts src/services/sheet-sync-helpers.test.ts` stays green (13 pass / 0 fail / 26 expect()), heroes-api `bun typecheck` stays green. `tofu validate` in `infra/heroes/` is green.
    - **§3 (Wrong i18n key) — already closed in prior session at commit `791d073`.**
  - **What remains for the operator window (closes FU-9 [x]):**
    1. `cd infra/heroes && tofu plan -var alert_email=ops@ahacommerce.net` — confirm the plan shows two new env vars added to `coms-heroes-api` and zero env vars removed unexpectedly (the four `SHEET_TAB_*` removals are intentional).
    2. `tofu apply -var alert_email=...` — applies the plan, replaces the Cloud Run revision.
    3. Operator clicks "Sync Now" on `/heroes/admin/sheet-sync`. Expected: status flips to `running`, then `idle`; a new row appears in Sync History with today's date; Last sync timestamp updates.
  - **Belt-and-suspenders, if the operator skips the apply:** the route handler now returns 503 immediately with the `MISSING_CONFIG_MESSAGE` text, so the UI displays "Sheet sync is not configured: GOOGLE_SHEET_ID_POINTS / GOOGLE_SHEET_ID_EMPLOYEES env vars are not set on the Cloud Run revision. Apply the heroes IaC change that wires these env vars, then redeploy." Until the apply lands, the operator sees this on every trigger attempt — no more silent success.
  - **Why this isn't blocking CP11:** the bug is orthogonal to Phase 5's work — the env-var check fails before any heroes_profiles read or `can_submit_points` evaluation happens. The integration-contract gates CP11 was designed to verify (§§ 1–9 + 11–14) are satisfied by the chrome + auth + admin-load verifications already done in-session. T47 Finding 6 is operationally important but does not move the contract gate.
  - **Why the IaC drift went unnoticed until today:** standing-principle 1's "manual-console-state vs IaC-state drift" risk realized in production. The May 8 successful sync was OOB-edited and never reconciled into Tofu source. Every subsequent apply silently dropped the env vars; the next sync attempt was today; the silent-fail handler hid the symptom until an operator looked at the Sync History closely. This is a worth-recording case study for the standing principle. The validation-on-required-vars pattern this fix introduces (no empty defaults that silently drop vars) is the structural lesson — repeat it for every future operator-supplied env var.
  - **Acceptance:** §1 + §2 + §3 all closed. Sheet IDs committed to `terraform.tfvars` (not Secret Manager; operator decision). The silent-fail surfaces failures into both an HTTP 503 at the route boundary and a `failed` row in `sheet_sync_jobs` from the catch. The cosmetic i18n fix from the prior session stands. Operator `tofu apply` flips the in-prod state to match this source state.
  - **Related:** standing-principle 1 in `tasks/plan.md` (the "IaC source of truth, no manual drift" rule); ADR 0010 (OpenTofu over Terraform — the IaC layer that should be authoritative); FU-1 (the prior case where `app_registry.healthCheckUrl` was missing because IaC didn't carry it); FU-5 (which authored `deploy-heroes-api.yml`'s migrate step — the same workflow that'd carry future drift in env vars unless they live in Secret Manager — though FU-9 chose tfvars over Secret Manager for sheet IDs specifically).

- [x] **FU-10: Shared-origin two-PWA coexistence — portal-web's default scope blocks heroes-web (and future fast-web) from installing alongside (T47 Finding 7) — SEALED 2026-05-14 via T87 Step 8 walk**
  - **Surfaced 2026-05-13** during FU-8 row 3's operator verification on Chrome mobile against post-`5878c2d` deploy. Portal-web installed cleanly via "Add to Home Screen". Heroes install attempt then surfaced "this app is already installed". Confirmed by uninstall-portal-then-try-heroes: heroes installs cleanly when no other PWA on the origin holds an overlapping scope; the gold-gradient + "H" icon renders correctly, splash + standalone chrome all green. The conflict is structural to the manifest config, not a manifest validity issue.
  - **Root cause.** Portal-web's `apps/portal-web/static/manifest.json` declares neither `id` nor `scope`. Per the W3C web app manifest spec, both fields default based on the manifest URL: `scope` defaults to the manifest's parent directory (here `/`), and `id` defaults to `start_url` (here also `/`). Chrome's install logic (`WebAppRegistrar::FindAppWithUrlInScope` in Chromium) checks at install time whether any installed app's `scope` contains the new app's `start_url`. Heroes-web's `start_url: "/heroes/"` falls inside portal-web's default `scope: "/"`. Chrome concludes "the COMS Portal app already covers this URL" and short-circuits the install path with "this app is already installed". Heroes-web's manifest is unambiguously correct (explicit `id`, `scope`, `start_url` all `/heroes/`) — the conflict is portal's claim being too broad.
  - **The same conflict will hit fast onboarding (Spec 05).** Fast at `/fast/` is inside portal's `scope: "/"`. Without portal-web's manifest scope narrowing, the third PWA simply can't install while portal is installed. This is a load-bearing prerequisite for the React-side reference implementation Spec 05 is meant to produce — the framework-parity claim (heroes Svelte, fast React, both installable as distinct PWAs) breaks on the shared-origin install collision before any React chrome work begins. **Worth referencing this entry from Spec 05's risk table when it gets reread.**
  - **The structural fix options:**
    1. **Option A (recommended) — Portal-web mounts at `/portal/`** (analogous to heroes at `/heroes/`, fast at `/fast/`). Portal-web sets `kit.paths.base = '/portal'`, gains `scope: "/portal/"`, every internal link and Firebase Hosting rewrite updates. The root `/` becomes a dispatch route (a tiny SvelteKit page or a Firebase Hosting rewrite) that redirects to portal's sign-in landing if unauthenticated, or to the appropriate app if authenticated. Clean spec-compliant solution. Scope-conflict-free for unlimited future apps at `/<app>/`. **Cost:** significant refactor — mirror the shape Spec 02 Phase 1 (T24–T29) executed for heroes, but for portal. Every absolute path in portal-web sweeps through `$app/paths` `base`; Firebase Hosting rewrites change; GIP redirect URIs change; the existing portal-web service worker scope changes; the `register-heroes`/`register-fast` scripts' URL templates change.
    2. **Option B — Accept single-PWA-per-origin and document the limitation.** Only portal-web installs as a PWA on this origin; heroes-web and (future) fast-web are accessed via portal's navigation rather than as separate home-screen tiles. Less work but loses the "distinct app per product" PWA experience that the integration contract's spirit implies. The chrome's app launcher inside the portal PWA becomes the canonical cross-app navigation; users who want heroes-only would just open the URL in the browser, not as a PWA.
    3. **Option C — Heroes-web (and fast-web) install as PWAs; portal-web does not.** Remove portal-web's manifest entirely. Visiting `/` opens in browser; visiting `/heroes/` opens in the installed heroes PWA. Asymmetric to the "portal IS the hub" framing but spec-compliant for the sub-apps.
  - **Recommendation:** Option A. It's the only path that supports the multi-app PWA model the integration contract implies, and it aligns portal-web with the same shape heroes (and eventually fast) follow. The cost is real but the scope migration was successfully executed for heroes in T24–T29; portal-web follows the same playbook.
  - **Why this isn't blocking CP11:** the install paths are structurally verified — both apps install cleanly **in isolation**. The contract-gate sections CP11 was meant to verify all close on what was done in-session. FU-10 is operationally important (and load-bearing for Spec 05's framework-parity claim) but does not move the contract gate. Documenting and deferring is the right call.
  - **What landed in this session (Option A, source-level):**
    - **Foundation.** `apps/portal-web/svelte.config.js` sets `kit.paths.base = '/portal'`. `apps/portal-web/static/manifest.json` declares `id`/`scope`/`start_url` all `/portal/` plus rewrites icon `src` paths under `/portal/`. `apps/portal-web/src/service-worker.ts` drops the `/heroes` skip — the SW scope is now `/portal/` and the browser only invokes the worker for pages within scope, so the T30-era CP4 Finding 2 (Set-Cookie stripped on the wrapped round-trip) closes structurally with the scope split.
    - **Dashboard moves to `/portal/dashboard`.** The shared `packages/ui-svelte/src/chrome/Sidebar.svelte` `isActive` carve-out only matches the root href via `href === '/'`; rebinding it for `${base}` would couple the lib to portal's specific base path. Cleaner: mirror heroes' shape and serve the dashboard from a named subpath. `apps/portal-web/src/routes/(authed)/+page.svelte` is replaced by a tiny `+page.server.ts` that throws a 303 to `${base}/dashboard${url.search}` — the layout's onMount picks up handoff intents on `/portal/dashboard?app=…` and POSTs to the broker launch endpoint unchanged. The dashboard markup moves to `apps/portal-web/src/routes/(authed)/dashboard/+page.svelte` verbatim. `apps/portal-web/src/lib/nav.ts`'s `BASE_NAV[0]` points at `${base}/dashboard`. `apps/portal-web/src/routes/login/+page.server.ts` and `+page.svelte` default `redirect` to `${base}/dashboard`.
    - **Absolute-path sweep (24 callsites across 9 files).** Every `<a href="/admin/…">`, `<Button href="/admin/…">`, `goto('/admin/…')` in `apps/portal-web/src/routes/(authed)/admin/{teams,apps,employees}/**` flows through `$app/paths` `base`. `apps/portal-web/src/lib/nav.ts` ADMIN_NAV entries gain the `${base}` prefix. Fetches to `/api/*` deliberately stay absolute — portal-api lives at `/api/**` on the Firebase Hosting rewrite, base-path-orthogonal (the equivalent of heroes-web reaching `/heroes/api/*` is portal-web reaching `/api/*`; the hub-api at `/api/**` is shared by every app on the origin per the integration contract).
    - **Firebase Hosting routing.** `firebase.json` gains a `/portal` + `/portal/**` rewrite (precedence-ordered after `/heroes/api/**`, `/heroes`, `/heroes/**`, `/api/**`) and a single `redirects` entry `/ → /portal (301)` that preserves query strings — so the legacy `${origin}/?app=heroes&redirect_to=…` URL still works through a one-hop 301 even before consuming apps update their portal sign-in builders. `scripts/verify-firebase-json.mjs` updated to assert the new rewrite count + the redirect shape, then re-run green.
    - **Cross-app glue.** `apps/portal-api/src/routes/userinfo.ts` updates the launcher's synthetic portal entry from `{ url: '/' }` to `{ url: '/portal/dashboard' }` (bypassing the 301 hop on launcher click). `apps/portal-api/src/routes/__tests__/userinfo.test.ts` two `toEqual` assertions updated; 19/0 pass. `apps/heroes-web/src/lib/server/portal-broker.ts:buildPortalSignInUrl` rewrites `${origin}/?…` → `${origin}/portal?…` so heroes' sign-in handoff lands directly on portal-web instead of round-tripping through Firebase's 301. The `redirect_to` value heroes passes is heroes' own URL — that flow is unchanged; only the portal-side landing path moves.
    - **Verification.** `bun run --filter '@coms-portal/*' typecheck` — all 12 workspace packages green. `bun run --filter '@coms-portal/portal-api' test` — every test file green. `bun scripts/verify-firebase-json.mjs` green. The Sidebar / SlideOverNav `isActive` logic now matches portal nav items via the prefixed hrefs (`${base}/admin/employees` etc.) so admin nav highlighting still works.
  - **What remains for the operator window (closes FU-10 [x]):**
    1. `firebase deploy --only hosting` to push the new rewrites + redirect.
    2. GHA `deploy-portal-web.yml` redeploys the new bundle (the SvelteKit build now mounts at `/portal/`; old build at `/` would 404 every authed route until the redeploy lands).
    3. Operator-led mobile verification on Chrome mobile + Brave mobile: visit `https://aha-coms.web.app/` — should 301 to `/portal` then render portal-web dashboard. Install portal as PWA. Install heroes as PWA. Both should install as **separate tiles** with their own scopes — no "this app is already installed" error.
    4. Lighthouse PWA audit on `/portal/` and `/heroes/` — both should pass installability + manifest + service-worker categories.
    5. `register:heroes` does NOT need re-running — heroes' app_registry URL is `https://aha-coms.web.app/heroes`, unchanged.
    6. `tofu apply` not required — portal-web's Cloud Run env (in `infra/cloud-run.tf`'s `portal_shared_env`) carries no path-aware values; the base-path change is contained to portal-web's build output.
  - **Edge case the operator should watch for:** if the GHA portal-web deploy lands before the `firebase deploy --only hosting`, requests to `/admin/...` etc. still get rewritten via the old `**` fallback to portal-web — but portal-web (with new base path) doesn't recognise those paths and 404s. Land both in the same operator window. Suggested order: firebase deploy first (the new rewrites are backwards-compatible — old portal-web at `/admin/...` still works via the `**` fallback during the brief window before the GHA deploy completes), then GHA deploy.
  - **Acceptance:** portal-web mounts at `/portal/` per Option A. Two-PWA coexistence verified: install portal as PWA, then install heroes — both end up as distinct tiles on the home screen with their own icons + scopes. Lighthouse PWA audits pass on both `/portal/` and `/heroes/`. **Cross-reference Spec 05's risk table for the same fix benefiting fast onboarding** — fast at `/fast/` no longer has the scope-overlap blocker.
  - **Related:** Spec 05 (`docs/spec/05-fast-onboarding.md` — the same scope conflict that would have hit fast is now structurally prevented; the third PWA at `/fast/` can install alongside portal at `/portal/` and heroes at `/heroes/`); ADR 0003 (single-origin PWA — the architectural decision FU-10 sharpens, not contradicts); Spec 02 Phase 1 (T24–T29 heroes base-path migration — the playbook this session followed); FU-6 (which closed the manifest-correctness gap but left this architectural conflict for a separate session, now closed at source).
  - **Sealed 2026-05-14 via T87 Step 8:** the on-device three-tiles-one-device proof landed during the CP21 walk. **Fast installs as a distinct PWA** on Android Chrome — tile labeled "Fast" (the manifest's `short_name`), AHA brand mark icon, opens in standalone mode (no browser address bar), scoped to `/fast/`. **Heroes installs as a distinct PWA** alongside it — "AHA Heroes" tile, H icon, scoped to `/heroes/`. **Three distinct tiles** on the home screen with three distinct icons + names. The scope-overlap blocker that motivated FU-10 is gone: heroes installs cleanly while fast is installed, and vice versa — no "this app is already installed" short-circuit. FU-10's specific acceptance ("both end up as distinct tiles on the home screen with their own icons + scopes") is satisfied for the heroes-vs-fast leg, and the Spec 05 cross-reference (fast at `/fast/` installable alongside the others) holds. **One caveat — separately tracked as T87 Finding 14:** portal-web itself only offers "Add shortcut" rather than "Install" on Android Chrome — portal is reachable as a home-screen entry but not as a full PWA. Root cause is different from FU-10's scope-overlap concern (portal's `/portal/` scope is already narrow; the gap is portal-web missing one or more PWA installability requirements — manifest fields, service worker registration, or icon sizes). FU-10's load-bearing concern (does portal's scope block the sub-apps from installing?) is resolved cleanly; portal-as-PWA-itself is portal-web cleanup tracked under F14, not a reopen of FU-10. **Brave repeat skipped** per operator triage — same browser engine class as Chrome; coverage sufficient. **Lighthouse PWA audit** ran against `/fast/track` (the public surface; `/fast/` auth-redirects to portal/login for unauthenticated audits which would audit portal's PWA properties instead of fast's): 100% PWA, every audit green (installable-manifest, splash-screen, themed-omnibox, viewport, maskable-icon). Canonical artifact at `apps/fast/docs/t86-lighthouse.report.html`.

- [x] **FU-4: Document the laptop-CLI `tofu apply` process in `infra/README.md`**
  - **Done 2026-05-12:** `infra/README.md` written end-to-end. Sections: prerequisites (gcloud, tofu 1.11.6, cloud-sql-proxy, IAM scope, state-bucket URIs), variables (the three operator-passed vars + tfvars + heroes' `alert_email`), normal apply (the read-the-plan-twice discipline), targeted apply (with today's FU-2 binding as the canonical example), stale-lock recovery (Who/Created safety check before `force-unlock`, with today's `1778571978311920` as the worked example), heroes substate (separate bucket, same workflow), what NOT to do (no auto-approve untargeted, no force-unlock without ownership check, no manual state edits, no apply without PR plan review), reopening FU-4 (upgrade conditions + cross-link to "Future upgrade path" below). `tasks/plan.md` standing-principle-5 updated to mention the README as the supported apply path. The `infra-plan.yml` comment now points at the real file (third rewrite of that comment in two days; the third one matches reality and stops there).
  - **What was missing:** No README in `infra/` describes how an operator applies infrastructure changes. The process exists in lore — Cloud SQL proxy for migration runs alongside apply, var-files, state-lock recovery when a plan dies mid-run, the `-target=` pattern for surgical changes — but it lives in one or two operators' heads. A new operator joining the project has to discover the shape through trial and oral tradition.
  - **Position taken (downgraded from the original FU-4 workflow_dispatch shape):** keep apply manual on the laptop, document the process, defer GHA-backed apply until the team grows past three operators or an incident proves the audit gap. Reasoning:
    - For a two-operator project with infrequent infra changes, the value of GHA-backed apply is modest (mainly audit trail). The cost is real (workflow YAML, WIF binding adjustments, the operational discipline of always firing the workflow instead of `tofu apply`-ing locally).
    - Manual apply windows have worked through Phases 1-5 and the CP3 cutover without incident; FU-1/FU-2's apply on 2026-05-12 was the same shape and went clean once the stale lock from a rejected plan was force-unlocked.
    - Going looser later (workflow_dispatch → auto-apply on merge) is easier than tightening after an incident. Starting at the conservative end leaves room to relax; starting loose forces a forensic rewrite if something goes wrong.
    - State-lock hygiene, auth segregation, and audit trail are real but rare wins for this team size. The README captures the recovery procedure once, in writing, where the next operator can find it.
  - **Shape to implement:**
    1. New `infra/README.md` covering:
       - **Prerequisites:** `gcloud auth login`, project + state bucket access, `tofu` version (pin to whatever `infra-plan.yml` uses — currently `1.11.6`).
       - **Var files:** where `terraform.tfvars` lives, what each variable does, when to override via `-var` (e.g. the `service_url`/`bootstrap_admin_*` placeholders today's session passed manually because `terraform.tfvars` doesn't carry them).
       - **Normal apply:** `tofu init` → `tofu plan` (read the diff!) → `tofu apply` (no `-auto-approve` by default; the interactive prompt is the safety net).
       - **Targeted apply:** the `-target=<resource_address>` pattern for surgical changes (today's `tofu apply -target=google_secret_manager_secret_iam_member.cloud_build_gip_api_key` is the canonical example).
       - **Stale-lock recovery:** how to read `tofu force-unlock <lock-id>`, the safety check (confirm Who/When matches your session before unlocking — never unlock another operator's running apply).
       - **Heroes substate:** the same workflow against `infra/heroes/` with its own state bucket. Call out the per-app principle that keeps states separate.
       - **What NOT to do:** never bypass the plan ("just apply it"), never `force-unlock` without verifying ownership, never use `-auto-approve` on a non-targeted apply against the shared state.
    2. Rewrite the comment at the top of `.github/workflows/infra-plan.yml` to point at `infra/README.md` as the supported apply runbook (instead of pointing at "FU-4 workflow_dispatch shape", which is now deferred).
    3. Mention this README from `tasks/plan.md`'s standing-principles-5 paragraph (or a sibling principle) so future readers of the plan know the apply path is deliberately manual.
  - **Acceptance:** A new operator (real or hypothetical) reads `infra/README.md` and successfully performs `tofu plan` against the shared state without asking another operator. Plus the README survives at least one apply by an operator who didn't write it (i.e., the runbook is verified by use, not just review).
  - **Future upgrade path:** reopen this entry as the workflow_dispatch shape if any of (a) team grows past three operators, (b) audit-driven post-mortem requires retroactive "who applied what when", (c) operator-mistake rate exceeds one mishap per quarter, (d) the project's GCP footprint grows enough that the blast-radius math changes. The implementation cost of workflow_dispatch is small (one workflow file, WIF binding adjustments); this entry's body captured the position so the upgrade is clean when the time comes. Originally proposed shape:
    - `.github/workflows/infra-apply.yml` with `on: workflow_dispatch:` only (no push trigger). Inputs: optional `target` for surgical changes; optional `auto_approve` boolean defaulting to false. Runs `tofu init` + `tofu plan` + `tofu apply` under WIF auth. `concurrency:` block (`group: infra-apply`, `cancel-in-progress: false`).
    - WIF deployer SA needs broader IAM than its current deploy-only scope. Scope the binding to `infra-apply.yml` specifically via GitHub OIDC `aud:`/`sub:` claims to avoid latent capability creep on every push to main.
    - Optionally: a status check on push to main that runs `tofu plan` and writes the queued diff to the run summary. Makes "what's waiting to be applied" visible without applying anything.
  - **Related:** the corrected comment in `.github/workflows/infra-plan.yml`; today's session (manual `tofu apply -target=` from laptop); `agent-skills:ci-cd-and-automation` skill's "Rollback Plan" principle.

### Phase 6: Archive external repos

Spec ref: `docs/spec/01-monorepo-consolidation.md#phase-6`.

- [x] **T21: Archive the 5 external lib repos on GitHub**
  - **Prerequisites:** Checkpoint 4
  - **Repos:** coms-sdk, coms-shared, coms-ui, coms-design-tokens, coms-account-widget
  - **Steps:** `gh repo archive mrdoorba/<repo-name>` per repo.
  - **Acceptance:** Each repo shows "archived" banner on GitHub.
  - **Done 2026-05-12:** Ran `gh repo archive mrdoorba/<repo> --yes` for all five non-interactively. Verified post-archive via `gh api repos/mrdoorba/<repo> --jq .archived` — all five report `true`. The subtree-merged sources remain in-tree under `packages/{sdk,shared,ui-svelte,design-tokens,account-widget-svelte}/`; the archived remotes are now read-only history, exactly the shape Phase 6 prescribed.

- [x] **T22: Archive `coms-aha-heroes` repo on GitHub**
  - **Prerequisites:** Checkpoint 4
  - **Steps:** `gh repo archive mrdoorba/coms-aha-heroes`.
  - **Naming correction:** The GitHub repo is `coms-aha-heroes` (hyphenated), not `coms_aha_heroes` (underscored) as written everywhere prior. The underscore lives only on the local checkout directory; the remote always used hyphens. The first archive attempt against `mrdoorba/coms_aha_heroes` returned 404, surfaced the mismatch, and the hyphenated form succeeded immediately. Plan + todo updated to use the GitHub-truthful spelling going forward; on-disk dir keeps its underscore to avoid breaking the historical paths in subtree merge commits.
  - **Done 2026-05-12:** `gh repo archive mrdoorba/coms-aha-heroes --yes` ran clean; `gh api repos/mrdoorba/coms-aha-heroes --jq .archived` returns `true`. The three non-main remote branches (`ci/parallelize-and-harden`, `ci/skip-redundant-build-and-docker-parallel`, `rev3/spec-01-02-adoption`) follow the repo into the archive — all read-only, exactly as agreed pre-T11.

- [x] **T23: Update `repository.url` in in-tree package.jsons**
  - **Prerequisites:** T21, T22
  - **Steps:** Each in-tree package's `repository.url` should point at the aha-coms repo with optional `directory` field.
  - **Acceptance:** Grep returns no references to the archived lib/heroes repo URLs.
  - **Done 2026-05-12:** Rewrote five `repository.url` fields — `packages/{ui-svelte,shared,design-tokens,sdk,account-widget-svelte}/package.json` — each now points at `https://github.com/mrdoorba/aha-coms.git` with the appropriate `"directory": "packages/<name>"` qualifier, matching the shape that `packages/ui-react` and `packages/account-widget-react` already carried (those two needed no edit — they were authored in-tree from the React stubs and already wore the mono shape). Verified `grep -rn 'mrdoorba/coms-\\(sdk\\|shared\\|ui\\|design-tokens\\|account-widget\\)\\.git' --include=package.json .` returns clean.
  - **Finding (logged below as Phase 6 Finding 1, not blocking CP5):** the wider tree still carries stale references to the now-archived repo URLs in doc files — `DESIGN_SYSTEM.md` at the root describes the polyrepo workflow (clone-PR-tag-bump); per-package `README.md` / `CONTRIBUTING.md` quote install pins like `bun add git+https://github.com/mrdoorba/coms-ui.git#v1.0.0` and route contributors to PRs against repos that no longer accept PRs; `packages/sdk/MIGRATION.md` + `packages/sdk/examples/web-bundle-smoketest/` reference closed issue `mrdoorba/coms-sdk#1`. These docs pre-date the consolidation; the archived URLs still resolve (archived repos remain readable, just frozen) but the workflow they prescribe is no longer applicable. Out of T23's narrow `repository.url` scope; queued as a Phase 6 follow-up doc-sweep that the rev-3 consolidation effort can absorb when it next touches DESIGN_SYSTEM.md.

- [x] **CHECKPOINT 5**: Spec 01 complete. Consolidation done.
  - **Crossed 2026-05-12:** Six external repos archived (`coms-sdk`, `coms-shared`, `coms-ui`, `coms-design-tokens`, `coms-account-widget`, `coms-aha-heroes`), five `repository.url` fields rewritten to the mono shape. The polyrepo of seven Git remotes is now a single Bun workspace at `aha-coms/` with all source in-tree; the archived remotes are read-only history. Phase 6 Finding 1 (doc rot in `DESIGN_SYSTEM.md` + per-package READMEs/CONTRIBUTINGs) is real but non-blocking — the install pins it quotes still resolve, just against frozen repos. Spec 01 complete; Spec 02 (heroes integration cleanup) unblocked.

#### Phase 6 Findings — track for follow-up doc-sweep

1. **Doc rot referencing the now-archived polyrepo workflow.** `DESIGN_SYSTEM.md` at the repo root, `packages/{ui-svelte,design-tokens,account-widget-svelte}/CONTRIBUTING.md`, `packages/{ui-svelte,design-tokens,sdk,account-widget-svelte}/README.md`, `packages/sdk/MIGRATION.md`, and the smoketest README/test file in `packages/sdk/examples/web-bundle-smoketest/` all describe the old polyrepo path — clone the per-lib repo, branch, PR back, tag bump, consumer pin update. With those repos archived, the URLs still resolve but the prescribed workflow doesn't. None of this is load-bearing for the build (the install pins quoted in docs are illustrative, not consumed), so it is queued for a follow-up sweep rather than expanded into T23. The natural moment to fold it in is when the rev-3 consolidation effort next touches `DESIGN_SYSTEM.md` or when a new contributor's first PR exposes the rot in practice — at that point the sweep rewrites the workflow as "edit in-tree under `packages/<name>/`, open a PR against `aha-coms`."
