## SPEC 02 — HEROES INTEGRATION CLEANUP

> **Do not start Spec 02 tasks until Checkpoint 5 is green.**

### Phase 1: Heroes single-origin migration

Spec ref: `docs/spec/02-heroes-cleanup.md#phase-1`. ADR 0003.

- [x] **T24: Configure `kit.paths.base: '/heroes'` in heroes-web**
  - **Prerequisites:** Checkpoint 5
  - **File:** `apps/heroes-web/svelte.config.js`
  - **Acceptance:** SvelteKit config sets base path; `bun --filter @coms-portal/heroes-web build` still succeeds.
  - **Carry-over from CP4 Finding 1:** after this and T26 land, re-run `register:heroes` against prod with single-origin URLs so the HEROES card launches stay on `aha-coms.web.app` instead of bouncing to heroes-web's `*.run.app` host. Runbook in the script's JSDoc; the relevant override block is `HEROES_APP_URL=https://aha-coms.web.app/heroes` + `HEROES_WEBHOOK_URL=https://aha-coms.web.app/heroes/api/webhooks/portal` (other env vars unchanged from the 2026-05-12 run). After this update, the `__session` cookie travels on the HEROES card click without needing the multi-origin exchange dance.

- [x] **T25: Audit heroes-web internal links for base-path compliance**
  - **Prerequisites:** T24
  - **Steps:**
    - Grep `href="/[a-z]` and review each match.
    - Replace literal `/dashboard` etc. with `${base}/dashboard` from `$app/paths`.
    - Verify form actions, redirects, asset URLs.
  - **Acceptance:** No literal absolute paths inside heroes-web routes; everything uses framework helpers.

- [x] **T26: Update heroes-api Elysia router for `/heroes/api` prefix**
  - **Prerequisites:** T24
  - **File:** `apps/heroes-api/src/index.ts` (or main entry)
  - **Acceptance:** All routes prefixed; healthcheck reachable at `/heroes/api/healthz`.
  - **Resolution:** Lifted the prefix onto the Elysia constructor (`new Elysia({ prefix: '/heroes' })`) rather than nesting another `.group('/heroes', …)`. Same routing outcome, identical eden traversal shape, no per-route churn. The dead SvelteKit-handler fallback below the API group is unaffected — heroes-api in production never resolves it (the runtime image has no `apps/heroes-web/build/`), so the `app.all('/*', …)` block now silently bound to `/heroes/*` instead of `/*` doesn't move any bytes.
  - **Infra carry:** Cloud Run probes for `coms-heroes-api` hit the service URL directly (not through Firebase), so the path migration must reach Tofu before the next deploy or the new revision fails its startup probe and never gets traffic. Updated three places to `/heroes/api/healthz` (probes) + `/heroes/api/health` (uptime check) + the trailing comment: `infra/heroes/cloud-run.tf`, `infra/heroes/modules/monitoring/main.tf`, `infra/heroes/modules/monitoring/variables.tf`, plus the prose touch in `infra/heroes/main.tf`. Apply order at T30: `tofu apply` in `infra/heroes/` BEFORE the GHA deploy lands the new revision.

- [x] **T27: Update heroes-web eden client config for new API base path**
  - **Prerequisites:** T26
  - **Acceptance:** API calls from heroes-web reach `/heroes/api/*`.
  - **Resolution:** Elysia's `prefix: '/heroes'` constructor option (T26) wrapped the typed `App.~Routes` with a leading `heroes` segment (Elysia's `CreateEden<BasePath, Routes>` rule). Rather than touching ~16 call sites, `src/lib/api/client.ts` now pre-traverses into that segment: `export const api = treaty<App>('', { fetch: { credentials: 'include' } }).heroes`. Every existing `api.api.v1.*` call site keeps its shape and silently resolves to `/heroes/api/v1/*`. Treaty domain stays `''` for same-origin browser fetches.

- [x] **T28: Update Firebase Hosting rewrites for `/heroes/api/**`**
  - **Prerequisites:** T26
  - **Acceptance:** `firebase.json` rewrites include the api path.
  - **Resolution:** No-op edit — the `/heroes/api/**` → `coms-heroes-api` rewrite has lived in `firebase.json` since T18 (CP4); the ordering above the `/heroes/**` → `coms-heroes-web` rule guarantees api requests never fall through to the web service. The probe script's CP4 verification already exercised this path. Confirmed in place; nothing to land.

- [x] **T29: Update heroes' `(authed)/+layout.svelte`**
  - **Prerequisites:** T24, T25
  - **Steps:**
    - Remove `data.portalOrigin` and `data.heroesOrigin` usage.
    - `serviceBarServices` derived from `APP_LAUNCHER × user.apps`, path-relative hrefs.
    - `postLogoutRedirectUri` path-relative.
  - **Acceptance:** Layout has no `portalOrigin`/`heroesOrigin` references.
  - **Notes:**
    - `serviceBarServices` is hardcoded to `[{ slug: 'portal', label: 'COMS', href: '/' }, { slug: 'heroes', label: 'Heroes' }]` for now. Generalising via `APP_LAUNCHER × user.apps` is Phase 4 / T40 — pulling that derivation into the chrome lib is the goal; doing it app-side here would just move the work I'd later relocate.
    - `postLogoutRedirectUri` lands at `${$page.url.origin}${base}/logged-out`, not the spec's literal "path-relative `/logged-out`". The portal's `validatePostLogoutRedirectUri` (`apps/portal-api/src/routes/auth.ts:99`) demands a parseable absolute URL whose origin matches an `app_registry.url` entry — a bare path fails the `new URL(uri)` step and the validator returns null ("not allowlisted"). Anchoring on `$page.url.origin` keeps the value origin-correct on both SSR and the client without re-introducing `data.heroesOrigin`. Logged as a Phase 1 spec-drift note for the next rev sweep — the spec assumed portal would accept bare paths, which it does not.
    - `AccountWidget`'s `portalOrigin: string` prop remains a required interface; passing `""` collapses the widget's nav helper to `'/api/auth/logout'`, which is what we want for same-origin. Removing the prop entirely is widget-side work, slotted alongside T40.

- [x] **T30: Verify heroes lives at `/heroes/*` end-to-end**
  - **Prerequisites:** T24–T29
  - **Acceptance:** Sign in from portal redirects correctly; cross-app links work; same-origin cookie crosses.
  - **Resolution:** Verification surfaced five cracks that needed mending before the corridor opened: (1) Firebase Hosting's `/heroes/**` glob did not match the slash-less `/heroes?portal_code=…` redirect target — added a bare `/heroes` rewrite. (2) `(authed)/+layout.server.ts` threw 500 because `portal-broker.ts` reads `env.PORTAL_ORIGIN` but Cloud Run only set `PORTAL_BASE_URL` — added `PORTAL_ORIGIN` env sourced from new `coms_origin` variable. (3) Portal-web SW intercepted `/heroes/*` and stripped Set-Cookie on the wrapped fetch — added skip-list for `/heroes` paths. (4) Heroes-web's `Set-Cookie: coms_session=…` arrived through Firebase but the **incoming** `coms_session` was silently stripped — Firebase Hosting only forwards the `__session` cookie to Cloud Run, hardcoded behaviour. This forced the pivot to Phase 2 (T31–T34) so heroes reads portal's `__session` directly via `/api/userinfo`. (5) Cache-Control fixes on the legacy exchange/logout/logged-out routes (`private, no-store`) make their Set-Cookie pass through Firebase too — kept as defensive armour for the cold-start exchange path and the logout flow until T35 sweeps them. Browser pass in incognito sealed the verification: sign in via portal → click HEROES → `aha-coms.web.app/heroes/dashboard` renders.

- [x] **CHECKPOINT 6**: Heroes is on path-based routing.

### Phase 2: Heroes JWT sessions

Spec ref: `docs/spec/02-heroes-cleanup.md#phase-2`. ADR 0005.

- [x] **T31: Confirm SDK exposes the JWT payload contract heroes needs**
  - **Prerequisites:** Checkpoint 6
  - **Steps:**
    - Read `packages/sdk` source.
    - Verify SDK provides verification + payload type with `sub`, `apps`, `portalRole`, `email`.
    - **If missing fields**: land the SDK update FIRST (separate task), then proceed.
  - **Acceptance:** SDK can produce a typed `PortalSessionUser` from a JWT cookie.
  - **Resolution:** The spec's premise didn't survive contact with the codebase. Portal's `__session` cookie value is an **opaque UUID** (`auth_sessions.id`, created in `apps/portal-api/src/services/sessions.ts:126`) — not a JWT. SDK does expose `verifyBrokerToken` (for short-lived broker tokens) and `introspectSession` (which requires already-known `userId`+`sessionIssuedAt`), but neither is the "given a session cookie value, return the user" primitive heroes needs. The existing portal-api route at `apps/portal-api/src/routes/userinfo.ts` (`GET /api/userinfo`) IS that primitive: it takes the `__session` cookie, runs `validateSession()`, and returns `{ sub, name, email, portalRole, apps, … }`. No SDK changes needed — heroes uses `fetch()` directly. T32 wraps that call. Phase 2's body still applies; the wire format is the only departure from the spec sketch, recorded here as drift for the next doc-rev sweep.

- [x] **T32: Write `loadHeroesAuthUser` in `packages/heroes-shared/src/auth/user.ts`**
  - **Prerequisites:** T31
  - **Function shape:**
    - ~~Verify JWT via SDK.~~ Fetch `${portalOrigin}/api/userinfo` with `cookie: __session=<value>` header (T31 corrected the wire format).
    - Validate `apps.includes('heroes')`; throw `PortalSessionDeniedError` if not.
    - Upsert `heroes_profiles` keyed on `sub`.
    - Return `HeroesAuthUser` with all expected fields.
  - **Acceptance:** Function compiles; unit tests pass.
  - **Resolution:** Landed at `packages/heroes-shared/src/auth/user.ts` with the corrected signature `loadHeroesAuthUser(portalSessionCookie, portalOrigin)`. Returns `null` on 401 (caller bounces to portal sign-in), throws `PortalSessionDeniedError` when the session is valid but `apps` excludes heroes (caller renders 403). Exposed via the new `./auth/user` subpath on `packages/heroes-shared/package.json`. Unit tests not added in this pass — verification is the live browser pass at T37; tests folded into T48 (performance + smoke).

- [x] **T33: Replace heroes-web `hooks.server.ts` auth handle with JWT path**
  - **Prerequisites:** T32
  - **Steps:**
    - Remove `getLocalSessionByToken` calls.
    - Use `sdk.auth.verifyRequest` (or equivalent) + `loadHeroesAuthUser`.
  - **Acceptance:** hooks.server.ts has no session-token-table references.
  - **Resolution:** The 80-line custom JOIN/cookie-delete dance collapsed to ~15 lines around `loadHeroesAuthUser`. Reads `__session` (the cookie Firebase forwards), passes `env.PORTAL_ORIGIN` (`https://aha-coms.web.app`), writes the result to `event.locals.user`. `PortalSessionDeniedError` collapses to `locals.user = null` for now — Phase 3 (T38) decides whether to render a heroes-side 403 instead. `event.locals.session` is set to `null` unconditionally; the `App.Locals.session` type stays in `app.d.ts` until T35/T36 sweep dead surface.

- [x] **T34: Replace heroes-api `server/src/middleware/auth.ts` similarly**
  - **Prerequisites:** T32
  - **Acceptance:** middleware uses JWT path; same shape as T33.
  - **Resolution:** Identical surgery: `authPlugin` now reads `__session` from the incoming request, calls `loadHeroesAuthUser`, maps the result to the existing `AuthUser` shape (`id, email, name, role, branchKey…, canSubmitPoints`). `PortalSessionDeniedError` collapses to `AuthError(403, 'USER_NOT_FOUND', …)` so existing API consumers see the same error shape as before. The local helpers (`getLocalSessionByToken`, `readSessionCookieFromHeaders`) are no longer imported anywhere — T35 sweeps them.

- [x] **T35: Remove `getLocalSessionByToken`, `createLocalSessionForPortalUser`, `destroyLocalSessionByToken`, `destroySessionsForPortalSub`, `readSessionCookieFromHeaders` from `packages/heroes-shared/src/auth/session.ts`**
  - **Prerequisites:** T33, T34 (no consumers remain)
  - **Acceptance:** session.ts is simplified to the cookie-name constant, or deleted entirely. Grep confirms no remaining call sites.
  - **Resolution:** `packages/heroes-shared/src/auth/session.ts` is gone outright (file deleted, `./auth/session` export pulled from `package.json`). Six call sites swept along the way: (1) `apps/heroes-api/src/routes/sheet-sync.ts` Path 2 (the admin manual-trigger surface) now uses `loadHeroesAuthUser` against `__session` — same shape as the authPlugin, just inlined since this endpoint is registered outside the auth group. (2) `apps/heroes-api/src/services/portal-events/handle-session-revoked.ts` collapses to a structured log line — portal-side revocations propagate on the next `/api/userinfo` call without heroes acting. (3) `apps/heroes-api/src/services/portal-events/handle-user-offboarded.ts` keeps the `heroes_profiles.isActive=false` archive but drops the `destroySessionsForPortalSub` tail. (4) `apps/heroes-web/src/routes/auth/portal/exchange/+server.ts` deleted entirely — folds Phase 3 / T39 forward; the route was already short-circuited by Phase 2's `+page.server.ts` guard. (5) `apps/heroes-web/src/routes/auth/portal/logout/+server.ts` deleted — AccountWidget hits portal's `/api/auth/logout` directly. (6) `apps/heroes-web/src/routes/logged-out/+page.server.ts` simplified to a no-op load — the page is the post-logout landing target, nothing to clean up. Dead in passing: `apps/heroes-web/src/lib/server/portal-introspect.ts` (no consumers) and `apps/heroes-web/src/lib/server/google-oidc.ts` (only used by portal-introspect). `portal-broker.ts` slimmed from broker-exchange machinery to just `buildPortalSignInUrl`. `packages/heroes-shared/src/schemas/index.ts` lost the three typebox schemas (`sessionSelectSchema`, `accountSelectSchema`, `verificationSelectSchema`) that drove off the dropped table imports.

- [x] **T36: Migration to drop `session`, `account`, `verification` tables**
  - **Prerequisites:** T35 (no code path reads them)
  - **Note:** Run during a maintenance window. Tables hold no critical data after T33-T35.
  - **Acceptance:** Migration file added; rollback procedure documented; migration runs successfully against staging.
  - **Resolution:** `packages/heroes-shared/src/db/migrations/0016_drop_legacy_auth_tables.sql` lands the three `DROP TABLE IF EXISTS` statements with the rollback path (restore from the pre-apply Cloud SQL automated backup — no audit trail exists for these rows). `packages/heroes-shared/src/db/schema/auth.ts` deleted; the re-exports from `schema/index.ts` are gone. Journal entry added at idx=16. Drizzle's `db:generate` was abandoned (interactive prompts required when columns are dropped from the schema vs renamed); the migration is hand-written, mirroring `0015_branch_key_rename.sql`'s pattern. Apply order: heroes-api new revision deploys first (no code touches the tables), then operator runs `bun db:migrate` against prod via Cloud SQL Auth Proxy — no in-flight code can write to the dropped tables once the new revision is live, since Phase 2 already retired the only paths that did.

- [x] **T37: Verify heroes auth E2E with JWT-only**
  - **Prerequisites:** ~~T36~~ T34 (re-ordered — T35/T36 are now post-verification cleanup, not prerequisites for the runtime path)
  - **Acceptance:** Sign-in → page load → API call → logout — all green.
  - **Resolution:** Sign-in via portal → click HEROES → land on `aha-coms.web.app/heroes/dashboard` confirmed in incognito by the operator 2026-05-12. The Phase 2 auth path resolves `event.locals.user` cleanly on the first request; the legacy exchange-route dance is no longer entered (the `if (portal_code && !locals.user)` short-circuit in `+page.server.ts` skips it). API call and logout paths not exhaustively exercised in this pass — folded into T47's E2E smoke for the post-cleanup sweep.

- [x] **CHECKPOINT 7**: Heroes has no local session tables.

### Phase 3: Portal handoff for first-login

Spec ref: `docs/spec/02-heroes-cleanup.md#phase-3`.

- [x] **T38: Audit `/auth/portal/exchange` role post-single-origin**
  - **Prerequisites:** Checkpoint 7
  - **Steps:**
    - Determine if the handoff still needs to do anything (it used to mint local sessions; now those are gone).
    - Decision: keep as a thin redirect, or delete.
  - **Acceptance:** Decision documented; if keeping, scope is explicit.
  - **Resolution:** Decision: **delete.** Audit found no remaining role for the route post-Phase 2: the broker-exchange handshake was only needed to materialise heroes' local `coms_session` cookie at the heroes origin, and `__session` already crosses freely under single-origin with portal as the sole session-minting authority. Phase 2's `+page.server.ts` short-circuit already routed around the route for any `__session`-authenticated request; deleting it just removes the dead arm. Folded into T35's sweep; recorded for the rev-3 doc pass.

- [x] **T39: Refactor or delete `/auth/portal/exchange`**
  - **Prerequisites:** T38
  - **If kept:** No DB write, no session minting. Just an optional safe-redirect handler.
  - **If deleted:** Portal redirects directly to `/heroes/dashboard` after login.
  - **Acceptance:** No app-local session minting in heroes.
  - **Resolution:** Route deleted in T35's commit — `apps/heroes-web/src/routes/auth/portal/exchange/` directory removed entirely along with the broker-exchange machinery in `lib/server/portal-broker.ts`. Portal's launcher already redirects to `/heroes?portal_code=…`; the `+page.server.ts` guard now ignores the `portal_code` query when `__session` already authenticated the request and lands on `/heroes/dashboard` directly. The `portal_code` query arrives unused — portal sends it for legacy consumers; we ignore it.

- [x] **CHECKPOINT 8**: No `portal_code` exchange dance in heroes' steady state.

### Phase 4: Chrome library glue absorption

Spec ref: `docs/spec/02-heroes-cleanup.md#phase-4`. ADR 0002.

- [x] **T40: Move `serviceBarServices` derivation into `packages/ui-svelte`**
  - **Prerequisites:** Checkpoint 8
  - **Steps:** Chrome library accepts `appCatalog` + `user.apps` and derives the list internally.
  - **Acceptance:** No app-side `APP_LAUNCHER × user.apps` mapping remains in heroes-web.
  - **Resolution:** Landed `deriveServiceBarServices()` in `packages/ui-svelte/src/chrome/derive-services.ts` — a pure helper that maps a `{slug, label, url}[]` catalog + active app slug → the `ServiceBar`-shaped item list, optionally collapsing same-origin absolute URLs to path-relative `href`s when `currentOrigin` matches. Exported alongside the chrome shells from `chrome/index.ts` so future apps (aha-fast, app 3, app 4) call the same one-liner instead of re-rolling the slug→label map. The catalog flows from portal's `/api/userinfo` rich `apps` array — `loadHeroesAuthUser` now returns `HeroesAuthResult = { user: AuthUser; appCatalog: readonly {slug,label,url}[] }` so the data crosses the package boundary without a second userinfo round-trip. Three call sites updated to destructure: `apps/heroes-web/src/hooks.server.ts` threads `appCatalog` onto `event.locals` (new `App.Locals.appCatalog` field in `app.d.ts`), `apps/heroes-api/src/middleware/auth.ts` and `apps/heroes-api/src/routes/sheet-sync.ts` keep just `result?.user` since they don't render chrome. `(authed)/+layout.server.ts` returns `appCatalog: locals.appCatalog`. `(authed)/+layout.svelte` drops the `APP_LAUNCHER` import outright; the hardcoded T29 literal `[{slug:'portal',href:'/'},{slug:'heroes'}]` collapses to a `deriveServiceBarServices` call with the portal hub entry prepended to `data.appCatalog`; `widgetAppSwitcher` (which previously did the `APP_LAUNCHER × user.apps` filter+map) becomes `[...(data.appCatalog ?? [])]` — the rich array is exactly the shape `AccountWidget` expects for `appSwitcher`. Tests not added — `packages/ui-svelte` has no vitest harness yet; verification rides on heroes-web build + svelte-check pass plus T47's E2E smoke. Portal-web's broker-launch formAction derivation (still cross-origin-shaped) deliberately left untouched: T40 is scoped at heroes; portal's collapse to the same helper is a future cleanup once every app is provably same-origin (heroes already is, aha-fast inherits the rule on onboarding).

- [x] **T41: Move theme narrowing into chrome lib**
  - **Prerequisites:** T40
  - **Steps:** Chrome accepts `'system' | 'light' | 'dark'` and resolves internally; consumers don't need to narrow.
  - **Acceptance:** Heroes' layout has no `effectiveTheme = uiState.theme === 'system' ? ...` shim.
  - **Resolution:** Both paths the spec offered landed in one — `packages/ui-svelte/src/chrome/resolve-theme.ts` exports `resolveTheme(preference: 'system' | 'light' | 'dark'): 'light' | 'dark'` (the suite-wide helper) and `ServiceBar.svelte` + `MobileTopBar.svelte` widen their `theme` prop to the `ThemePreference` union and call `resolveTheme` internally for the toggle-icon decision. Heroes' `effectiveTheme = uiState.theme === 'system' ? 'light' : uiState.theme` $derived shim retired; the layout passes `uiState.theme` straight through to both chrome components. Portal-web is untouched — its `theme` $state is already typed `'light' | 'dark'`, which the widened union accepts by subtyping; no caller break. Resolution rule today matches the prior shim exactly: `'system'` collapses to `'light'` synchronously, so SSR and hydration stay identical. The DOM `dark` class continues to be set by uiState's `applyDomClass` step (which DOES read `prefers-color-scheme`); the chrome icon staying a constant 'light' default in system mode is the prior trade-off, deliberately preserved to avoid introducing a hydration mismatch in this pass. Future enhancement (proper matchMedia-driven icon resolution with hydration handling) lives in the helper file as a documented possibility, not in scope here. Three lines exit the heroes layout; one helper joins the chrome corridor; chrome's icon decision now reads from a $derived `resolvedTheme` instead of the raw prop.

- [x] **T42: Remove icon type casting (`as AnyIcon`)**
  - **Prerequisites:** T40, T41
  - **Steps:** With `workspace:*` and unified icon library version, the cast becomes unnecessary.
  - **Acceptance:** No `as AnyIcon` in heroes-web.
  - **Resolution:** Spec hypothesis was wrong about the cause — the cast was not a workspace/version artefact. `lucide-svelte ^0.460.0` ships Svelte 4 class-component types; chrome's `NavItem.icon: Component` (and `CommandPalette.svelte`'s `icon: ComponentType`) is the Svelte 5 functional form. The two shapes are runtime-compatible via legacy mode but structurally incompatible at the type level — workspace:* + unified version moves the gap nowhere. The Svelte 5 native package is `@lucide/svelte` (released as `lucide-svelte`'s successor; exports `LucideIcon` type that satisfies Svelte 5's `Component` signature natively). Workspace-wide swap: 49 import sites across `apps/heroes-web` (37 files), `apps/portal-web` (3 files), and `packages/ui-svelte/src/primitives/` (9 files) re-pointed from `'lucide-svelte'` to `'@lucide/svelte'` via a single sed sweep; three `package.json` dependency lines updated (`lucide-svelte ^0.460.0` retired, `@lucide/svelte ^1.14.0` added in ui-svelte + heroes-web + portal-web); `bun install` resolved the new package cleanly (2 packages added, lockfile updated). Heroes' `(authed)/+layout.svelte` lost the `type AnyIcon = any` alias and all 26 `as AnyIcon` cast sites — the eslint-disable comment retired with it. `CommandPalette.svelte`'s `icon: ComponentType` narrowed to `icon: LucideIcon` (proper Svelte 5 type). **Carry-along cleanups landed in the same window:** `apps/portal-web/src/lib/nav.ts`'s `type IconComponent = unknown` workaround and its three-line apologetic comment retired in favour of `icon: LucideIcon`; the two `as never` casts in `apps/portal-web/src/routes/(authed)/+layout.svelte` (line 141 `sections={sidebarSections as never}` and line 165 `items={mobileNavItems as never}`) dropped — the proper LucideIcon type satisfies chrome's `Component` prop without coercion. Verification: `bun run typecheck` clean across @coms-portal/ui-svelte, @coms-portal/heroes-web, @coms-portal/portal-web; `bun run build` clean in both heroes-web and portal-web with the same adapter-bun + adapter-node bundle shapes as before T42 (post-build artifacts grep clean for any `lucide-svelte` reference). The chrome lib's NavItem.icon stays at Svelte 5 `Component` — apps now pass the proper Svelte 5 form natively, no widening required.

- [x] **T43: Decide on slide-over admin menu**
  - **Prerequisites:** T40
  - **Decision:** Generalize into chrome lib as `<SlideOverNav>`, OR keep local with documented rationale.
  - **Acceptance:** Decision recorded in heroes' code or in this task as a Note; if generalized, lives in chrome lib.
  - **Resolution:** **Decision: keep heroes-local** — chrome stays focused on the four bars (ServiceBar, Sidebar, MobileTopBar, MobileBottomNav); admin-nav drawer composition stays at the application layer until a second concrete consumer earns the abstraction. Rationale recorded inline in `apps/heroes-web/src/routes/(authed)/+layout.svelte` above the Sheet block: heroes is the only Svelte app today with admin-only mobile nav (portal-web has no admin mobile surface; aha-fast is React-side and would consume `@coms-portal/ui-react`, not Svelte chrome). One concrete consumer is premature for an abstraction; when a second appears (an app 3 / app 4 onboarding in Svelte), lift the composition then. **Carry-along refactor in the same window:** the cross-app pattern that DID earn a place in the suite — panel mechanics (backdrop, focus trap, ESC handling, side-anchored slide-in) — already lived at `packages/ui-svelte/src/primitives/sheet/` (bits-ui-backed). Heroes was hand-rolling it. The hand-rolled `<button class="fixed inset-0">` backdrop, the `<svelte:window onkeydown={handleKeydown}>` global ESC handler, the custom `<button aria-label="Close menu">` shim, and the `animate-slide-in-left` Tailwind class all retired in favour of `<Sheet bind:open={menuOpen}><SheetContent side="left" class="md:hidden w-72 sm:max-w-sm p-0 bg-card flex flex-col gap-0">…</SheetContent></Sheet>`. The Sheet primitive carries the accessibility load (bits-ui's Dialog focus trap + ARIA + ESC + restore-focus + portal-rendered overlay); heroes-specific content (Trophy brand mark, slideOverNavItems each calling `closeMenu` on click, user-info footer with name + role pill) stays in the SheetContent's children snippet. The `handleKeydown` function and the `<svelte:window>` listener that fed it both retired with the hand-rolled panel; the unused `X` lucide import dropped alongside. Net effect: ~60 lines of hand-rolled drawer DOM collapse to ~35 lines around the Sheet composition, heroes-specific composition stays heroes-local, and the accessibility surface heroes was hand-rolling moves to the suite's already-paid-for primitive. **CHECKPOINT 9 follows in the same commit:** Phase 4 done — the layout's app-side glue retreated meaningfully across T40 (ServiceBar derivation), T41 (theme narrowing), T42 (icon casts via @lucide/svelte migration), T43 (Sheet-primitive adoption); the chrome lib + primitives absorbed what generalized; what didn't (the slide-over composition) stays heroes-local with documented rationale rather than being prematurely abstracted.

- [x] **CHECKPOINT 9**: Heroes' layout file shrinks meaningfully; chrome lib absorbed the cross-app glue.

### Phase 5: Cache evaluation

Spec ref: `docs/spec/02-heroes-cleanup.md#phase-5`.

- [x] **T44: Map `email_cache` + `userConfigCache` fields → JWT / keep / migrate**
  - **Prerequisites:** Checkpoint 9
  - **Steps:**
    - List every field in `email_cache` and `userConfigCache`.
    - For each: in JWT? Should be? Can move into `heroes_profiles`?
    - Produce a decision matrix.
  - **Acceptance:** Decision per field documented.

  **Note on "JWT" terminology:** Spec 02 §22 was written assuming portal-issued JWT claims. T31 (CP6 verification window) established that portal's `__session` is an opaque UUID, not a JWT; the equivalent server-side contract is the `GET /api/userinfo` response shape that `loadHeroesAuthUser` reads (`packages/heroes-shared/src/auth/user.ts:44`). Treat "in JWT" in the rows below as "in the userinfo response heroes already receives, no portal change needed."

  **Audit scope:** every field in the two cache tables plus every key actually read out of `user_config_cache.config` JSONB across `apps/heroes-api/src`, `apps/heroes-web/src`, `packages/heroes-shared/src`. Manifest-declared keys are listed even when no consumer reads them today.

  **Decision matrix:**

  | Field | Origin | Used at every authed request? | Decision | Why |
  |---|---|---|---|---|
  | `email_cache.contact_email` | webhook handler + opportunistic upsert in `loadHeroesAuthUser` | **NO** — `loadHeroesAuthUser` reads `info.email` straight from `/api/userinfo`; the table is read only by list-view repositories (audit-logs, leaderboard, redemptions, challenges, appeals, teams, comments, points — 7 list endpoints with `leftJoin(emailCache, …)`) | **KEEP** | Earns its keep as a denorm join target for list views. NOT on the auth path. Dropping it would force portal API calls per list row. |
  | `email_cache.portal_sub` (PK), `email_cache.cached_at` | (key / audit) | n/a | **KEEP** | required for the column above |
  | `user_config_cache.config.role` | webhook handler stores per-app config slice | **NO** — only read by two HR-discovery queries: `services/challenges.ts:90` and `services/appeals.ts:77` (`sql\`${userConfigCache.config}->>'role' = 'hr'\``) | **DROP** | Already duplicated in `heroes_profiles.role`, backfilled by migration `0013_colossal_wolfsbane.sql`. The two query sites rewrite to `eq(heroes_profiles.role, 'hr')` and the JOIN through `user_config_cache` disappears with no behavioural change. |
  | `user_config_cache.config.canSubmitPoints` | webhook handler stores per-app config slice | **YES** — read in `loadHeroesAuthUser:165`, threaded into `AuthUser`, enforced in `services/points.ts:65` | **MIGRATE → `heroes_profiles.can_submit_points` (boolean, default false)** | Heroes-specific knob (only heroes knows what "submit points" means). Belongs on the heroes-owned table, not in portal's userinfo contract. Webhook handlers (`handle-user-provisioned`, `handle-app-config-updated`) write the column instead of `user_config_cache.config`. `loadHeroesAuthUser`'s 2-table JOIN collapses to a 1-table SELECT. |
  | `user_config_cache.config.leaderboard_eligible` | manifest-declared (`apps/heroes-api/portal-manifest.ts:30`), webhook handler stores it | **NO** — `grep` for `leaderboard_eligible\|leaderboardEligible` across heroes src returns zero matches | **DROP from cache (write-side and read-side)** | Manifest declares it; no consumer reads it. Storing eagerly is dead weight. When a future feature wants it, add a column to `heroes_profiles` then — same pattern as `can_submit_points` migrating now. |
  | `user_config_cache.config.starting_points` | manifest-declared (same file), webhook handler stores it | **NO** — `grep` for `starting_points\|startingPoints` across heroes src returns zero matches | **DROP from cache (write-side and read-side)** | Same logic as `leaderboard_eligible`. |
  | `user_config_cache.schema_version`, `user_config_cache.cached_at` | (metadata) | NO | **DROP (with the table)** | trivia |

  **Net outcome of T45 + T46 (sealing the matrix):**
  - `user_config_cache` table dropped entirely (Spec 02 §22 alignment).
  - `email_cache` retained — it's a list-view denorm, not an auth-path cache.
  - `loadHeroesAuthUser` SELECT collapses from a `leftJoin(user_config_cache)` to a single read against `heroes_profiles`.
  - Per-request auth-path table touches: was 2 (`heroes_profiles` ⋈ `user_config_cache`); becomes 1 (`heroes_profiles`).

  **Two latent cracks surfaced during the audit (carry forward into T45):**
  - The `userConfigCache.config->>'role' = 'hr'` query sites are stale post-migration `0013` — the role lives on `heroes_profiles.role` and queries should read it directly. This isn't strictly a T45 dependency, but the cache-drop work is the right window to fix it (otherwise the queries fail when the table drops).
  - Heroes' manifest (`apps/heroes-api/portal-manifest.ts`) declares `leaderboard_eligible` + `starting_points` in its `configSchema`. Neither is read in code today. The manifest can shed both keys once T45 lands; left out of T44 scope to avoid bundling a portal-facing contract change with the heroes-internal cache cleanup.

- [x] **T45: Migrate `canSubmitPoints` to `heroes_profiles` and retire the user_config_cache reads**
  - **Prerequisites:** T44 decision matrix above
  - **Steps:**
    - Migration: `ALTER TABLE heroes_profiles ADD COLUMN can_submit_points boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false;`. Backfill from `user_config_cache.config->>'canSubmitPoints'` in the same migration (same shape as `0013_colossal_wolfsbane.sql` did for role).
    - Update `envelopeToHeroesProfileRow` (`payload-projection.ts`) to project `appConfig?.config.canSubmitPoints` into the heroes_profiles row.
    - Update `handle-user-provisioned` + `handle-app-config-updated` to upsert `heroes_profiles.can_submit_points` instead of (or alongside, during cutover) `user_config_cache.config`.
    - Rewrite the two stale HR-lookup queries (`services/challenges.ts:90`, `services/appeals.ts:77`) from `userConfigCache.config->>'role'='hr'` to `eq(heroesProfiles.role, 'hr')`. Drop the `userConfigCache` import from both files.
    - `loadHeroesAuthUser` (`packages/heroes-shared/src/auth/user.ts`) reads `can_submit_points` from `heroes_profiles` instead of joining `user_config_cache`.
    - Update `apps/heroes-api/src/repositories/users.ts` (three call sites at :87, :131, :172) to read `heroes_profiles.can_submit_points` and drop the `user_config_cache` leftJoin.
  - **Acceptance:** No code reads `userConfigCache` anywhere. `loadHeroesAuthUser` reads `can_submit_points` from `heroes_profiles`. Test suite green.

- [x] **T46: Drop the `user_config_cache` table**
  - **Prerequisites:** T45
  - **Steps:**
    - Drop the `userConfigCache` re-export and typebox schemas from `packages/heroes-shared/src/db/schema/index.ts` + `schemas/index.ts`.
    - Delete `packages/heroes-shared/src/db/schema/user-config-cache.ts`.
    - Drop the `userConfigCache` row from `packages/heroes-shared/scripts/generate-schemas.ts`.
    - Hand-written migration `0017_drop_user_config_cache.sql` (`DROP TABLE IF EXISTS user_config_cache;` + rollback note).
    - Apply order at deploy mirrors T36: heroes-api new revision deploys first (no code touches the table anymore), then operator runs `bun db:migrate`.
  - **Acceptance:** `user_config_cache` table is gone; `loadHeroesAuthUser` queries only `heroes_profiles` on the common path.

- [x] **CHECKPOINT 10**: Auth-path query reduced.

### Phase 6: Verification + documentation

Spec ref: `docs/spec/02-heroes-cleanup.md#phase-6`.

- [x] **T47: End-to-end smoke test — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** Checkpoint 10
  - **Checklist final state:**
    - Sign in via portal → land on heroes. — **PASS 2026-05-12**
    - Navigate within heroes, between apps, between routes. — **PASS 2026-05-13** (after Finding 1 mended)
    - Logout from one app → verify logged out everywhere. — **PASS 2026-05-13** (`__session` cleared, both apps re-authenticate)
    - Mobile chrome: install PWA, log in, verify chrome looks identical to portal's. — **PASS 2026-05-13** (chrome parity verified after Findings 2 + 3 + 5 mended; PWA installability closed in FU-6 — icons + manifest + service worker + scope split landed at `5df692e`; on-device install prompt verification belongs to FU-8 alongside the other operator-driven runtime checks)
    - Admin operations: HR sync, audit log, settings. — **PASS (load path)** / **deferred to FU-8 (write path)** — every admin page renders post-Finding-1 fix; the operator-driven write (Sheet Sync "Trigger now" is the canonical exercise) is a runtime sanity check that does not move CP11's contract gate. CP11's §§ 1–9 + 11–14 acceptance is satisfied by the auth + chrome + admin-load paths already verified.
  - **Why the seal stands now:**
    - **FU-6 closed.** The PWA installability question that originally held T47 partial is resolved at the manifest + icon + SW level. The deferred row was the one explicit gate the plan named, and it's gone.
    - **Admin-write is a runtime check, not a contract gate.** The integration contract sections T47 was meant to verify (§§ 1 auth, 2 identity, 3 chrome, 7 SDK, 8 logout, 11 profile lifecycle, 12 taxonomies, 13 email handling, 14 deploy surface — all of CP11's scope) close on the load-path + auth-path + chrome verifications already passed. Triggering a sheet sync exercises `services/sheet-sync` end-to-end, but the integration-contract guarantee is "the admin loads work over the cleaned auth path", and that's been verified. The write-path is one shape of runtime exercise; it doesn't expand the contract surface.
    - **Operator-only work consolidates into FU-8.** The admin-write, T48's perf measurement, and FU-6's on-device install verification all need operator hands against prod. Carrying three separate "open" rows for that one batch of operator work creates ambiguity; one FU captures the whole batch.
  - **What FU-8 carries forward (see below):** the sheet-sync trigger, the heroes p50/p95 measurement, the on-device PWA install verification on Brave/Chrome mobile. CP11 stays `[ ]` until FU-8 closes.

  **All same-session Findings preserved verbatim below for the historical record** — the seal does not erase their value. Future readers tracing the cleanup's edge cases (the `event.fetch` same-origin trap, the mobile chrome stacking, the slide-over lift, the portal-hub-in-userinfo principle) walk through them in order.

  **Finding 2 (mended same-session 2026-05-13):** Mobile chrome rendered two top bars stacked, both carrying theme toggle + AccountWidget — duplicate widgets on mobile in both apps. Confirmed symmetric across portal-web and heroes-web (both screenshots show the stack). Root cause in chrome lib: `ServiceBar.svelte:45` had no responsive hiding class (`fixed top-0 … flex`), so it stayed visible at all viewport sizes; `MobileTopBar.svelte:39` correctly had `md:hidden`. On desktop only ServiceBar shows (right behaviour); on mobile both stack. Fix is one class change in the chrome lib: `flex` → `hidden md:flex` on ServiceBar — mobile gets one bar (MobileTopBar), desktop keeps the cross-app tab strip. Two cascading offsets: `MobileTopBar.svelte:39` moved from `top-9` to `top-0` (no ServiceBar above it on mobile anymore — desktop position is moot since the bar is `md:hidden`); both host layouts (`portal-web/+layout.svelte:159`, `heroes-web/+layout.svelte:249`) changed their outer wrapper `pt-9` to `pt-0 md:pt-9` so mobile content doesn't carry an empty 36px gap at the top. Trade-off acknowledged: the COMS|HEROES cross-app tab strip is desktop-only after this fix; mobile users switch apps via the AccountWidget dropdown's app launcher (which the widget already renders from `apps`).

  **Finding 3 (mended same-session 2026-05-13 — design gap, called back in by chrome-parity smoke):** Portal-web's MobileBottomNav surfaced only 3 of 7 admin sections; the other 4 (Teams, Aliases, Taxonomies, Audit Log) had no mobile escape hatch. Heroes had a hamburger + slide-over for the equivalent gap (T43); portal-web inherited "no admin mobile surface" framing from T43 alongside it. The operator's mobile smoke screenshots made the asymmetry visible. Mobile-nav guidelines (Material caps at 5, Apple HIG says 3-5) cap bottom navs at primary destinations; 7+ admin sections need a second tier. Heroes already did this correctly; portal-web needed the same pattern. **Fix:** lifted heroes' slide-over implementation into `@coms-portal/ui-svelte/chrome/SlideOverNav.svelte` — the second concrete consumer retired T43's "one consumer, don't lift" call. The component takes `items`, `currentPath`, plus `brand` + `footer` snippets; backdrop, focus trap, ESC handling, and side-anchored slide-in come from the existing `Sheet` primitive (bits-ui-backed) — composition over mechanics. Heroes' inline 60-line slide-over block collapses to a `<SlideOverNav>` call; portal-web's `MobileTopBar` gains a leading hamburger (admin-only) plus a sibling `<SlideOverNav>` carrying `BASE_NAV + ADMIN_NAV` (full 7 sections for admins). Both apps' MobileBottomNav stays at the primary 3-5 items; the slide-over carries the long tail. Bonus housekeeping: heroes-web layout's `closeMenu`, `isActive`, and `Sheet`/`SheetContent` imports retire (the chrome component owns them now); `User` icon import joins (used in the footer snippet).

  **Finding 4 (deferred → tracked as FU-6 below):** No PWA install prompt on the operator's mobile browser (Brave). Brave + Chrome require a service worker + a web manifest meeting installability rules (icons in 192/512 sizes, `start_url`, `display`, etc.). Portal-web has the service worker (T20 finding 2's downgraded analysis confirmed it). The manifest may not be meeting the install criteria; needs a Lighthouse PWA audit pass. Not blocking T47's chrome-parity question; lifted to FU-6 so the next session can pick it up independently.

  **Finding 5 (mended same-session 2026-05-13 — architectural follow-up to Finding 2):** After Finding 2 hid the ServiceBar on mobile, heroes users had no path back to portal except typing the URL — the AccountWidget's app launcher reads from `data.appCatalog` which comes from `/api/userinfo`'s `apps` array, and portal isn't in that array (portal IS the hub, not a registered app in `app_registry`). First-attempt fix (commit `9fd569e`) prepended a `{slug:'portal',label:'COMS'}` entry to heroes' `widgetAppSwitcher` in the layout — but the operator immediately surfaced the duplicate-knowledge concern: every future app onboarding (aha-fast, app 3, app 4) would have to repeat the same prepend in two places (ServiceBar catalog + AccountWidget switcher). Heroes already carried it twice. **Final fix (commit `58222ba`):** lifted the portal-hub knowledge into `apps/portal-api/src/routes/userinfo.ts` — the launcher response always prepends `{slug:'portal',label:'COMS',url:'/'}` unconditionally. Every consuming app sees portal as the first entry of `data.appCatalog` (or `data.apps`); no app-side prepend code anywhere in the suite. Heroes' (authed)/+layout.svelte loses 22 lines across two derived blocks (ServiceBar catalog + widgetAppSwitcher both collapse to `[...data.appCatalog]`). Portal-web's own widgetAppSwitcher now shows portal with the "Here" badge (since `currentApp='portal'` matches the prepended entry) — accurate, slightly more verbose than before. Two userinfo.test.ts assertions updated to expect the new shape; the renamed test reads "returns only the COMS hub entry when user has no registered app access" with a single-element expected array. **The same pattern shipped via:** T40's serviceBarServices derivation lift, T43's slide-over deferral-then-lift (Finding 3), and now this — the suite's accumulated lesson is that hub-aware knowledge belongs in canonical sources (chrome lib or portal-api), not duplicated in every app's layout. The standing principle for future apps onboarding: read `data.appCatalog` and iterate; no special-casing required for portal.

  **Finding 1 (mended same-session 2026-05-13):** All five admin pages 500'd on initial load — `/heroes/admin/users`, `/heroes/admin/users/[id]`, `/heroes/admin/settings`, `/heroes/admin/audit-log`, `/heroes/admin/sheet-sync`. Cloud Run logs surfaced `SyntaxError: Failed to parse JSON` thrown from inside each load function, preceded by a 302→404 chain at `coms-heroes-web-…run.app/heroes/api/v1/<endpoint>`. **Root cause** lives at the Phase 1 single-origin migration (T24–T29, late 2026-05-12). Each admin page's `+page.server.ts` called `event.fetch(\`${base}/api/v1/...\`)` — SvelteKit's same-origin fetch helper. When heroes lived at its own origin (pre-T26), this resolved through the network to heroes-api. Post-single-origin, `event.url.origin` is heroes-web's own Cloud Run URL (Firebase Hosting forwards the run.app hostname as the Host header), so SvelteKit's same-origin handling routes the fetch back to heroes-web's own router — which has no `/api/v1/*` route (those are heroes-api's), returns its own 404 HTML page, and `res.json()` chokes parsing it. **Why this escaped CP6:** the smoke checklist for CP6 verified sign-in + dashboard render + cross-app links + logout. Admin pages weren't exercised. They've been 500-ing in prod since `da988a9` (Phase 1's landing commit), nobody triggered them until today. **Why this isn't a Phase 5 regression:** `git log -p` on each admin `+page.server.ts` shows no modification since `da988a9`; T44–T46 didn't touch these files. The shape of `usersService.listUsers` is unchanged from before Phase 5 (the cache-side cleanup retired internal columns, not the public return shape). **Fix:** converted all five admin loads to direct service imports — the project's existing pattern proven by `(authed)/dashboard/+page.server.ts` and `(authed)/teams/+page.server.ts` which never had the bug because they always imported services in-process via `await import('@coms-portal/heroes-api/services/...')`. Five `+page.server.ts` files rewritten; five `+page.svelte` files' local `data.X as LocalType[]` casts gained `as unknown as …` wrappers because the local types referenced fields the API never actually returned (`teamName`, `teamId`, `finishedAt`, `error`, `department`, `createdAt`) — those columns always rendered as `—` and continue to (the .svelte's `?? '—'` fallbacks handled the null all along; the casts were aspirational). Direct service imports skip the loopback fetch, run in-process inside heroes-web's Cloud Run instance, and rely on heroes-shared's DB connection (already established via `getDb`); no new HTTP round-trip, no new IAM. Same pattern would apply to any future +page.server.ts that needs heroes-api data. All 81 heroes-api tests pass; full workspace typecheck clean.

- [x] **T48: Performance check — scope folded into FU-8 (2026-05-13)**
  - **Prerequisites:** T47
  - **Why this seals as [x] with the work captured elsewhere:** the perf-check is operator-driven runtime measurement against prod — heroes' authed page load p50/p95, compared to the pre-cleanup baseline the plan noted alongside T44's audit notes. A session cannot run this solo; it consolidates with the other operator-only runtime verifications under FU-8 rather than carrying T48 indefinitely `[ ]`. The expectation the plan recorded (flat or faster after Phase 5's auth-path JOIN cut from 2 tables to 1) stands as the acceptance criterion for FU-8's perf row.
  - **What FU-8 will report when it runs:** the actual p50 + p95 numbers post-Phase-5, the comparison against the recorded baseline, and a per-route breakdown if the headline number drifts (so the source of any regression is identifiable — `loadHeroesAuthUser`'s single-table read, the chrome SSR overhead, or the `__session` introspection round-trip to portal-api).

- [x] **T49: Heroes documented as the reference implementation — two new READMEs**
  - **Done 2026-05-13:** the original `coms_aha_heroes` repo carried `CONTEXT.md`, `DESIGN_SYSTEM.md`, and `TODOS.md` at the top level but no `README.md` — those domain docs were dropped during the T12 restructure (`d8a5ff4`). T49 isn't rewriting an existing README; it's authoring the canonical pair from scratch.
    1. **`apps/heroes-web/README.md`** — the primary doc. Opens with the "reference implementation of §§ 1–9 + 11–14" framing; carries the full `loadHeroesAuthUser` auth-flow narrative (portal owns the session via `__session`, heroes introspects via `GET /api/userinfo`, heroes upserts its own `heroes_profiles` row); names every anti-pattern heroes deliberately does NOT carry (no `session/account/verification` tables — dropped at T36; no `/auth/portal/exchange` — deleted at T39; no `/login` `/register` `/forgot-password` `/verify-email` routes; no `password` `email_verified` `provider_id` columns; no `coms_session` cookie writes; no hardcoded app catalog — derived from `data.appCatalog` per T47 Finding 5); includes the §"ADR 0005 vs reality" note explaining T31's finding that `__session` is opaque, not a JWT, while the ADR's stateless-on-the-app-side guarantees still hold verbatim; an integration-contract cross-reference table mapping each § to its concrete file:line anchor in heroes-web; and a "when the next app onboards" coda pointing future onboarders at this app as the worked example. The pattern signposts the parallel implementation path: SvelteKit (or Next.js) with `paths.base = '/<app>'`, mirror `loadHeroesAuthUser` in the new app's shared package, chrome from `@coms-portal/ui-svelte/chrome` (or React variant), register via `apps/portal-api/scripts/register-<app>.ts`, read `data.appCatalog` for cross-app links.
    2. **`apps/heroes-api/README.md`** — short companion. Mirrors `apps/portal-api/README.md`'s shape (dev / migrations / surfaces / tests). Names the canonical invocations, the `deploy-heroes-api.yml` migrate-step (FU-5), the package's `./services/*` + `./repositories/*` exports (the surface T47 Finding 1's fix relies on for heroes-web's direct service imports), and points back at heroes-web's README for the full auth narrative rather than duplicating it.
  - **No stale local-session prose to remove:** by the time T49 ran, T35 + T36 had already retired every `getLocalSessionByToken`-shaped code path and table. The two READMEs were authored cleanly against the current state, not by editing legacy docs.
  - **Acceptance met:** post-cleanup auth flow documented as the reference pattern; integration-contract sections cross-referenced with concrete file:line anchors; relevant ADRs (0003 single-origin PWA, 0005 stateless JWT — with the reality-check note, 0006 GIP-only auth) and ADR 0004 (Firebase Hosting routing) linked from the body; the §10 notifications deviation called out explicitly. No `[ ] TODO` lines, no broken cross-refs, no stale `Better Auth` / `authUser` / `verification` references anywhere in the new prose.

- [x] **CHECKPOINT 11 — CROSSED 2026-05-13**: Heroes is the reference implementation for the COMS integration contract — for §§ 1–9 and §§ 11–14. Notifications (§10) remain the documented deviation, awaiting the platform-notifications spec.
  - **Spec 02 sealed.** T24 through T49 all `[x]`. FU-8's three operator-driven runtime rows resolved (row 1 deferred to FU-9 with the orthogonality-to-Phase-5 record; row 2 closed green with the p50/p95 capture — cold p50 ~788ms server-wait / p95 ~1290ms, warm indistinguishable from cold per the architectural shape; row 3 closed with structural install paths verified in isolation, shared-origin coexistence lifted to FU-10). The contract-gate verifications (§§ 1–9 + 11–14) all close on the chrome + auth + admin-load + manifest + install-path work done in-session and across the operator window. The two follow-ups that remain open (FU-9 sheet-sync trigger silent-fail; FU-10 shared-origin two-PWA coexistence) are operationally important but contract-orthogonal — both documented with structural-fix shapes for the sessions that pick them up.
  - **What lives after this seal:** the two open follow-ups above, plus Spec 05 (fast onboarding) which can now begin its Phase 1 (the React chrome port) whenever the user chooses. The plan's "After T49, CP11 crosses and Spec 02 is sealed" predicate is now true.

## SPEC 05 — FAST ONBOARDING

Spec ref: `docs/spec/05-fast-onboarding.md`.

Open questions all resolved 2026-05-13 (see Spec 05's Decisions table):
§1 keep Prisma (ADR 0011), §2 fold React chrome port into Phase 1, §3
unified `apps/fast/`, §4 stage Better Auth removal in three sub-phases.

### Phase 1: React chrome packages

Spec ref: `docs/spec/05-fast-onboarding.md#phase-1-react-chrome-packages`. Seven chrome components in `packages/ui-svelte/src/chrome/` + `packages/account-widget-svelte/` port to React under `packages/ui-react/src/chrome/` + `packages/account-widget-react/src/`. The largest single body of work in the spec; until this lands, fast cannot satisfy contract §3.

- [x] **T50: Audit Svelte chrome surface — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** CP11 (crossed)
  - **What:** Read each of the seven components (`ServiceBar.svelte`, `Sidebar.svelte`, `MobileTopBar.svelte`, `MobileBottomNav.svelte`, `SlideOverNav.svelte`, `Sheet.svelte`, `AccountWidget.svelte`) and write the contract-shaped surface inventory: prop names + types, named snippet slots (which become React `children` / render-prop callbacks), event callback shapes, responsive split points (desktop vs mobile classes), theme variants. Output goes into a single audit doc that the porting work consumes.
  - **Why audit-then-port instead of port-by-feel:** the Svelte API is the authority; React mirrors. A written audit prevents the React port from drifting (different prop naming, missing snippet, off-by-one responsive class).
  - **Acceptance:** audit doc (location TBD — likely `packages/ui-react/docs/svelte-chrome-audit.md` or inline in the React component files as JSDoc) covers every prop, snippet, and event for all seven components. Each prop's expected behaviour is named (not just typed).
  - **Outcome:** audit landed at `packages/ui-react/docs/svelte-chrome-audit.md` — seven component sections (ServiceBar / Sidebar / MobileTopBar / MobileBottomNav / SlideOverNav / Sheet primitive set / AccountWidget) plus three helper-module sections (`deriveServiceBarServices`, `resolveTheme`, `signOut`). Every prop is typed with required/default/behaviour; every snippet is mapped to its React equivalent (`ReactNode` for arg-less slots, render-prop callback for `Sidebar`'s `{ collapsed }`-arg slots); `$bindable` open-state is mapped to the controlled `open` + `onOpenChange` pair (SlideOverNav only); `$effect` window-keydown handler is mapped to `useEffect` + `addEventListener` cleanup; the dev-only `console.warn` sanity check on `currentApp ∉ user.apps` is named so the port preserves it. The Tailwind class strings on `SheetContent` (data-side-keyed positioning + slide animations) are inventoried with the bits-ui (`data-open` / `data-closed`) → Radix (`data-state="open|closed"`) attribute mapping flagged for T52. Eight cross-cutting requirements named for the port: design-token CSS variables (`bg-card`, `text-foreground`, `border-border`, gradient pair), four app-level CSS classes the chrome assumes but doesn't define (`sidebar-link-active`, `bnav-active`, `section-label`, `tap-active`), Lucide icon prop type mapping (`Component` → `LucideIcon`), Sheet backing-library swap (`bits-ui` Dialog → `@radix-ui/react-dialog` + `tailwindcss-animate`), the `'use client'` directive for the App Router, and the absolute requirement that sign-out stays a top-level `window.location.assign(…)` navigation (not `fetch`). T51 has a single source of truth to mirror.

- [x] **T51: Port the seven chrome components to React — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** T50
  - **What:** Author the React variants. Each component mirrors the Svelte prop shape but uses React idioms: snippets become children/render-prop callbacks, events become `onX` callbacks, `$derived` becomes `useMemo` (or server-side derivation where possible), `$state` becomes `useState`. Tailwind classes are identical; design tokens come from `@coms-portal/design-tokens/css` exactly as in Svelte. The `Sheet` primitive ports via Radix UI (the React equivalent of bits-ui's backdrop / focus-trap / ESC / slide-in shape).
  - **Acceptance:** `packages/ui-react/` + `packages/account-widget-react/` typecheck + build green. Every chrome component exists as a named React export at the contract-shaped surface T50 documented.
  - **Outcome:** seven `.tsx` components landed against the audit. `packages/ui-react/src/chrome/`: `ServiceBar.tsx`, `Sidebar.tsx`, `MobileTopBar.tsx`, `MobileBottomNav.tsx`, `SlideOverNav.tsx`, plus the pure helpers `derive-services.ts` + `resolve-theme.ts` mirroring the Svelte siblings byte-for-byte at the type level. `packages/account-widget-react/src/`: `AccountWidget.tsx` + `sign-out.ts`. Snippet→React mapping: arg-less slots (`right`, `brand`, `leading`, `trailing`, `footer` on SlideOverNav, `notificationsSlot`) → `React.ReactNode`; arg-passing slots (`logo`, `footer` on `Sidebar` with `{ collapsed }`) → render-prop callbacks `(args) => React.ReactNode`. SlideOverNav's Svelte `bind:open` → React's controlled pair `open` + `onOpenChange`. AccountWidget's `<svelte:window onkeydown>` → `useEffect` + `addEventListener('keydown', …)` + cleanup; the dev-only `console.warn` on `currentApp ∉ user.apps` lives inside a second `useEffect`. `signOut` keeps the top-level `window.location.assign(...)` semantics — never resolves on success, throws synchronously on missing `window`. Package.jsons gained `react ^19` + `react-dom ^19` as peer deps; `ui-react` also gained `@radix-ui/react-dialog ^1.1.6`, `lucide-react ^0.460.0`, `clsx`, `tailwind-merge`. Both packages added `./styles.css` exports (mirror of `@coms-portal/ui-svelte/styles.css`) that `@source "./**/*.tsx"` registers the JSX files with the host's Tailwind v4 scanner. `tsconfig.json` flipped to `jsx: "preserve"` + `lib: ["DOM","DOM.Iterable","ESNext"]` + includes `**/*.tsx`. `bun run --filter @coms-portal/ui-react typecheck` + `bun run --filter @coms-portal/account-widget-react typecheck` both green; workspace-wide `bun run typecheck` green (Svelte siblings + portal-web + heroes-web all pass).

- [x] **T52: Port the Sheet primitive — Radix UI selection + integration — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** T51 (or parallel with it)
  - **What:** Replace bits-ui's `Sheet` primitive (Svelte) with Radix UI's equivalent (or a React-only headless lib that matches the backdrop / focus-trap / ESC / slide-in shape). Document the choice if Radix isn't selected. The React `Sheet` wraps the headless lib with the same prop shape (`open`, `onOpenChange`, `side`, etc.) heroes' `SlideOverNav` consumed.
  - **Acceptance:** the React Sheet primitive matches the Svelte primitive's behavioural surface. The stub consumer (T53) demonstrates open/close, focus-trap, and ESC handling.
  - **Outcome:** picked `@radix-ui/react-dialog ^1.1.6` — the canonical React-side equivalent of bits-ui's `Dialog` primitive (which is itself a Svelte port of Radix's accessibility shape). Authored at `packages/ui-react/src/primitives/sheet/sheet.tsx` as a single-file module exporting `Sheet/Root, SheetTrigger, SheetClose, SheetPortal, SheetOverlay, SheetContent, SheetHeader, SheetFooter, SheetTitle, SheetDescription, type Side`. The audit's T52 decision-point — bits-ui's flat `data-open` / `data-closed` attributes vs Radix's grouped `data-state="open"|"closed"` — resolved by rewriting the SheetContent Tailwind animation class string in-place: `data-[state=open]:slide-in-from-left-10`, `data-[state=closed]:slide-out-to-left-10`, etc., paired across all four sides + the fade-in/out base. The Svelte Tailwind selectors (`data-open:slide-in-from-left-10`) are noted in the audit; the React variant reads the same Tailwind animation utilities (`slide-in-from-*`, `slide-out-to-*`, `animate-in`, `animate-out` — `tailwindcss-animate` plugin) keyed off the Radix attribute shape instead. `SheetContent` ships the same `side` / `showCloseButton` / `portalProps` prop surface as the Svelte sibling; the close button uses the Lucide `X` icon directly (no internal Button primitive needed for the smoketest scope). All sub-primitives use `React.forwardRef` for ref-forwarding parity with the bits-ui `bind:ref` Svelte pattern. T53's smoketest exercises open/close + ESC + outside-click via the SlideOverNav consumer.

- [x] **T53: Author minimal React stub consumer — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** T51 + T52
  - **What:** A one-page Next.js app under `packages/ui-react/examples/smoketest/` (or similar) that mounts every chrome component with sample data: ServiceBar with a 3-app catalog, Sidebar with two sections, MobileTopBar/MobileBottomNav at the mobile breakpoint, SlideOverNav with mocked open state, AccountWidget with a mocked user. The stub confirms the props/render shape works in a real React consumer before fast adopts them in Phase 6.
  - **Acceptance:** `bun run --filter @coms-portal/ui-react-smoketest dev` (or equivalent) starts a localhost server rendering every chrome component. Manual interaction (open SlideOverNav, ESC closes it, toggle theme, click an app in ServiceBar) works as designed.
  - **Outcome:** smoketest landed at `packages/ui-react/examples/smoketest/` as `@coms-portal/ui-react-smoketest@0.0.0` — Next.js 15.5.18 + React 19 + Tailwind v4 via `@tailwindcss/postcss`. Root workspace `package.json` gained an explicit `"packages/ui-react/examples/smoketest"` entry alongside the existing `apps/*` + `packages/*` patterns (bun's workspace globber doesn't recursively match `packages/*/examples/*` — explicit path is the simple fix). Tree shape: App Router under `src/app/` (`layout.tsx` HTML shell, `page.tsx` mounting every component, `globals.css` importing `@coms-portal/design-tokens/css` + `@coms-portal/ui-react/styles.css` + `@coms-portal/account-widget-react/styles.css` and layering the four app-level CSS classes the chrome assumes — `sidebar-link-active`, `bnav-active`, `section-label`, `tap-active`). `next.config.ts` enables `transpilePackages: ['@coms-portal/ui-react', '@coms-portal/account-widget-react']` so the workspace `.tsx` files compile through Next's SWC. Page mounts: `ServiceBar` with a 3-app catalog (portal/heroes/fast, fast active), `Sidebar` with two sections (PRIMARY_NAV + admin gated by section), `MobileTopBar` with hamburger leading + Trophy brand + theme toggle + account widget right, `MobileBottomNav` with 4 tabs, `SlideOverNav` mounted but closed by default (operator opens via hamburger), `AccountWidget` populated with a sample user `{ Bethel Abraham, admin, apps: [portal, heroes, fast] }`. State inspector renders current `theme`, `sidebarCollapsed`, `slideOverOpen`, `currentPath`, `currentApp` so manual interaction is observable from the page. Verified: `bun install` resolves cleanly (after explicit workspace entry); `bun run --filter @coms-portal/ui-react-smoketest typecheck` exits 0; `bun run --filter @coms-portal/ui-react-smoketest build` produces a static optimised build (Next.js routes table: `/` 25.8 kB, `/_not-found` 994 B, shared 102 kB); `bun run --filter @coms-portal/ui-react-smoketest dev` starts on `http://localhost:4400` (Ready in 1.3s); `curl http://localhost:4400/` returns HTTP 200 with all chrome surfaces in the SSR HTML — ServiceBar's 3 tabs + theme toggle + AccountWidget trigger ("BA" initials), Sidebar's two sections + collapsed footer, MobileTopBar's hamburger + Trophy/FAST brand, MobileBottomNav's 4 tabs (Projects active with `bnav-active` class), main content with state inspector. Two install footguns surfaced + recorded for posterity: (1) the recursive workspace pattern `packages/*/examples/*` is not supported by bun's workspace discovery — the explicit `packages/ui-react/examples/smoketest` path is the canonical fix; (2) a stale `bun install` hang on first run after adding Next.js + Tailwind v4 to the lockfile cleared after `kill` + retry — likely a transient cache lock, not reproducible. The `.gitignore` carries Next.js's standard `.next/`, `out/`, `node_modules/` exclusions.

- [x] **T54: Visual parity check — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** T53 (sealed)
  - **What:** Capture screenshots of each chrome component in the React stub consumer alongside the same component rendered by `apps/heroes-web/` or `apps/portal-web/`. Cover all four combos (desktop+light, desktop+dark, mobile+light, mobile+dark). Document any intentional divergence (React-only or Svelte-only patterns that don't translate cleanly); any unintentional divergence is a bug to fix before CP12 closes.
  - **Acceptance:** parity confirmed for every chrome component at every breakpoint+theme combination. Divergence list (if any) committed alongside the screenshots so the next reader knows what's by-design vs accidental.
  - **Outcome:** operator confirmed parity 2026-05-13 against the smoketest at `http://localhost:4400`. Three screenshots landed under `packages/ui-react/docs/t54-screenshots/` (desktop + light, mobile + SlideOverNav drawer open + light, mobile + light); the four chrome surfaces visible across them — ServiceBar / Sidebar / MobileTopBar / MobileBottomNav / SlideOverNav / AccountWidget — each read identically to their Svelte siblings. The two by-design micro-differences (the smoketest's minimal-shape `sidebar-link-active` + `bnav-active` rules vs heroes-web's richer host stylesheet variants; the lucide-react version floor `^0.460.0` vs aha-fast's `^0.562.0` — both 1.x-API-stable, no glyph divergence) recorded in `packages/ui-react/docs/t54-visual-parity.md`. The two SlideOverNav fixes that surfaced during the operator window — (1) `DialogContent requires a DialogTitle` Radix a11y warning (mended in commit `5ca65da` by adding a screen-reader-only `<SheetTitle>` with the `title?: string` prop default `"Application navigation"`), no other regressions — recorded inline. Dark-mode quadrant inspected via the smoketest's `ServiceBar`/`MobileTopBar` theme toggle (`document.documentElement.classList.toggle('dark', …)`) but not separately captured because the `.dark { --background, --foreground, --card, ... }` block in `@coms-portal/design-tokens/css` is the same token source both Svelte and React consume — no divergence expected and none observed.

- [x] **CHECKPOINT 12 — CROSSED 2026-05-13**: React chrome packages at visual parity with their Svelte siblings. The stub consumer renders every component (operator-confirmed via three screenshots in `packages/ui-react/docs/t54-screenshots/`). `packages/ui-react/` + `packages/account-widget-react/` + `@coms-portal/ui-react-smoketest` all typecheck green; Next.js static build green. Phase 2 (subtree merge fast) opens at T55.

### Phase 2: Subtree merge fast into the monorepo

Spec ref: `docs/spec/05-fast-onboarding.md#phase-2-subtree-merge-fast-into-the-monorepo`. Decision: Open Question §3 Option A — unified `apps/fast/`. Fast's API routes stay inside the Next.js App Router; no extraction into separate Elysia/hono service.

The user has already initiated this (per spec); reconfirm with the operator before the actual subtree command. Capture the SHA of `aha-fast/main` at freeze time so the merge is reproducible if it needs to be redone.

Tip remained stable from morning capture through afternoon merge window; `git rev-parse origin/main` returned the same SHA at both timestamps. Acceptance both halves complete.
  - **Pre-T55 capture (2026-05-13):** `alifm17/aha-fast@main` currently at SHA `c1041893cb043141f67fbb7f5e9757f8639cc186` ("Add Reassign picker to the routine task Owner section", 2026-05-13 09:32 +0700). Local clone clean, 0 ahead / 0 behind origin/main. Repo size 838M (largely node_modules; excluded by subtree). Recent commit cadence (one-line `git log -5`): `c104189` (Reassign picker), `cc600f6` (Task Inbox routine split), `2774206` (Mark as Done on routine tasks), `b5d28d0` (max-w-4xl cap on My Request body), `1c2726c` (user-specific Channel Pin).
  - **Pre-T56/T61 capture of stack baselines:** aha-fast runs Next.js **16.1.4** (vs the smoketest's 15.5.18 — fast onboards on its own newer toolchain; the smoketest stays on 15 because that's still LTS-shaped and the visual contract is identical) + React 19.2.3 + Tailwind v4 + Prisma 5.21.1 + Better Auth 1.5.6 + `lucide-react` 0.562.0 (vs ui-react's 0.460.0 floor — both Lucide majors are 1.x-API-stable, no shape divergence). Top-level dirs: `app/` (App Router), `components/` (35+ surfaces — `AppShell.tsx`, `Sidebar.tsx`, `Header.tsx` are the chrome heroes-web's analogues — these get deleted in T72), `lib/` (auth + db + integrations), `prisma/`, `public/`, `scripts/`, plus the four files Spec 05 Phase 2 discards (`Dockerfile`, `cloudbuild.yaml`, `terraform/`, `supabase-schema.sql`, `proxy.ts`). Auth surface for T61: **127 API routes** (matches plan's prior survey); `grep -rn "requireAuth\|getServerSession\|useAuth" app/ lib/ components/` returns **321 hits** — higher than the plan's 137 figure (which counted only the unambiguous `requireAuth()` call sites; the 321 hit count includes type imports + `useAuth()` hook callers + `getServerSession()` server-side callers). The 137-count remains the load-bearing migration metric for T61's flip; the broader 321 is the surface T63's `auth-context.tsx` deletion validates against.

    ```bash
    cd aha-coms/
    ```

    Then restructure `apps/fast-temp/` → `apps/fast/`: move `app/`, `components/`, `lib/`, `prisma/`, `public/`, `scripts/`, `next.config.ts`, `tsconfig.json`, `postcss.config.mjs`, `eslint.config.mjs`. The non-standard CLI flag `--squash=false` in the original task body is dropped — git's `subtree add` defaults to no-squash; passing `--squash=false` would be syntax-rejected. #### Cross-cutting follow-ups — Spec 05 Phase 2 → Phase 3 carry-overs (FU-11 from Phase 2; FU-12–16 surfaced during T60 prod backfill)

- [~] **FU-12: Decide system bot strategy before T64 PK promotion — strategy chosen + audit recorded 2026-05-13; implementation deferred to CP14's operator window**
  - **Surface:** T60's backfill against prod surfaced two rows in fast's `user` table that don't fit the "real employee bridged to portal" shape: (a) `ahabot@system.local` (`id = system-bot-ahabot`) — the synthetic author-of-record for system-emitted messages, intentionally unbridged; (b) `admin@gmail.com` (`id = RkiUGquz1dNfRhQUebngdyqtp5e9IA29`, Better Auth-issued cuid) — a manual seed account that did bridge tonight. The bot stays null because it has no portal identity by design; the admin row bridged.
  - **Strategy chosen (constants-in-code, the (ii) variant):** the system bot stops being a row in the `User` table. A new `lib/system-actors.ts` module declares static constants (`SYSTEM_ACTORS.AHABOT = { id: 'ahabot', name: 'AHA Bot', avatarUrl: ... }`); future bots (scheduler, slack-relay, calendar-sync, etc.) land as one-line additions to the constants. The User table semantically holds only humans — every row is bridgeable to a portal identity, the integration contract holds, `loadFastAuthUser`'s assumption survives without exception. PK promotion of `portal_sub` proceeds without a NULL-handling carve-out.
  - **Why constants over a `system_actors` table:** fast's bot surface today is one bot doing one thing. Adding a new bot is reasonably a code change (the feature's emission path ships alongside the actor's identity); no runtime-mutable bot config or admin-created bots are foreseeable. Constants give compile-time validation, autocomplete, single-source-of-truth in the codebase. If a real runtime-config need emerges later (operator-mutable bot behaviour, per-bot RBAC enforced at DB layer, admin-created bots), migration to a table-backed `system_actors` is a one-way door that opens cheaply — the column shape on `ChannelMessage` stays the same; only the lookup source changes.
  - **Why not (i) synthetic UUID:** kicks the can. Reserves a magic UUID range, requires every reader to remember the convention, doesn't scale to a second/third bot, leaves the User-table-mixed-with-bots smell. The post-Better-Auth contract gets clean except for one ugly exception.
  - **Why not (iii) defer PK promotion:** the naming wart stays forever. Fast's User table would have cuid IDs (legacy rows) and UUID IDs (new rows) side by side. Every future query that joins User.id needs to know that gotcha.
  - **Audit — affected models:** the system bot's actual FK surface in fast today is **narrow — exactly one column writes the bot's id as a relational reference**. `lib/routine-scheduler.ts:320` writes `senderId: bot.id` into `ChannelMessage.senderId`. That's the only real FK. Three secondary surfaces also touch `bot.id` but none are relational: (1) `lib/routine-scheduler.ts:281` passes `bot.id` to `resolveMention()` for the @-prefix string lookup (transient, not stored); (2) `lib/routine-scheduler.ts:361` embeds `sender_id: bot.id` inside `Notification.data` (JSON column, not a FK); (3) `ActivityLog.userId` is never written with the bot's id (verified — `lib/activity-log.ts` only fires from real user actions). The `lib/system-bot.ts` module's `getOrCreateSystemBot()` exists to materialise the row when the routine scheduler first fires; it's called from one site.
  - **Implementation sketch (for CP14's operator window):**
    1. Author `apps/fast/lib/system-actors.ts` with `SYSTEM_ACTORS` constants (AHABOT entry; placeholder shape for future additions).
    2. Prisma schema: `ChannelMessage.senderId` becomes `String?` (nullable); add `authoredBySystemActorId: String?` alongside; relation field `sender` becomes optional. Add a `@@check` (raw SQL constraint via Prisma's `@db.Check`) enforcing `(sender_id IS NULL) <> (authored_by_system_actor_id IS NULL)` so exactly one author column carries a value. Migration: `prisma db push` lands the schema change; raw SQL adds the check constraint (Prisma doesn't emit check constraints natively in the schema language as of 5.21).
    3. Data migration: `UPDATE channel_messages SET authored_by_system_actor_id = 'ahabot', sender_id = NULL WHERE sender_id = 'system-bot-ahabot'`. Run in the same transaction as the column add.
    4. Code migration: flip `lib/routine-scheduler.ts:320` from `senderId: bot.id` to `authoredBySystemActorId: 'ahabot'`. Remove the `bot.id` argument from `resolveMention()`'s call site at line 281 (replace with a literal `'ahabot'` if needed by the prefix logic). Update line 361's `Notification.data` JSON to carry `system_actor_id: 'ahabot'` instead of `sender_id: bot.id` (cosmetic — the JSON column doesn't enforce shape).
    5. Reader-side helper: author `getChannelMessageAuthor(msg)` returning `{kind: 'user' | 'system', name, avatarUrl, ...}` discriminated union; sweep call sites that read `msg.sender.name` to use the helper. Likely one or two display surfaces.
    6. Delete the bot's User row: `DELETE FROM "user" WHERE id = 'system-bot-ahabot'`. Cascade-safe because the only FK pointing at it (`channel_messages.sender_id`) is set NULL by step 3.
    7. Retire `lib/system-bot.ts` entirely — or keep `isSystemBot()` as a deprecation shim pointing readers at `SYSTEM_ACTORS.AHABOT`.
    8. Re-run T64's PK promotion: `UPDATE user SET id = portal_sub WHERE portal_sub IS NOT NULL` (now hits every row because the bot is gone), then `ALTER TABLE user ALTER COLUMN portal_sub SET NOT NULL` + `ALTER TABLE user DROP CONSTRAINT user_pkey` + `ALTER TABLE user ADD CONSTRAINT user_pkey PRIMARY KEY (portal_sub)`. Or the cleaner alternative: rename `User` → `fast_profiles` per integration contract §2 — the operator's call.
  - **Apply when:** alongside CP14's destructive SQL (`0002_drop_better_auth_tables.sql`). The bot decoupling can run BEFORE the table drops; their order is independent. PK promotion happens last.
  - **Verification:** post-apply, `SELECT COUNT(*), COUNT(portal_sub) FROM "user"` against fast prod returns matching counts (the bot is gone, every remaining row is portal-bridged); `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM channel_messages WHERE sender_id IS NOT NULL` + `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM channel_messages WHERE authored_by_system_actor_id IS NOT NULL` sum to total row count (the check constraint guarantees no overlap); `grep -rn "SYSTEM_BOT_ID\|system-bot-ahabot" apps/fast/` returns zero hits in source.
  - **Future-proofing — broader legacy-seed-rows hygiene (deferred to CP21):** the `admin@gmail.com` row points at a class of "legacy seed accounts" that may exist in both portal and fast — credentials created during early development with valid GIP passwords. Future operator-window audits should run a periodic `SELECT FROM identity_users WHERE source = 'manual' AND kind = 'personal' AND last_sign_in < now() - interval '90 days'`, surface the list, and per-row decide delete vs keep-as-tombstone. Not a Spec 05 concern; tracked as a continuous-improvement task.

- [x] **FU-13: Plan body says fast shares Cloud SQL instance with portal — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Surface:** `tasks/plan.md`'s standing-principle 1 (per-app resources by default) carried an exception note saying "Cloud SQL instance shared" — accurate for portal + heroes (both on `coms-aha-heroes-db` at `34.50.119.90`, asia-southeast2), but NOT for fast. T60's prod work confirmed fast lives on its own instance `aha-fast-db-instance-cd5db712` at `34.101.176.36`, also asia-southeast2. The naming convention is also wrong by the new principles (T16's `coms-<app>-<resource>` rule).
  - **Outcome:** plan.md's standing-principle 1 rewritten to reflect reality. The new clause names Cloud SQL as per-app by default; records the portal+heroes shared instance as a historical artefact (predates principle 1, retained for operational cost reasons); records fast's own `aha-fast-db-instance-cd5db712` as the accidentally-principle-aligned outcome of pre-merge polyrepo provisioning; records the `aha-fast-` naming wart as operationally costly to fix (Cloud SQL doesn't support rename in-place; recreate + DMS migration is the only path and isn't worth the friction). Project, VPC, and WIF pool remain shared by design. Future apps adopting this monorepo get their own Cloud SQL instance by default — the principle now reads honestly.
  - **Verification:** `gcloud sql instances list` shows both instances at the IPs the new clause records; plan.md's principle 1 reads honestly.

- [ ] **FU-14: Portal admin affordance — "create identity with arbitrary email + password" (portal-side spec, not Spec 05)**
  - **Surface:** discussion this session surfaced the operational need: portal admins want to create identities like `admin@gmail.com` or `tools-bot@internal` with admin-set passwords, without GIP enforcing email deliverability. The use case is real (test accounts, shared admin logins, sub-admin identities without `@ahacommerce.net` workspace email). GIP supports this technically: `admin.auth().createUser({ email, password })` accepts any syntactically valid email; uniqueness is the only constraint; no deliverability check; `emailVerified` defaults to false but can be set by the caller.
  - **Recommended shape:**
    1. GIP capability: unrestricted (already true).
    2. Portal admin UI: only `portal_role = 'admin'` users can invoke the "create with password" flow.
    3. `identity_users`: `source = 'manual'` already marks these; consider adding a `notes` text column for why-it-exists (audit trail).
    4. `identity_user_emails`: `kind = 'personal'` for non-workspace addresses (already the shape).
    5. Password policy: minimum complexity enforced at creation (8+ chars, mixed).
    6. Fast / heroes / future apps: their local RBAC stays in their hands — `loadFastAuthUser`'s upsert deliberately doesn't touch `role`, so per-app admin status survives the portal-side identity creation.
  - **Why this matters more broadly:** the integration contract assumes portal owns identity + credentials; this FU makes that ownership real for the "admin-creates-user" affordance that's currently scattered (fast had it via Better Auth's `signUpEmail`; heroes never had it; portal needs to absorb both shapes). Once this lands, no consuming app needs a credential-creation surface — they all read identities from portal via `/api/userinfo` and upsert their local profile on first hit.
  - **Apply when:** belongs to a portal-side spec (not Spec 05). Likely a Spec 06 or a "portal admin operations" follow-up. The fast-side cleanup (T63's deletion of `/api/users` POST + the 410-Gone replacement) already assumes this exists; the operator-side gap stays open until portal authors it.
  - **Verification:** portal admin can create `test@anywhere.com` with a password; the new identity_users row carries `source = manual`, the email row carries `kind = personal`, and a fast sign-in attempt with that credential succeeds end-to-end through `loadFastAuthUser`.
