- [x] **FU-15: Hardcoded prod DB password in `apps/fast/scripts/*.ts` — code-side sealed 2026-05-13; rotation closed via Op-3 in T83's first-apply window 2026-05-14; history scrub closed via FU-19 (partial-1) force-push 2026-05-14**
  - **Surface:** the same `'***REMOVED-FU-19-DB-PW***'` literal hid in FIVE scripts, not just `add-teams.ts` — also `check-teams.ts`, `set-leader.ts`, `reseed-teams.ts`, `set-admin.ts`. All five constructed an explicit `datasources.db.url` against the prod IP `34.101.176.36`. Same admin user (`aha-fast-admin`) across all five.
  - **Outcome (code-side):** all five scripts rewritten to read `DATABASE_URL` from `process.env`. The explicit `datasources` block retires; `new PrismaClient()` reads the env via Prisma's default behaviour, matching `backfill-portal-sub.ts`'s shape. Each script gains a fail-fast guard (`if (!process.env.DATABASE_URL) { process.exit(1); }`) and a header comment pointing operators at `add-teams.ts`'s runbook. Final grep: `grep -rn "Mvpvrgri\|34.101.176.36" apps/fast/scripts/` returns zero hits. The runbook itself stays one-line: `export DATABASE_URL='postgres://aha-fast-admin:<pw>@<host>:5432/aha-fast-db' && bun run apps/fast/scripts/<script>.ts`.
  - **Outcome (operator-window, deferred at the time):** the working tree no longer leaks the credential, but **git history still carries it**. Five commits in the subtree-merge era (pre-T56) embed the literal — recoverable only by a destructive `git filter-repo` history rewrite + force-push, which the operator deferred at the time (the repo is public so the credential is effectively exposed already; a rotation is the safer mitigation than a history rewrite). Recommended rotation: (a) generate a new password (`openssl rand -base64 32`); (b) `gcloud sql users set-password aha-fast-admin --instance=aha-fast-db-instance-cd5db712 --password=<NEW>` updates Cloud SQL; (c) update Secret Manager (`echo -n "postgres://aha-fast-admin:<NEW>@..." | gcloud secrets versions add aha-fast-db-url --data-file=-`); (d) Cloud Run picks up the new value on next deploy (no service restart needed — Cloud Run resolves the secret on each cold start). Until rotation lands, anyone with public repo history access can read the prod credential.
  - **Verification:** `grep -rn "Mvpvrgri\|34.101.176.36" apps/fast/` (working tree) returns zero hits ✓. The operator-side rotation promotes the marker to `[x]`.
  - **Sealed via Op-3 (2026-05-14):** T83's first-apply operator window (line 1292 in this file) folded the rotation into Op-3 alongside `aha-fast-db-url`'s Secret Manager refresh. Cloud SQL's `aha-fast-admin` password rotated; Secret Manager's `aha-fast-db-url` versioned to the new DSN; Cloud Run picks up the new value on next deploy with no service restart needed. The live DSN no longer matches the historical leak — anyone reading the public-repo history reads a credential that authenticates against nothing. Marker flipped `[~]` → `[x]` in the post-CP21 cleanup window when the stale-marker situation was caught.
  - **History scrub sealed via FU-19 (partial-1) force-push 2026-05-14:** the `git filter-repo` rewrite + force-push that Op-3 deliberately kept separate from rotation closed cleanly later the same day. Every occurrence of the exact literal in every commit's blob content was substituted by the marker `***REMOVED-FU-19-DB-PW***`; the audit literal `Mvpvrgri` substring survives in `tasks/todo.md` prose only as a grep-pattern reference, which is documentation about the audit, not the credential. The history copy of the password is now unauthenticated **and** un-readable from the public refs. FU-19's surviving half (the Apps Script HMAC literal) waits on FU-18 (b)'s engineer closure.

- [x] **FU-16: Surviving fast auth routes belong to portal — sealed 2026-05-13 between CP14 and CP15**
  - **Surface:** T63 left six routes under `apps/fast/app/api/auth/` standing: `approve`, `forgot-password`, `google`, `me`, `pending`, `register`. T63's outcome explained each: `approve` + `pending` are admin operations over fast's `accountStatus` column (orthogonal to identity); `google` is OAuth callback for Google Calendar (T67's Phase 4 scope, doesn't go away); `me` is the new endpoint T61 authored. The two that DO logically belong to portal are `forgot-password` (generates reset tokens + emails them) and `register` (public signup creating Prisma User rows + sending activation emails). Both worked via Prisma + email directly — never imported Better Auth — but their semantics ("a person creates a fast account" / "a person resets their fast password") were already portal's responsibility per the integration contract.
  - **Why now (vs. the original "post-CP21" gate):** the audit step the original entry called out (Step 1, "post-T70 verify no UI surface POSTs to /api/auth/register|forgot-password") collapsed in-session — T62 had already razed the five credential page directories (`/login`, `/register`, `/forgot-password`, `/activate`, `/complete`), and T66's absolute-path sweep rewrote every auth-fallback to redirect to portal. A direct `grep -rn 'api/auth/register\|api/auth/forgot-password' apps/fast/` returned exactly one hit and it was inside the route's own comment. The post-CP21 gate was conservative scheduling, not a real prerequisite; the contract-tightening lands cleanly now.
  - **Outcome:** `apps/fast/app/api/auth/register/route.ts` (67 lines) + `apps/fast/app/api/auth/forgot-password/route.ts` (58 lines) deleted outright via `git rm -r`. **Side-cleanup:** `apps/fast/components/AppShell.tsx:13`'s `PUBLIC_ROUTES` array collapsed from `['/login', '/register', '/request', '/track', '/activate', '/complete', '/forgot-password', '/reset-password']` to `['/request', '/track']` — the six zombie page paths refer to directories T62 razed, so the strings never match a real URL (Next.js 404s before AppShell renders). Middleware's allowlist (`apps/fast/middleware.ts`) was already correct — names only `/request`, `/track`, the OAuth callback, and infra-shaped paths — so no middleware change needed.
  - **Verification:** `ls apps/fast/app/api/auth/` → `approve  google  me  pending` ✓. `grep -rln "fetch.*api/auth/register\|fetch.*api/auth/forgot-password" apps/fast/` → zero hits ✓. `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast typecheck` → exit 0 (the stale `.next/types/validator.ts` referenced the deleted routes; deleting `apps/fast/tsconfig.tsbuildinfo` + re-running after `next build` regenerated the validator types cleanly). `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` → exit 0, all routes prerender, `ƒ Proxy (Middleware)` registered. `bun run --filter '*' typecheck` → all 12 packages exit 0.
  - **What's NOT in scope:** the question of whether fast should KEEP its local `User` table or eventually delete it entirely (T64's deferred PK promotion + the integration contract's §2 "rename to `fast_profiles`" suggestion). That's CP14's destructive-apply window, not FU-16. The routes deleted here are the ones whose semantics moved to portal; the `User` table itself stays as fast's per-app profile substrate.

- [ ] **FU-17: `/api/slack/notify` route has no caller — wire it or delete it**
  - **Surface:** `apps/fast/app/api/slack/notify/route.ts` (117 lines) accepts `{ taskId, title, requesterName, requesterDivision, urgency, description }`, builds a Slack Block Kit message with urgency emoji + "Mark as Done" / "View in Dashboard" actions, and POSTs to `SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL`. A grep across `apps/fast/{app,components,lib}` for `slack/notify`, `slackNotify`, `notifySlack`, or any `fetch.*slack` returns **zero matches**. The route exists; no caller fires it. Surfaced during the Op-2 audit when deciding whether to create `aha-fast-slack-webhook-url` in Secret Manager.
  - **Two valid resolutions:**
    1. **Wire it.** Add a `fetch('/fast/api/slack/notify', ...)` call to the request-submission flow at `app/api/request/route.ts` (the natural caller — `sendRequestNotificationEmail` already fires there; Slack would be a sibling notification). Pair: create `aha-fast-slack-webhook-url` in Secret Manager + add the IaC reference back to `infra/fast/cloud-run.tf`'s secret env block. Once an operator records a real Slack delivery, FU-17 closes.
    2. **Delete it.** `git rm -r app/api/slack/notify/` + scrub `SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL` from `apps/fast/.env.example` + drop the corresponding IaC variable from the `infra/fast/` exclusion audit recorded in `variables.tf`. The route was authored speculatively (likely during fast's pre-merge polyrepo phase); removing it tightens the surface to what's actually load-bearing.
  - **Recommendation:** Wire it (Option 1). The Slack-Block payload is well-crafted and the use case (operations channel gets pinged on new requests) is a real product feature, not vestigial. Cost: ~30 lines in `app/api/request/route.ts` + the secret + IAM grant. Light enough to land alongside T76 or T77 if convenient.
  - **Apply when:** post-CP21 (after the corridor is real and the operations team has a Slack channel ready) OR alongside T76+T77 if the wiring is judged within Phase 7's scope.
  - **Acceptance:** option 1 — submitting a request via `/fast/track` fires the Slack webhook, message lands in #ops or wherever the webhook points, "Mark as Done" button updates the Task via fast's API; option 2 — `apps/fast/app/api/slack/notify/` does not exist, no env references survive.

- [x] **FU-18: Retire Resend — it's the fallback that doesn't deliver**
  - **Sealed 2026-05-14** across a nine-commit chain ending at `6a03dc7` (pre-FU-19-rewrite: `4f6d28b`). Five per-function retirements drained Resend out of `sendRequestNotificationEmail`, `sendTaskClaimedEmail`, `sendTaskCompletedEmail`, `sendAccountApprovedEmail`, `sendAccountRejectedEmail`. The two orphans (`sendActivationEmail` + `sendPasswordResetEmail`) deleted outright. The `_resend` client + `getResend()` factory + `import { Resend } from 'resend'` + the `resend` dependency in `apps/fast/package.json` + the resolved entries in `bun.lock` + the `RESEND_API_KEY=…` line in `.env.example` all withdrew. The notification env var renamed `RESEND_NOTIFICATION_EMAIL` → `ADMIN_NOTIFICATION_EMAIL` end-to-end (lib/email.ts + .env.example + infra/fast/variables.tf + infra/fast/cloud-run.tf). The Apps Script HMAC fallback literal at `apps/fast/lib/email.ts:9` (formerly :16) retired — runtime now requires `APPS_SCRIPT_SECRET` to be set; unset value warns + fails rather than authenticating with the historical literal. Incidental bug closed along the way: three of the five active senders had a function-entry guard on `RESEND_API_KEY` that silently no-op'd the entire send on the new Cloud Run revision (which runs without the key) — that no-op-via-guard shape is gone. The umbrella surface block below remains for the historical context that motivated the retirement.
  - **Caveat — Apps Script source mirror + FU-19 (b) handoff state.** Three of the five rotation steps landed during the 2026-05-14 evening operator window (commits `40e3b04`, `e99b82f` — pre-FU-19-rewrite: `ac2d801`, `654679f`); two remain for the engineer because they require Apps Script web-editor access (the script lives under `alif.masyhur@ahacommerce.net`, not the operator's `handers.the@ahacommerce.net`). State at handoff:
    1. **Done (`40e3b04`, pre-FU-19-rewrite `ac2d801`):** `apps/fast/scripts/google-apps-script-email.js` rewrites to read SHARED_SECRET from `PropertiesService.getScriptProperties().getProperty('SHARED_SECRET')`; the historical literal `aha-fast-email-secret-2026` is gone from the source tree.
    2. **Done (this commit, via `tofu apply`):** Secret Manager `aha-fast-apps-script-secret` has v1 (enabled, original literal value — what Cloud Run reads) + v2 (disabled, holds a freshly-generated candidate 64-hex-char random value written via `openssl rand -hex 32`). `infra/fast/cloud-run.tf:153` pins `APPS_SCRIPT_SECRET` to `version = "1"` explicitly so cold-starts stay deterministic during the window (Secret Manager's `:latest` alias resolves to v2 by version number regardless of disabled state — pinning to `"1"` sidesteps that ambiguity).
    3. **TODO — Apps Script editor (engineer):** open the Apps Script project at https://script.google.com (logged in as the owner), replace `Code.gs` with the contents of `apps/fast/scripts/google-apps-script-email.js`, save, set the `SHARED_SECRET` script property (Project Settings → Script Properties) to a chosen value — either re-enable v2 and read its value (`gcloud secrets versions enable 2 --secret=aha-fast-apps-script-secret --project=fbi-dev-484410 && gcloud secrets versions access 2 --secret=aha-fast-apps-script-secret --project=fbi-dev-484410`) or generate a new value and `gcloud secrets versions add` it as v3. Run `testSend` in the editor to verify end-to-end, then Deploy → Manage deployments → existing deployment → edit (pencil) → "New version" → Deploy.
    4. **TODO — Cloud Run revision (engineer or operator):** edit `infra/fast/cloud-run.tf` line 153 to change `version = "1"` back to `"latest"` (or to the specific version number the engineer chose), then `tofu apply -var alert_email=handers.the@ahacommerce.net` from `infra/fast/`. Cloud Run rolls a new revision pinned to the new version; cold-start reads the matching value; emails resume sending against the rotated Apps Script.
    5. **TODO — Cleanup (engineer):** once verified, disable v1 (`gcloud secrets versions disable 1 --secret=aha-fast-apps-script-secret --project=fbi-dev-484410`) so the historical literal is unauthenticated end-to-end. FU-19's (b) bucket then closes; the force-push scrub can proceed without leaving a usable secret in any post-rewrite clone.
  - **Surface:** `apps/fast/lib/email.ts` carries 8 exported send functions; 5 are actively called (request-notification, task-claimed, task-completed, account-approved, account-rejected) and 1 primitive (`sendViaAppsScript`). Two — `sendActivationEmail` + `sendPasswordResetEmail` — became orphans when FU-16 deleted their callers (the `/api/auth/register` + `/api/auth/forgot-password` routes). Of the 5 active functions, **every one tries Apps Script FIRST and only falls back to Resend on Apps Script failure**. Resend on free tier (`from: onboarding@resend.dev`) can only deliver to one verified address (`alif.masyhur@ahacommerce.net`), so the fallback only "works" for one operator's debug inbox; for every real user it's a no-op. Conclusion: Apps Script is the production email path; Resend is dead-weight maintenance burden.
  - **What to retire:**
    - Drop the `resend` dependency from `apps/fast/package.json` (with `import { Resend } from 'resend'` going).
    - In `lib/email.ts`: delete `_resend` + `getResend()` (lines 4-8), delete the `if (!process.env.RESEND_API_KEY) return false` guards (5 sites), delete the Resend `try { ... await getResend().emails.send(...) } catch` blocks at the tail of each of the 5 active send functions. Each active function shrinks from "try Apps Script, fall back to Resend" to "send via Apps Script, return its result".
    - Delete `sendActivationEmail` (lines 381-450) + `sendPasswordResetEmail` (lines 451-511) outright — orphans post-FU-16.
    - Rename `RESEND_NOTIFICATION_EMAIL` env var to `ADMIN_NOTIFICATION_EMAIL` (the semantic name; the variable name's "RESEND_" prefix is misleading since both Apps Script + Resend used it). Update `lib/email.ts:11`. Update `apps/fast/.env.example`. Update `infra/fast/variables.tf` (rename `resend_notification_email` → `admin_notification_email`) + `infra/fast/cloud-run.tf` (the env-var label).
    - Strip the `RESEND_API_KEY` line from `apps/fast/.env.example`.
  - **Why this is non-trivial:** `lib/email.ts` is ~600 lines and the per-function "try Apps Script then Resend" pattern is interleaved with the HTML template construction for each notification type. Refactor needs care — a wrong drop-edit produces silently-broken email paths. Recommend per-function commits (one commit per send function retiring its Resend fallback) so each diff is reviewable.
  - **Why now:** the public-repo + free-tier-sandbox combination makes the current setup misleading — it looks like fast has redundant email channels but in production only Apps Script delivers. Future operators reading the code waste time understanding a fallback that never fires. The Op-2 audit surfaced the gap; closing it removes the misdirection.
  - **Apply when:** between CP14 and CP21, when the fast tree is otherwise stable and the email surface isn't being modified for other reasons. Estimate: 2-3 hours for the refactor + manual smoke test against each of the 5 active send paths.
  - **Acceptance:** `grep -rn 'from .resend.' apps/fast/` returns zero hits; `grep -rn 'RESEND_API_KEY' apps/fast/` returns zero hits; `lib/email.ts` shrinks by ~150 lines; the 5 active send paths still deliver via Apps Script in a smoke test; `package.json` no longer carries `resend`; the orphaned activation + password-reset functions are gone.

- [~] **FU-19: Scrub leaked secrets from git history + force-push — partial-1 sealed 2026-05-14; partial-2 (Apps Script HMAC) gated on FU-18 (b) closure**
  - **Partial-1 sealed 2026-05-14 (DB password):** the `git filter-repo --replace-text` rewrite + `--force` push of the rewritten `main` to `origin` closed literal #1 cleanly. Audit catalogue of the five pre-rewrite commits where the literal lived in blob content (old SHAs, recorded for the audit trail; these no longer exist on origin): (a) `5dd6c2a` ("AHA FAST - Full application with all features", the subtree-import root that imported the literal in 5 `apps/fast/scripts/*.ts` seed scripts), (b) `03a31f0` ("Pull the prod credential out of five seed scripts — FU-15 code-side cut", the removal commit), (c) `3d93de7` ("Seed FU-12 through FU-16 — the corridor's loose ends"), (d) `13d4a77` ("Record system bot strategy + the narrow audit it rests on — FU-12"), (e) `4fc602d` ("Wire the destructive-migration escape hatch + queue the after-items"). The first two carry the literal in code; the last three carry it in `tasks/todo.md` prose. Method: fresh `git clone --mirror` to `/tmp/aha-coms-scrub.git`; `git filter-repo --replace-text /tmp/fu-19-replacements.txt` with the single line `_=*(Q<&Mvpvrgri%==>***REMOVED-FU-19-DB-PW***`; verify; `git remote add origin ...`; `git push --force origin refs/heads/main:refs/heads/main`. Branch protection's `allow_force_pushes: false` rejected the first attempt (admins can't bypass it despite `enforce_admins: false`); temporarily relaxed via `gh api -X PUT /repos/mrdoorba/aha-coms/branches/main/protection` flipping `allow_force_pushes` to `true`, pushed, then immediately PUT back to `false` to restore the pre-state. Pre-rewrite count of the `Mvpvrgri` substring across all refs: 23 lines (`git log --all -p | grep -c Mvpvrgri`). Post-rewrite count of the EXACT literal `_=*(Q<&Mvpvrgri%`: 0 lines (`git log --all -p | grep -Fc '_=*(Q<&Mvpvrgri%'`). Residual `Mvpvrgri` substring count: 8 lines — all are prose in `tasks/todo.md` (and one rewritten commit message) documenting the audit grep pattern `"Mvpvrgri\|34.101.176.36"`, not the credential. The 4-character substring without the surrounding `_=*(Q<&...%` punctuation does not authenticate against anything; documentation of what was audited stays informative for future readers. **SHA mapping (top of main, old → new):** `654679f` → `e99b82f` ("Pin APPS_SCRIPT_SECRET to v1"); `ac2d801` → `40e3b04` ("Lift the Apps Script source mirror to PropertiesService"); `949ef57` → `5b9d5a4` ("Seal FU-18 + FU-25"); `4f6d28b` → `6a03dc7` ("Retire the Apps Script HMAC's fallback literal"); `258eed7` → `34d3038` ("Re-name the notification corridor"). `git filter-repo` auto-rewrote inline SHA references in commit messages (the "Related: ..." trailers chain across the FU-18 commits stays internally consistent post-rewrite); blob-content SHA mentions in `tasks/todo.md` did NOT auto-rewrite and are repaired by this same commit. **Local backup ref:** annotated tag `pre-fu-19-scrub-2026-05-14` (NOT pushed) pins the pre-rewrite commit `654679f` in the working repo's object store, keeping those objects reachable through the 90-day GitHub GC grace window. **Recovery path if the rewrite is ever wrong:** delete the backup tag locally; force-push it as `main` (after relaxing `allow_force_pushes` again). **Side effects on the wider corridor:** every commit reference in old PR descriptions, issue threads, dashboards, monitoring annotations, etc. that named pre-rewrite SHAs is now stale; GitHub keeps the old SHAs accessible via raw URL for ~90 days, then 404s. The five PRs in `refs/pull/*/head` (the mirror saw `pull/1/head` + `pull/2/head`) were not pushed back (server-managed; GitHub regenerates them lazily). **Partial-2 (Apps Script HMAC literal `aha-fast-email-secret-2026`) deferred:** Secret Manager v1 (the literal's value) is still enabled and Cloud Run is pinned to v1 — scrubbing the literal from history NOW would still leave a usable secret in any pre-rewrite clone because production authenticates against v1. Waits on FU-18 (b)'s engineer closure (Apps Script editor steps 3-5 in FU-18's caveat block; once v1 disables, partial-2 can scrub literal #2 in a second force-push window). A second force-push will rewrite SHAs again, including the SHAs this partial-1 just minted.
  - **Surface:** The `mrdoorba/aha-coms` repository is public; git history carries at least two secrets that are now considered compromised by exposure:
    1. **Fast's prod Postgres password** (`***REMOVED-FU-19-DB-PW***` — the raw DSN with embedded password) was committed at least 5 times in the subtree-merge era (pre-T56, when aha-fast was still a separate npm-based repo). FU-15 closed the working-tree leak (commit `03a31f0` pulled the credential from five seed scripts) but explicitly deferred the history rewrite. Rotation is the safer mitigation than rewrite (Op-3) — but rotation only invalidates the live credential; the history copy is permanently in any clone made before the rotation lands.
    2. **The Apps Script HMAC fallback** (`aha-fast-email-secret-2026`) appears in `apps/fast/lib/email.ts:16` as a hardcoded default for `APPS_SCRIPT_SECRET` — the literal IS the prod value (matching the legacy Cloud Run env). FU-18 retires the fallback as part of the Resend refactor; until then, every commit touching that file embeds the value, and even after FU-18 closes, history still carries it.
    3. **Possible additional leaks** not yet audited: any commits referencing `process.env.GOOGLE_CLIENT_SECRET`, OAuth tokens, Resend API key values that may have been embedded in dev fixtures, etc.
  - **Why this matters:** the repo's `git log -p` is public-readable. Anyone can `git clone` and grep historical commits for `password|secret|api_key|GOCSPX-|re_` to harvest live credentials. The window is currently as wide as the time since each commit landed; closing it requires either (a) rotating every leaked credential AND accepting that old-clone copies remain usable until the credential rotates, OR (b) rewriting history to remove the values + force-pushing, which makes old-clone copies obsolete after the next fetch.
  - **Tool of choice:** `git filter-repo` (the modern replacement for `git filter-branch`; `bfg-repo-cleaner` is the second option but is less actively maintained). Install: `pip install git-filter-repo` or `brew install git-filter-repo`.
  - **Sequence (recommended):**
    1. **Audit phase** — grep `git log -p --all -G '<pattern>'` for each known secret value + likely-secret patterns. Catalogue every offending commit. Record the catalogue inline in this entry so the rewrite is auditable. Run BEFORE the rewrite — once history is gone, the catalogue is gone too.
    2. **Rotation phase** — rotate each catalogued credential against its live host (Cloud SQL password, Apps Script HMAC, OAuth client secret, etc.). After rotation, the history copy still leaks the secret but it no longer authenticates against any live system. Op-3 closes (a); FU-18 took the first half of (b) by retiring the runtime fallback at `apps/fast/lib/email.ts:9` — the second half (Apps Script source rotation + Secret Manager refresh + Cloud Run redeploy) still pends an operator window per FU-18's "Caveat — Apps Script source mirror" note; FU-25's audit closes (c) as no-op since no `GOCSPX-`-prefixed literal exists in history.
    3. **Pre-flight** — confirm no contributor has unmerged work on the branches being rewritten. Public repo with one contributor (mrdoorba) makes this trivially safe; if the repo gets transferred to an org with more contributors (FU-20), the pre-flight gets harder.
    4. **Rewrite** — `git filter-repo --replace-text replacements.txt` with one literal per leaked value. The tool rewrites every commit that contained the literal, replacing with `***REMOVED***` or similar marker. Tags + refs follow.
    5. **Force-push** — `git push --force-with-lease origin main` (and every other branch). `--force-with-lease` rejects the push if anyone else has pushed since you last fetched, which catches race conditions.
    6. **Coordinate** — every existing clone needs `git fetch --prune origin && git reset --hard origin/main` to pick up the rewritten history. Skip and the old refs linger as dangling commits in their reflog (technically still readable; the actual fix is to encourage re-clone).
    7. **Verify** — `git log --all -p | grep -E '<old-pattern>'` returns zero hits across history. Cloud Build / GHA cached layers may still embed old values if any docker image cached a layer that hashed the secret — verify by re-running deploys + observing fresh image SHAs.
  - **Risk assessment:**
    - **Destructive.** Rewrites every commit hash; PR / issue / commit links to old SHAs break.
    - **Public-history-permanence concern:** GitHub keeps old objects for ~90 days after force-push (the "garbage collection grace period"); within that window the old commits are still accessible via raw SHA URLs. After 90 days they're gone unless someone made an archive (Software Heritage, archive.org, etc.) before the rewrite.
    - **Coordinate with FU-20 (repo transfer):** if the repo is transferring to a new org, do the scrub BEFORE the transfer so the rewritten history is what transfers. Doing scrub after transfer means every member of the new org has to re-clone.
  - **Apply when:** before FU-20 (org transfer); after Op-3 (DB rotation) + FU-18 (Apps Script HMAC retirement) so rotation makes the history copy unauthenticated even before rewrite. Estimate: 2-3 hours including the audit phase, depending on how many leaked values surface.
  - **Acceptance:** `git log --all -p -G '<each catalogued pattern>'` returns zero hits across history; live deployment continues working post-rewrite (every workflow re-deploys after the force push); no contributor reports breakage from the rewrite.

- [x] **FU-20: Transfer repo ownership from `mrdoorba` to `AHA-Commerce-CIA-Project` org — sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Sealed 2026-05-14 across a four-commit chain** ending at the partial-closure seal of this entry. The repository's canonical URL is now `https://github.com/AHA-Commerce-CIA-Project/aha-coms`; old `mrdoorba/aha-coms` URLs auto-redirect via GitHub's transfer machinery for ~30 days then 404. Three author-commits prepared the in-tree state on `branch/repo-transfer`: `22bfc68` (IaC: portal tfvars + heroes/fast `github_org` defaults + the two WIF module-header comments), `e60ab9e` (package metadata: 7 `package.json` repository.url fields), `a9a0e23` (public docs: `apps/portal-api/src/routes/well-known.ts:60` + 3 `packages/*/CONTRIBUTING.md` DESIGN_SYSTEM.md links). Then the destructive cutover: `gh api -X POST /repos/mrdoorba/aha-coms/transfer --field new_owner=AHA-Commerce-CIA-Project` fired the transfer; `git remote set-url origin` aligned the working repo; three `tofu apply` invocations across heroes + fast + portal substates flipped the live WIF `attribute_condition` from `mrdoorba/aha-coms` to `AHA-Commerce-CIA-Project/aha-coms` AND the `wif_*_binding.member` principalSet path; `git push origin main` to the new origin fired all five Deploy workflows, which now authenticate against the new WIF binding.
  - **Refinement vs. the original FU-20 plan:** the planned sequence (transfer → push → tofu apply) carries an inherent failure window where deploys fire post-push but pre-apply and fail WIF auth. The actual sequence reversed apply and push (`transfer → tofu apply heroes/fast/portal → push`), eliminating the failure window in principle. Heroes + fast deploys succeeded first try (3-4 min each). **Portal deploys failed on first try with `Permission 'iam.serviceAccounts.getAccessToken' denied` at the 30-42s mark** — the workflow's `setup-gcloud` step reported "Successfully authenticated" but the subsequent `gcloud secrets versions access` failed when the deployer SA tried to impersonate via the freshly-rebuilt `wif_binding`. **Root cause: IAM propagation lag.** Portal's apply landed last (only ~1-2 min before workflows fired); heroes + fast had ~4 min for IAM to fully propagate, portal didn't. `gh run rerun --failed` ~5 min later let both portal deploys complete cleanly (portal-api 4m46s, portal-web 3m51s). **Mitigation for the next destructive WIF flip:** wait 60-120 seconds between the last `tofu apply` and the first push that fires WIF-authenticated workflows, or rerun any propagation-lag failures.
  - **Targeted applies vs. full applies.** Each substate carried pre-existing drift the FU-20 plan should NOT have touched: heroes' `coms_heroes_api.SELF_PUBLIC_URL` drift (live value `https://coms-heroes-api-45tyczfska-et.a.run.app`, declared `https://aha-coms.web.app`), portal's `coms_portal_web.client/client_version` going null (drift from `gcloud run deploy` annotations), portal's `coms_portal_api` getting a `SERVICE_URL=https://placeholder` env var added (the CLI's placeholder var leaking into the resource), and portal's `portal_runtime_brevo_api_key[0]` being destroyed (count=0 because the brevo wiring was deferred). **`tofu apply -target=...` constrained each apply to ONLY the two WIF resources** (`google_iam_workload_identity_pool_provider.github` + `google_service_account_iam_member.wif_*_binding`), leaving every other resource's drift as drift. **Three drift items now queued for separate triage** (recorded under a new follow-up entry below or against an existing FU-21 candidate — operator's call which corridor to file them under): (a) heroes-api SELF_PUBLIC_URL drift, (b) portal-api SERVICE_URL placeholder leak from CLI vars, (c) portal_runtime_brevo_api_key count=0 destroy.
  - **Slug catalogue + final state.** Seventeen line-level edits across 14 files. Three buckets: (a) IaC load-bearing (3 files: `infra/terraform.tfvars`, `infra/heroes/variables.tf`, `infra/fast/variables.tf` — `github_org` defaults / `github_repo` value flipped), (b) IaC cosmetic (3 files: `infra/terraform.tfvars.example`, `infra/heroes/modules/github-wif/main.tf` comment header, `infra/fast/modules/github-wif/main.tf` comment header), (c) in-tree metadata + docs (8 files: 7 `packages/*/package.json` `repository.url` fields + 1 `apps/portal-api/src/routes/well-known.ts:60` URL + 3 `packages/*/CONTRIBUTING.md` DESIGN_SYSTEM.md links — wait, that's 11 not 8; revised count below). Final catalogue (precise): IaC load-bearing = 4 (the 3 tfvars/variables.tf above + `infra/terraform.tfvars.example`), IaC comments = 2, package.json repository.url = 7, public docs = 1 (well-known.ts) + 3 (CONTRIBUTING.md) = 4. Total: 17. **NOT in scope:** the retired-polyrepo references in `DESIGN_SYSTEM.md` + several `packages/*/README.md` + `packages/sdk/{MIGRATION,CHANGELOG}.md` + `packages/sdk/examples/*/{bun.lock,package.json,README.md,smoketest.test.ts}` files that name `mrdoorba/coms-ui|coms-design-tokens|coms-account-widget|coms-sdk` — those are archived polyrepos that stayed at their old `mrdoorba` location post-FU-20 (the org transfer relocates only `mrdoorba/aha-coms`); the doc rot from the pre-monorepo era is a separate corridor.
  - **Verification.** All five Deploy workflows fire green on the new origin's main: `Deploy — fast` 3m27s, `Deploy — heroes-api` 4m2s, `Deploy — heroes-web` 4m18s, `Deploy — portal-api` 4m46s (re-run), `Deploy — portal-web` 3m51s (re-run). Live health endpoints: `curl https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/health` returns HTTP 200 with `dbReachable:true`; `curl https://aha-coms.web.app/heroes/api/healthz` returns HTTP 200 with `status:ok`; `curl https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/dashboard` returns HTTP 307 to portal sign-in (T68 middleware redirect intact). Live WIF state per substate: `gcloud iam workload-identity-pools providers describe ... --format='json(attributeCondition)'` confirms the new `AHA-Commerce-CIA-Project/aha-coms` condition on all three pools; `gcloud iam service-accounts get-iam-policy <deployer-sa>` confirms each deployer SA's `principalSet://...attribute.repository/AHA-Commerce-CIA-Project/aha-coms` membership with `roles/iam.workloadIdentityUser`. **Branch protection preserved post-transfer:** `gh api /repos/AHA-Commerce-CIA-Project/aha-coms/branches/main/protection` reports identical settings to the pre-transfer state (`allow_force_pushes: false`, `enforce_admins: false`, required status checks `Typecheck & unit tests` + `Lint hardcoded URLs`).
  - **30-day grace window starts 2026-05-14.** Old `https://github.com/mrdoorba/aha-coms` URLs continue to redirect through ~2026-06-13. External links in dashboards, monitoring annotations, internal docs, integration-contract consumers, etc. should be updated during the window. After the grace, the old URLs hard-404.
  - **Related:** FU-19 partial-1 (the history scrub that landed earlier today, so the rewritten history transferred — not the original; the pre-rewrite SHAs are now triple-stale: rewritten by FU-19, then transferred by FU-20); FU-19 partial-2 (still gated on FU-18 (b)'s engineer closure — when that lands, the second force-push will rewrite SHAs again, this time on the new origin); FU-21 (the cost-optimization umbrella that now inherits three drift items surfaced during FU-20's plan-then-target dance); T17 (the original WIF pool/deployer SA shape that this FU re-aimed without restructuring); the integration-contract document URL (the well-known endpoint's `service_documentation` field now points at the new home; consumers that fetch `/.well-known/openid-configuration` post-transfer get the canonical URL up front).
  - **Surface:** The repository currently lives at `mrdoorba/aha-coms` — personal account ownership. The team's eventual home is an AHA Commerce GitHub organization (working name "AHA Commerce CIA Project"; actual GitHub slug needs operator confirmation — could be `aha-commerce`, `ahacommerce`, `aha-commerce-cia`, etc.). Transferring ownership moves the repository under org-level governance: shared admin, member-managed access, team-based permissions, org-wide policy enforcement.
  - **Why this is non-trivial:** the repo's identity (`<owner>/<repo>` slug) is encoded in **at least seven IaC + workflow locations** that all break the moment the URL changes:
    1. `infra/wif.tf` — portal WIF provider's `attribute_condition = "assertion.repository == 'mrdoorba/aha-coms'"` (verify exact location; this is the portal-side WIF declaration)
    2. `infra/heroes/modules/github-wif/main.tf` line 27 — heroes WIF provider's identical condition
    3. `infra/fast/modules/github-wif/main.tf` line 27 — fast WIF provider's identical condition
    4. `infra/heroes/variables.tf` — `github_repo` default = `"aha-coms"` (the org part comes from `github_org` which is `"mrdoorba"` — needs flipping)
    5. `infra/fast/variables.tf` — same default
    6. All five `.github/workflows/deploy-*.yml` files — none of them currently hardcode the org slug (they use `actions/checkout@v6` which auto-resolves), but any `repository:` field or `gh` invocation referencing the slug would break
    7. `repository.url` fields in 5 in-tree `package.json` files (per T23) — currently `https://github.com/mrdoorba/aha-coms` — these are docs-only but get stale immediately on transfer
  - **The moment the repo transfers, every WIF auth attempt fails.** The OIDC token the GHA runner mints carries the new repo path (`<new-org>/aha-coms`); the WIF provider's `attribute_condition` rejects it; every `Deploy — *` workflow fails authentication with a Google Auth error. **Mitigation: prepare a single synchronized cutover window.**
  - **Pre-flight (operator):**
    - Confirm the destination org's GitHub slug exactly. `gh api /user/orgs` lists every org the operator has membership in.
    - Confirm the operator has `owner` or `admin` role in the destination org (transfer-in requires that).
    - Confirm the destination org's name doesn't conflict with anything (e.g., a private repo of the same name already exists there).
    - Decide on member access: who from `mrdoorba`'s collaborators (if any) gets migrated to the new org's membership.
    - Decide on rename: keep the repo named `aha-coms`, or rename to something else as part of the transfer. (Recommendation: keep — every in-tree reference uses the literal `aha-coms`.)
  - **Sequence:**
    1. **Audit + record** every place the slug appears: `grep -rn 'mrdoorba/aha-coms' --include='*.tf' --include='*.yml' --include='*.md' --include='*.json' .`
    2. **Author the IaC + workflow + package.json updates on a branch** (`branch/repo-transfer`). Don't push yet. Three commits:
       - One bumping all three WIF `github_org` defaults from `mrdoorba` → `<new-org>` + the attribute_conditions
       - One updating the five `package.json` repository.url fields
       - One updating any docs (CONTEXT.md, README.md, etc.) that hardcode `mrdoorba/aha-coms`
    3. **GitHub transfer** — `gh api -X POST /repos/mrdoorba/aha-coms/transfer --field new_owner=<new-org>` (or via GitHub UI: Settings → Danger Zone → Transfer ownership). The repo immediately becomes `<new-org>/aha-coms`. Web URLs auto-redirect via GitHub's transfer machinery; git operations follow the redirect for a grace period (~30 days for `git clone`/`git push` against the old URL, then break).
    4. **Update local remote** — `git remote set-url origin https://github.com/<new-org>/aha-coms.git`.
    5. **Push the prepared branch** + merge to main. Every Cloud Run deploy still works because the old WIF still works during the GitHub redirect window — BUT the next deploy will fail because the OIDC token carries the new path. **Critical: do steps 6-8 BEFORE the next deploy fires.**
    6. **`tofu apply` across all three states** to update WIF attribute_conditions: `cd infra && tofu apply`, `cd infra/heroes && tofu apply -var alert_email=…`, `cd infra/fast && tofu apply`.
    7. **Verify the WIF cutover** — re-run a probe push (touch any file under one app's path filter) and confirm the corresponding deploy workflow succeeds. If it fails with `iam.googleapis.com/...InvalidGrant`, the WIF condition didn't update.
    8. **Update repo vars** — none of `WIF_PROVIDER_*` or `WIF_SA_*` change (they reference resource paths in GCP, not GitHub paths), but verify by listing.
  - **Risk assessment:**
    - **Reversible but painful** — GitHub allows transferring back to the original owner if needed, but each transfer forces a redirect-period cleanup.
    - **30-day grace window** — Old `mrdoorba/aha-coms` URLs continue to redirect for 30 days post-transfer; after that, hard 404. Update any external links (docs, dashboards, monitoring annotations) during the window.
    - **Coordinate with FU-19 (scrub):** do the scrub first so the rewritten history is what transfers. Doing scrub after transfer forces every org member to re-clone.
  - **Apply when:** after FU-19 scrub completes + after operator confirms the destination org's GitHub slug. Estimate: 60-90 minutes for the cutover window + 30 days of grace-window observation.
  - **Acceptance:** `gh repo view <new-org>/aha-coms` shows the repo lives there; all five GHA deploy workflows fire successfully on a post-transfer probe push; all three Tofu states apply cleanly; no in-tree reference to `mrdoorba/aha-coms` survives.

- [~] **FU-21: Cost optimization + CI/CD streamlining audit — drift-cleanup + always-warm slices sealed 2026-05-14; ~8 cost/CI candidates still open**
  - **Always-warm audit slice sealed 2026-05-14** as the second FU-21 corridor. Three structural changes across the three substates closed the "scale-to-zero is a documentation lie" finding the Op-12 surface bullet originally named. Per-service decisions recorded inline so a future reader sees why each service holds its current shape:
    - **portal-api + portal-web: flipped `cpu_idle = true`.** Live state had `cpu-throttling=false` (CPU always allocated when warm) inherited from the original T80 Cloud Run wiring — implicit because portal's `infra/cloud-run.tf:71-76, 246-251` declared `resources { limits {...} }` without an explicit `cpu_idle` attribute and the google provider's default appeared to be `false` for that shape. Cost-wise, today both services scale to zero (no uptime probe → no induced warmth → $0 baseline), so the CPU-throttling setting only mattered if a probe ever got added later (~$46/mo cost shock per service). Flipped preventively: `infra/cloud-run.tf` resources blocks both now carry `cpu_idle = true` with an inline FU-21 comment. `tofu plan` post-apply confirms `cpu_idle = false -> true` in-place update on both services; `gcloud run services describe coms-portal-{api,web}` returns `cpu-throttling: true` live.
    - **heroes uptime probe + uptime_failure alert: removed entirely.** `infra/heroes/modules/monitoring/main.tf` previously declared `google_monitoring_uptime_check_config "health"` probing `/heroes/api/health` every 300s + a dependent `google_monitoring_alert_policy "uptime_failure"`. The 5-min probe was keeping heroes-api always-warm (~$2.50/mo memory cost on a service that would otherwise scale to zero) and provided ~10-min outage detection. Both resources deleted; an inline comment block at the resource-block site preserves the rationale + the re-add path for any future operator who wants sub-30-min proactive detection back. The 5xx alert + the Cloud SQL CPU alert below stay as the remaining outage signals. **Trade-off named explicitly:** a service with zero traffic that's silently broken won't trigger the 5xx alert (no requests means no 5xx ratio), so outage detection becomes reactive (operator/user-reported) rather than proactive.
    - **fast uptime probe + uptime_failure alert: removed entirely.** Same shape as heroes — `infra/fast/modules/monitoring/main.tf` previously declared the same probe-and-alert pair for `/fast/api/health`. The probe was redundant against fast-web's `min=1` always-warm shape (Path X kept per Op-7), and the dependent alert had been carrying `enabled = false` as a "until T79 lands /fast/api/health" deferral that never flipped. Both resources deleted; the same inline comment block records the rationale + re-add path. fast's 5xx alert + Cloud SQL CPU alert remain.
    - **fast-web Path X reconsidered + flipped.** The first pass of this slice preserved `min=1, cpu_idle=false` per Op-7's deliberate triplet. The operator immediately questioned whether the cpu_idle=false half was actually load-bearing, prompting a second-pass audit of fast's codebase against Op-7's two stated reasons. Audit findings: (1) the cited "Prisma connection pool maintenance between requests" is purely internal to Prisma's runtime — `apps/fast/lib/db.ts` just declares `new PrismaClient(...)` via the standard globalThis singleton, no module-load setInterval, no module-level pool-maintenance hooks; the pool self-heals on the first query after a quiet window (sub-second cold-path latency, not a structural break); (2) the cited "in-flight Promise resolution between requests" is also a red herring — fast's three SSE routes (`apps/fast/app/api/{chat,notifications,channels}/stream/route.ts`) carry `setInterval` timers INSIDE their request handlers, scoped to the `request.signal.abort` lifecycle, so they run only WHILE the SSE connection is open — during which Cloud Run treats the request as in-flight and keeps CPU allocated regardless of cpu_idle; (3) `apps/fast/instrumentation.ts` doesn't exist (Next.js telemetry hook unused), and the only module-level async work in `apps/fast/lib/` is await-inside-function-bodies (helpers that get called from request handlers, never at module-load). **Conclusion: fast has zero module-level continuous background work; the Op-7 rationale was theoretical, not load-bearing.** Flipped `cpu_idle = true` via `infra/fast/cloud-run.tf` (line 227) with the full scaling-block comment block rewritten to record the audit findings + the savings calculus + the surviving rationale for the other two settings (min=1 stays for cold-start cost; session_affinity=true stays for SSE per-instance state). `tofu apply` reported 1 changed; `gcloud run services describe coms-fast-web` returns `cpu-throttling: true` post-apply; fast `/health` returns HTTP 200 with `dbReachable: true`. **Savings: ~$47/mo** (the CPU baseline drops from ~$46.66/mo to near $0 — only billed during actual request handling). The 50-200ms first-request-after-idle latency is acceptable for admin-grade interactive traffic; rollback is one-revision-roll-back away if it ever surfaces as a regression.
    - **End-state.** Suite Cloud Run always-on cost drops from roughly $52.50/mo to roughly $2.50/mo (the heroes-api ~$2.50/mo probe-induced warmth is gone; portal cpu_idle flip is preventive with $0 current effect; fast Path X cpu_idle flipped to true saving ~$47/mo). Cloud SQL × 2 at db-f1-micro is the ~$20/mo line that the umbrella's Cloud-SQL-tier-audit candidate still owns. **Total monthly: ~$22.50/mo** (down from ~$70/mo). The audit's main structural win is removing the "always-warm via 5-min probe" sleight-of-hand: every service in the suite is now honest about its scaling shape (portal/heroes-api/heroes-web/portal-web all actually scale to zero; fast still stays at min=1 but no longer pays for always-allocated CPU between requests).
    - **Acceptance for this slice.** `tofu plan` reports "No changes" against all three substates (portal, heroes, fast) post-apply — first time the entire suite is drift-free + audit-clean. `gcloud monitoring uptime list-configs --project=fbi-dev-484410` returns empty (both probes gone). `curl https://aha-coms.web.app/heroes/api/health` returns HTTP 200 + `db: connected`; `curl https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/health` returns HTTP 200 + `dbReachable: true`. portal-api + portal-web continue serving the OpenID-Connect + middleware routes (the cpu_idle flip rolled a new Cloud Run revision; traffic shifted gracefully).
  - **Drift-cleanup slice sealed 2026-05-14** as the first FU-21 corridor. Four drift items closed structurally (three named in FU-20's seal entry plus a fourth that surfaced during the diagnostic pass):
    - **(a) heroes-api SELF_PUBLIC_URL — fixed via heroes apply.** Live value drifted to `https://coms-heroes-api-45tyczfska-et.a.run.app` (Cloud Run autogen URL); IaC declares `var.heroes_public_origin` default `https://aha-coms.web.app` (Firebase Hosting). The comment block at `infra/heroes/cloud-run.tf:208-222` explicitly warns the Cloud Run URL breaks webhook OIDC audience verification when heroes' inbound webhook endpoint flips back to `active` (the historical FU-24 bug). Targeted `tofu apply -target=google_cloud_run_v2_service.coms_heroes_api -var alert_email=...` flipped the live env var to the correct Firebase Hosting host; `gcloud run services describe` confirms `SELF_PUBLIC_URL = https://aha-coms.web.app` post-apply. Heroes `/health` returns HTTP 200 + db connected.
    - **(b) portal-api SERVICE_URL placeholder leak — closed structurally via tfvars enrichment.** `infra/cloud-run.tf:124-131` sets `SERVICE_URL` + `PORTAL_PUBLIC_ORIGIN` from `var.service_url`, but `variables.tf:57-66` declares the variable without a default — every apply that DIDN'T pass `-var service_url=<real-url>` would have leaked the README's `https://placeholder` sentinel into the deployed env vars (FU-20's plan output showed this exact addition). Fix: `infra/terraform.tfvars` gains `service_url = "https://coms-portal-api-45tyczfska-et.a.run.app"` (the stable Cloud Run URL). Future applies converge against the live value with no `-var` flag; the placeholder pattern dies. **`infra/README.md` rewritten** to retire the "three variables deliberately not in tfvars" section — the README's prior model assumed the Cloud Run URL was only known post-first-deploy, but T80's first apply landed long ago and the URL is now stable.
    - **(c) portal_runtime_brevo_api_key[0] count=0 destroy — closed structurally via tfvars enrichment.** `infra/iam-portal-runtime.tf:58-63` gates the brevo-secret IAM grant on `var.mail_transport == "brevo" ? 1 : 0`; the variable's default is `"stdout"` and the prior tfvars had no override, so every apply would have destroyed the live grant (which `coms-portal-run-sa` currently uses to read `coms-portal-brevo-api-key` for outbound mail). FU-20's targeted-WIF apply skipped this resource, but the next non-targeted apply would have broken email delivery. Live state confirms `MAIL_TRANSPORT=brevo` + `BREVO_FROM=handers.the@ahacommerce.net` on portal-api — the brevo transport is actively in use. Fix: `infra/terraform.tfvars` gains `mail_transport = "brevo"` + `brevo_from = "handers.the@ahacommerce.net"`. Count stays 1, grant survives, email continues working. `gcloud secrets get-iam-policy coms-portal-brevo-api-key` confirms the `roles/secretmanager.secretAccessor` grant on `coms-portal-run-sa` post-changes.
    - **(d) `gcloud run deploy` client/client_version annotation feedback loop — eliminated via `lifecycle { ignore_changes }`.** Each `gcloud run deploy` from the GHA workflow tags the new revision with `client = "gcloud"` + `client_version = "<sdk-version>"` annotations. Tofu reads these as drift on every plan and proposes to clear them back to null; the next workflow run re-adds them — a permanent Sisyphean feedback loop. Fix: extended the existing `lifecycle { ignore_changes }` blocks on both `google_cloud_run_v2_service.coms_portal_api` + `coms_portal_web` in `infra/cloud-run.tf` to include `client` + `client_version`. Tofu now ignores those fields on both portal services. `tofu plan` against `infra/` reports "No changes" post-fix. (Heroes did NOT have the same drift on its current plan, so no IaC change needed there yet; surfaces only when heroes' workflow next applies the same annotations.)
    - Also lifted `bootstrap_admin_email = "handers.the@ahacommerce.net"` + `bootstrap_admin_name = "Mr. Door"` into tfvars as part of the same tfvars-alignment pass (they had the same "must-pass-at-CLI" shape as service_url; their live values are stable). The portal substate now plans clean (`tofu plan -var-file=terraform.tfvars` → "No changes. Your infrastructure matches the configuration"), heroes plans clean post-apply, fast plans clean. Three substates aligned end-to-end with their declared state for the first time.
  - **Acceptance for this slice:** all three FU-20-inherited drift items closed + the gcloud-annotation drift eliminated. Portal + fast + heroes substates all plan as "No changes" against their tfvars (heroes after the SELF_PUBLIC_URL apply landed). Five Cloud Run services healthy via `curl https://aha-coms.web.app/{fast,heroes}/api/health` returning HTTP 200 (portal endpoints unchanged; portal-api's drift was preventive only). The brevo IAM grant intact.
  - **What FU-21 still leaves open** (the umbrella's broader cost + CI/CD candidates listed in the Scope-candidates bullets below):
  - **Surface:** The aha-coms suite now runs three Cloud Run services (portal-api, portal-web, heroes-api, heroes-web, coms-fast-web — five services), three Cloud SQL instances (well, two: coms-aha-heroes-db shared by portal+heroes, plus aha-fast-db-instance), three Artifact Registries, five GHA deploy workflows, monitoring + alerts per app. Cost-wise, the suite is small but the constellation of resources has grown faster than the cost-attribution discipline; CI/CD has accumulated patterns that could share more.
  - **Scope candidates (the operator picks which to pursue):**
    - **Cloud Run right-sizing.** Five services, each declared `cpu = "1", memory = "512Mi"` — likely overspec for low-traffic admin apps. Audit per-service P50/P95 utilization via Cloud Monitoring → decide if any can drop to `cpu = "0.5"` or `memory = "256Mi"`. Each step down saves ~$5-10/month per service.
    - **Always-warm audit + uptime-probe interaction.** coms-fast-web currently runs `min=1, cpu_idle=false` (Path X matched legacy — deliberate). Heroes-api, portal-api also currently run `min=0` BUT each carries a Google Monitoring uptime check that probes every 5 minutes against its `/healthz` path. Cloud Run's idle-shutdown timeout is ~15 minutes; a probe every 5 minutes resets the idle timer indefinitely, so `min=0` services with active uptime checks are **always-warm in practice** even though their IaC says scale-to-zero. The structural effect: every probed service incurs ~$2-3/mo memory cost (free CPU thanks to `cpu_idle=true`, but allocated memory is metered). Suite-wide that's ~$5-10/mo for the probe-induced warmth on top of the explicit `min=1` cost for fast. Three valid resolutions to consider during this audit, per-service:
      - **A. Keep 5-min probes.** ~$5-10/mo suite-wide for probe-induced warmth. Outage detection within 10 min. Most useful for actively-monitored services. Net effect: `min=0` is a documentation lie; services run warm.
      - **B. Drop probe frequency to 15 min** (Monitoring's longest interval). Lets the 15-min Cloud Run idle timeout actually fire between probes; instance scales to zero. Cost approaches free-tier. Outage detection becomes ~30 min, acceptable for admin-grade services where users aren't expecting sub-minute response anyway.
      - **C. Drop the uptime probe entirely; lean on the 5xx alert.** Lowest cost. Risk: a service with zero traffic that's silently broken won't trigger 5xx (no requests, no 5xx ratio). You'd only learn of an outage from user reports.
      - **Decide per-service** based on cold-start tolerance + traffic volume. Recommendation: keep A for fast (Path X intentional), B for heroes-api + portal-api + heroes-web + portal-web (admin-grade, no users expecting sub-minute responsiveness), and document the per-service decisions in IaC comments so the next person to touch monitoring sees why each service chose its shape.
      - **Cost detail recorded for the audit:** Cloud Run pricing today (asia-southeast2) — vCPU `$0.0000180/s` when allocated, memory `$0.0000020/GiB-s`. For a warm instance at `cpu=1, memory=512Mi, cpu_idle=true`: CPU $0/mo (idle allocated free), memory ~$2.35/mo after free-tier 360k GiB-s. Probe request count (~52k/mo per service from 6 GCM probe regions) sits well within Cloud Run's 2M-request free tier — request cost is effectively zero.
    - **Cloud SQL tier audit.** Both DB instances run `db-f1-micro` (shared vCPU, ~$10/month each). Adequate today; revisit if connection pool exhaustion or CPU saturation appears in monitoring.
    - **Artifact Registry lifecycle.** Three repos (coms-portal-registry, coms-heroes-repo, coms-fast-registry) each retain 5 most-recent versions per `keep-minimum-versions` policy. Tune the retention count vs. on-demand re-pull cost; 5 is fine for a small team, larger teams may want 10-20 for safer rollback windows.
    - **GHA bun-install cache.** All five deploy workflows declare `actions/cache@v4` against `~/.bun/install/cache + node_modules + per-workspace node_modules`. Cache hit rate isn't currently observed; the `restore-keys: bun-${{ runner.os }}-` fallback might never hit if the cache layer schema drifted. Audit cache utilization, possibly switch to `actions/setup-bun@v2`'s built-in caching if it's cheaper to maintain.
    - **Docker layer caching.** Each `docker build` uses `--cache-from="${IMAGE}:latest"` — every commit pulls the latest tagged image as cache. Works but is bandwidth-heavy for runners. Alternative: GitHub Actions cache backend for buildx (`docker/build-push-action@v5` with `cache-from: type=gha`).
    - **Shared CI workflow.** The four `Deploy — *` workflows are 80% identical (same auth steps, same gcloud setup, same docker build pattern). Could factor common steps into a reusable workflow (`workflow_call`) for cleaner authoring. Risk: composability hides per-app details; not all teams find it worth it.
    - **`tofu plan` automation.** `infra/README.md` records `tofu apply` as laptop-only deliberately. But `tofu plan` as a PR check (read-only, no apply) could land cheaply — it shows the operator what an apply WOULD do before merge, catching drift early. Each tofu state would need a deployer SA with `roles/viewer` (heroes' deployer already has it; fast's does not).
    - **Cost rollup dashboard.** The standard label set (`app`, `service`, `environment`, `managed-by`) is applied per principle 4. Build a Cloud Billing-export-to-BigQuery dashboard that groups cost by `label:app` for headline + drills by `label:service` for breakdown. Probably <1 hour of work, gives visibility for every subsequent optimization decision.
    - **Pre-commit hooks coverage.** The `Detect hardcoded secrets` + `code-review-graph detect-changes` hooks land on every commit. Auditing what they catch + miss (e.g., FU-15's leaked DSN slipped through them initially) would tell the operator whether to extend coverage.
  - **Why broad-spec:** the operator's direction was "optimising cloud resources and CI/CD automation" — that's an umbrella request, not a list. Recording it here invites the operator to scope when picking up: "do all of these in one sprint" vs. "do the dashboard first then revisit" vs. "skip — it's working and the cost isn't material."
  - **Apply when:** post-CP21 (Spec 05 complete) so optimization isn't competing with feature work for context. Each scope candidate is independent; pick by ROI.
  - **Acceptance:** scoped per the operator's chosen items. The umbrella entry closes when the operator records "the candidates we wanted are done; the rest we deliberately defer."

- [x] **FU-25: Rotate GCP OAuth client secret (named in FU-19's rotation phase (c))**
  - **Sealed 2026-05-14 as no-op.** The audit pass ran three patterns against full history: (1) `git log --all -p -G 'GOCSPX-[A-Za-z0-9_-]{20,}'` (tight pattern for actual `GOCSPX-`-prefixed client secrets with a 20+ char suffix to filter documentation references) returned zero hits; (2) `git log --all -p -G 'GOCSPX-'` returned only two hits, both in `tasks/todo.md` documentation defining the audit pattern itself (commits `4fc602d` + `1ed8a85`); (3) `git log --all -p -G 'GOOGLE_CLIENT_SECRET\s*=\s*[^Y$]'` (excluding the `YOUR-OAUTH-CLIENT-SECRET` placeholder) returned five hits, all from heroes' early `.github/workflows/deploy.yml` where the `--set-secrets` flag references Secret Manager resource IDs (`GOOGLE_CLIENT_SECRET=coms-aha-heroes-google-client-secret:latest`) — i.e. secret-name references, not secret-value embeddings. **Conclusion: no actual GCP OAuth client secret value has ever appeared in git history.** No rotation is owed for scrub correctness; FU-19's `replacements.txt` does not need a `GOCSPX-` entry. The Secret Manager `aha-fast-google-client-secret` value remains unleaked.
  - **Surface:** FU-19's rotation phase names three credential buckets that need rotation before the history scrub becomes meaningful: (a) DB password — closed via Op-3 (FU-15), (b) Apps Script HMAC — closes via FU-18, (c) **GCP OAuth client secret** — currently the value behind Secret Manager's `aha-fast-google-client-secret`, used by fast's Google Calendar OAuth callback at `apps/fast/app/api/auth/google/route.ts` (T87 Step 6 verified the redirect URI registration). If the cleartext form leaked into git history at any point (audit phase of FU-19 will catalogue), the same rotation pattern that closed Op-3 applies here.
  - **Pre-flight audit:** `git log --all -p -G 'GOCSPX-'` (Google OAuth client secrets share the `GOCSPX-` prefix) returns the commits where any such literal appears. Working tree currently shows zero hits — `grep -rn 'GOCSPX-' apps/fast/ packages/ infra/` confirms — so the secret has only ever lived in Secret Manager + `.env` files outside the tree. **The audit is to confirm history is clean too.** If any commit embeds the literal (e.g., an early dev-fixture commit with a real client secret), rotation becomes load-bearing for FU-19's scrub phase.
  - **Rotation sequence (if audit surfaces hits):**
    1. Google Cloud Console → APIs & Services → Credentials → OAuth 2.0 Client (the one wired into fast's Calendar OAuth) → "Add Secret" → generate new → copy.
    2. `gcloud secrets versions add aha-fast-google-client-secret --data-file=<(echo -n "<NEW>") --project=fbi-dev-484410`. Cloud Run picks up the new version on next deploy (no service restart — secret resolves on cold start).
    3. Wait ~5 min for any in-flight OAuth sessions to complete on the old secret; then return to Google Cloud Console → delete the old secret. After this, the historical leak is unauthenticated.
  - **Apply when:** during FU-19's audit phase. If audit shows zero hits for `GOCSPX-` across `git log --all -p`, this FU closes immediately as "no leak found, rotation not needed for scrub correctness." If audit shows hits, rotate before the rewrite + force-push.
  - **Acceptance:** either (a) `git log --all -p -G 'GOCSPX-'` returns zero hits and FU-25 closes as no-op, or (b) the OAuth client secret rotates in Google Cloud Console + Secret Manager + a Cloud Run deploy verifies the new secret authenticates the next OAuth round-trip; the historical leak is unauthenticated; FU-25 closes.
  - **Related:** FU-19 (history scrub — this FU lives in FU-19's rotation phase (c)); FU-15 (the same pattern's (a) bucket, sealed via Op-3); FU-18 (the (b) bucket, retiring the Apps Script HMAC literal hardcoded in `apps/fast/lib/email.ts:16`).

- [x] **FU-24: Heroes carries the same `SELF_PUBLIC_URL` audience-mismatch crack fast just mended — IaC sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Surface:** discovered while closing CP18 on 2026-05-14. Portal-api's `apps/portal-api/src/services/webhook-dispatcher.ts:251` mints the OIDC token audience as `new URL(endpoint.url).origin`. For both heroes and fast, the registered `app_webhook_endpoints.url` is fronted through Firebase Hosting (`https://aha-coms.web.app/heroes/api/webhooks/portal` and `https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/webhooks/portal` respectively), so the audience portal mints is `https://aha-coms.web.app` in both cases. Fast's `SELF_PUBLIC_URL` was set to `https://aha-coms.web.app/fast` and rejected every inbound webhook with 401 until the operator window flipped it to the bare origin. Heroes' `SELF_PUBLIC_URL` is currently `https://coms-heroes-api-45tyczfska-et.a.run.app` (the Cloud Run URL, set when heroes' webhook URL was still the Cloud Run URL pre-single-origin); the same mismatch lurks but stays hidden because `app_webhook_endpoints` for heroes is `status='disabled'` (failure reason "Cloud Tasks retries exhausted", `failure_count=1`, `last_failure_at=2026-05-12`).
  - **Why this matters:** the next operator who re-enables heroes' webhook endpoint will see every inbound delivery 401 with the same audience-mismatch shape fast just mended. Fixing it ahead of time costs ~3 lines of `infra/heroes/cloud-run.tf` + one redeploy; fixing it after the re-enable means another round of operator triage on a webhook delivery that should "just work" from heroes' side.
  - **Recommended shape:** edit `infra/heroes/cloud-run.tf` so `SELF_PUBLIC_URL = var.heroes_public_origin` (or however the Firebase Hosting origin variable is named in heroes' IaC — likely the same `fast_public_origin` shape), drop any path-suffix construction. Bonus: add the same audience-anchored comment block fast now carries (`infra/fast/cloud-run.tf` post-CP18) so the lesson stays attached to the env var.
  - **Apply when:** before the next operator window that re-enables heroes' webhook endpoint. Or any quiet code-side session before then.
  - **Acceptance:** `gcloud run services describe coms-heroes-api --format=...` reports `SELF_PUBLIC_URL=https://aha-coms.web.app`. After heroes' endpoint is re-enabled (separate operator action), `coms-portal-cli smoketest heroes` returns `{"ok":true}` with each endpoint reporting `status=200`.
  - **Cross-reference:** the fast-side fix lands in the same commit that this finding is filed; see `infra/fast/cloud-run.tf`'s `SELF_PUBLIC_URL` block + the comment explaining the audience convention.
  - **What landed:** edited `infra/heroes/cloud-run.tf:217` so `SELF_PUBLIC_URL = var.heroes_public_origin` (the existing variable that already resolves to `https://aha-coms.web.app`) instead of the dead `var.heroes_api_public_url` it had used. Added an anchored comment block above the env declaration explaining `new URL(endpoint.url).origin` as portal's audience-mint rule + recording the failure mode so a future infra reader doesn't accidentally re-introduce the `coms-heroes-api-*.run.app` URL on the theory that "heroes-api lives there." Removed the orphaned `heroes_api_public_url` variable from `infra/heroes/variables.tf` (no remaining consumers post-edit; gcloud-run-deploy from `.github/workflows/deploy-heroes-api.yml` doesn't set `--update-env-vars`, so live env-var propagation needs either `tofu apply` against `infra/heroes/` or a manual `gcloud run services update`; both stay deferred until heroes' webhook is actually re-enabled).
  - **What stays for the operator window:** the live `SELF_PUBLIC_URL` on `coms-heroes-api` is still the legacy Cloud Run URL — the IaC change won't propagate without one of (a) `cd infra/heroes && tofu apply` or (b) `gcloud run services update coms-heroes-api --update-env-vars=SELF_PUBLIC_URL=https://aha-coms.web.app`. Neither is urgent (heroes' `app_webhook_endpoints.status='disabled'`), but either MUST land before the operator flips heroes' webhook status back to `'active'` — otherwise the first delivery 401s and re-triggers Cloud Tasks' retry exhaustion that put heroes in the disabled state to begin with.

- [x] **FU-23: `deploy-fast.yml`'s `[skip-db-push]` gate substring-tripped on body prose — sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Surface:** commit `e76bbd6` (T77 + T78, additive `PortalWebhookEvent` + `TaxonomyCache` schema) deployed green in 3m5s, but the `Apply Prisma schema (db push)` step was **skipped** with conclusion `skipped`. The commit's subject line did NOT carry the `[skip-db-push]` token (the convention's correct opt-out location). Root cause: the workflow's gate at `deploy-fast.yml:110` used `!contains(github.event.head_commit.message, '[skip-db-push]')` — a whole-message substring match — and the commit's body explained at one line why the token wasn't being used: *"The schema additions are additive, so no `[skip-db-push]` token —"*. That literal mention itself satisfied `contains()`, so the step skipped. Self-defeating narrative prose.
  - **What landed:** introduced a `Resolve db-push skip token` step BEFORE the existing `Apply Prisma schema (db push)` step. The new step reads only the first line of `${{ github.event.head_commit.message }}` via `head -n1`, greps it for the literal `[skip-db-push]`, and exposes a `skip` output (`true` / `false`). The downstream step's gate flipped from `!contains(github.event.head_commit.message, '[skip-db-push]')` to `steps.dbpush.outputs.skip != 'true'`. The inline comment on the `Apply Prisma schema (db push)` step now says *"at the end of the commit's SUBJECT LINE (not anywhere else in the message)"* so the next author doesn't repeat the same prose-trip. Same commit re-fired `Deploy — fast` via a one-line marker append to `apps/fast/README.md` so the `Apply Prisma schema (db push)` step finally got to run against fast's Cloud SQL.
  - **Why this matters:** GitHub Actions' `contains()` is a naive substring match across the full commit message. Any token mentioned in body prose (even when explaining its absence) will satisfy the check. The fix restricts the match to the subject line, which is where the convention has always placed the token (e.g., `Re-mark the corridor again [skip-db-push]`). Whole-message matches are a recipe for these traps.
  - **Cross-reference:** discovered while watching the post-T77+T78 deploy. The `[skip-db-push]` convention itself stays; only the matching scope tightens.

- [x] **FU-22: Teach `spec07-register-fast.ts` drift-detection-and-upsert (heroes FU-1 shape) — sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Surface:** `apps/portal-api/scripts/spec07-register-fast.ts` is idempotent on `slug='fast'` — when a row already exists with `status != 'deprecated'`, the script logs `[spec07-register-fast] FAST already registered (id=…, status=…); nothing to do.` and exits 0 without inspecting the row's contents. That shape is safe (no accidental overwrites) but cuts both ways: when the existing row holds stale values (different URL, broker_origin, service_account_email, health_check_url), the script can't fix it. The CP14 → CP20 operator window (2026-05-14) hit this in practice — fast's `app_registry` row carried legacy `aha-fast-app-45tyczfska-et.a.run.app` URLs from a pre-Spec-05 registration, and clicking the FAST card from portal's launcher sent the operator to the dead legacy run.app instead of `https://aha-coms.web.app/fast`. Resolved that session via direct SQL `UPDATE` on `app_registry` (+ `app_webhook_endpoints` for the webhook URL), but the script itself stayed unchanged.
  - **Prior art — heroes:** `apps/portal-api/scripts/spec07-register-heroes.ts` (or the equivalent register-heroes path) learned a drift-detection-and-upsert shape during FU-1 — when the existing row's values differ from the env-provided shape, the script computes a diff, prints it, and applies an UPDATE. Same idempotency guarantee (safe to re-run) plus the upsert semantics that fix drift instead of skipping it.
  - **Recommended shape:**
    1. After the `existing.length > 0 && existing[0].status !== 'deprecated'` early-return, replace the bare exit with a comparison block: fetch the full existing row (id + url + broker_origin + service_account_email + base_path + status + the webhook endpoint's url + the manifest's display_name + config_schema + taxonomies).
    2. Compute a diff against the env-provided shape (FAST_APP_URL, FAST_BROKER_ORIGIN, FAST_APP_SA, derived FAST_HEALTH_CHECK_URL = `${FAST_APP_URL}/api/health`, the constants `BASE_PATH` + `ADAPTER_TYPE` + `TRANSPORT_MODE` + `HANDOFF_MODE` + `APP_ROLES` + `CONFIG_SCHEMA` + `TAXONOMIES` + `SUBSCRIBED_EVENTS` + the derived webhook URL `${FAST_APP_URL}/api/webhooks/portal`).
    3. If no diff, log `[spec07-register-fast] FAST registered + in-sync (id=…); nothing to do.` and exit 0.
    4. If diff detected, log each diverging field with `[drift] <field>: <old> → <new>`, then apply `UPDATE` statements in a single transaction. Webhook endpoint row update wraps in the same transaction (always re-syncs the URL even though `status` stays whatever the operator set it to — never flip status here; that's T77's call).
  - **Why this matters:** the next operator window that re-runs the script (e.g., when fast's URL changes again, when a new field gets added to `app_registry`, when fast's runtime SA rotates) needs the script to fix drift, not skip it. Direct SQL UPDATE works but bypasses the script's own knowledge of which fields belong together — easy to forget the manifest sync or the webhook URL re-write. The drift-aware shape centralises that knowledge.
  - **Apply when:** before the next `app_registry`-touching operator window (most likely when T77 lands the webhook consumer and the `app_webhook_endpoints.status` flip from `disabled` to `active` lands — that's the natural moment to also re-verify the row's contents). Or any quiet code-side session before then.
  - **Acceptance:** `bun run --cwd apps/portal-api scripts/spec07-register-fast.ts` against the live `app_registry` (a) detects the row's current shape, (b) reports "in-sync" when no drift exists, (c) reports + applies fixes when drift is detected, (d) preserves the early-return for the `deprecated` status case (per the existing safeguard). Verified by running the script against a deliberately-drifted local copy of the row (e.g., reverting the URL to the legacy run.app and confirming the script catches + fixes it).
  - **Cross-reference:** the heroes equivalent script for the same shape; FU-1 (2026-05-12) recorded the heroes-side fix.
  - **What landed:** rewrote `apps/portal-api/scripts/spec07-register-fast.ts` to mirror `register-heroes.ts`'s shape line-for-line, adapted for fast's slightly different env-var surface. Key changes from the prior idempotent-skip-only shape: (1) the existing-row branch now fetches the four drift-prone fields (`url`, `healthCheckUrl`, `serviceAccountEmail`, `brokerOrigin`) plus the webhook endpoint's `url`, computes a per-field diff against the env-provided + derived shape, and either reports "already registered with matching values" + returns (clean) or logs each diverging field as `<field>: <old> → <new>` and applies UPDATE statements in the same transaction. (2) New optional env vars `FAST_WEBHOOK_URL` (defaults to `${FAST_APP_URL}/api/webhooks/portal` — backwards-compatible with the prior runbook) and `FAST_HEALTH_CHECK_URL` (defaults to the api origin of `FAST_WEBHOOK_URL` + `/api/health`) match heroes' override pattern. (3) `healthCheckUrl` now lands at INSERT time too — the prior insert didn't set it, which is why the CP14-CP20 operator window had to UPDATE it via raw SQL after the registration. (4) Webhook endpoint's `status` field is NEVER flipped on update — flipping `disabled` → `active` (or back) belongs alongside T77's consumer rollout and is recorded inline as a deliberate omission so a future reader doesn't add it. (5) New early-exit for the `status='deprecated'` case (preserved from the original safeguard, lifted to its own check so the drift-detect branch doesn't need to handle the deprecated edge case). The script's idempotent "exit 0 if matching values" path makes it safe to re-run from any operator window without producing duplicate rows or accidental updates. **Verified:** `bun --filter @coms-portal/portal-api typecheck` exits 0 (no new errors); a future dry-run against a deliberately-drifted local copy of the `app_registry` row would catch the drift via the diff block.

- [x] **FU-11: Fast's pre-existing typecheck errors — sealed 2026-05-13 after Phase 4 closed**
  - **Surface (pre-fix):** `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast typecheck` exited non-zero with 23 errors clustered in four families. The Prisma `InputJsonValue` cluster the original FU-11 entry called out (`lib/syncCommentReply.ts:14`) dissolved during Phase 3 — T63's auth-lib razing took `syncCommentReply.ts` with it, so the issue retired by attrition.
  - **What landed:** five-piece slice, one commit. (1) **Family 1 — regex `s` flag (TS1501, 9 errors across 5 files):** bumped `apps/fast/tsconfig.json` `target` from `ES2017` directly to `ES2022` (not the minimum-bump `ES2018` the original FU-11 note called out) — the rest of the monorepo's app-level packages already land on `ES2022` (heroes-web, heroes-api, sdk, heroes-shared, the React smoketest), and Next.js 15's Node 18+ floor makes the higher target free. Clears `ChannelMessageItem.tsx:570,574`, `ForwardToChannelModal.tsx:104,335`, `ConversationList.tsx:45,49`, `MessageThread.tsx:311,315`, `ChannelPane.tsx:775` in one line. (2) **Family 2 — RBAC narrowing (TS2367, 4 errors at `app/users/page.tsx:465,471,472,557`):** widened `UserRow.role` and the `formRole` `useState` generic from `'leader' | 'member'` to `'admin' | 'leader' | 'member'`. The runtime API already returns `'admin'` (it's the Master role); the type just didn't include it. (3) **Family 3 — `viewTicket.custom_fields` (TS18048 + TS2339, 8 errors at `app/nexus/page.tsx:1917–1979`):** added `assessment_edited_at?: string` to the inline `custom_fields` type (clears the two TS2339); wrapped the `.length > 0` guards in `(... ?? 0) > 0` and switched the two `.map` call chains to use `?.map` so the optional chain narrows cleanly (clears the six TS18048). (4) **Family 4 — one-offs:**
    - `ChannelMessageFeed.tsx:247` + `ChannelPane.tsx:736` (TS2741/TS2719): two local `Message` interfaces diverged when `ChannelMessageItem.tsx` required `updatedAt: string` but the feed + pane's local copies didn't. Added `updatedAt: string` to both, mirroring the consumer's shape.
    - `BottomNav.tsx:81` (TS2322): inferred element-literal `badgeKey: 'changelog'` widened to `string` because the array contained items without `badgeKey`. Wrapped the array literal in `(...] satisfies MoreItem[]).filter(...)` so each element type-checks against `MoreItem` before the `.filter` strips the `requireLeader` guard rows.
    - `EmojiPicker.tsx:98` (TS1117): `'🔥'` key appeared twice with identical values (line 60 + line 98). Dropped the second.
    - `MessagesIndex.tsx:428` (TS2322): `SectionMenuProps.anchorRef` was typed `React.RefObject<HTMLElement>`; React 19's `useRef` defaults always include `| null`. Widened the prop to `React.RefObject<HTMLElement | null>` to match.
  - **Verification:** `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast typecheck` → exit 0. `bun run --filter '*' typecheck` → all 12 packages green (portal-api, portal-web, heroes-api, heroes-web, fast, sdk, shared, ui-svelte, ui-react, account-widget-svelte, account-widget-react, heroes-shared + smoketest). `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` → green; all routes including the `ƒ Proxy (Middleware)` registration land cleanly. Stale `apps/fast/tsconfig.tsbuildinfo` deleted in the run because incremental compile cached the old `ES2017` view and kept resurrecting the TS1501 family even after the target bump.
  - **Why now (vs the original "after Phase 3" gate):** Phase 4 sealed in the same window CP14 closed. The surface that survived Phase 3's auth-lib razing is the surface that stays; deferring further only pushes T61's "every removal passes typecheck" claim further from a green CI signal. The cleanup was a one-pass touch.

### Phase 3: Better Auth removal — staged in 3 sub-phases

Spec ref: `docs/spec/05-fast-onboarding.md#phase-3-better-auth-removal--staged-per-open-question-4`. Decision: Open Question §4 Option B — three sub-phases ((a) loadFastAuthUser alongside Better Auth, (b) flip 127 `requireAuth()` call sites, (c) delete surfaces + Prisma migration). The 137 grep hits surveyed quantify the scope; the staged cadence makes a missed call site fail in (b) rather than after (c).

- [x] **T60: Sub-phase (a) — Author `lib/auth/load-fast-auth-user.ts` + add nullable `portal_sub` to User + backfill — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** CP13
  - **What:** Mirror `packages/heroes-shared/src/auth/user.ts`'s shape (170 lines, the canonical pattern). Read the portal `__session` cookie via Next.js's `cookies()` helper from `next/headers`; fetch `https://aha-coms.web.app/api/userinfo` with the cookie forwarded; introspect the response; upsert `User.portal_sub` keyed on the portal UUID; return the React/Next.js-shaped `AuthUser`. Next.js Server Components consume via a Server Component wrapper; API routes consume via a replacement helper that returns the same shape `requireAuth()` does today (smoothing the T61 flip). Add `portal_sub String? @unique` column to the Prisma `User` model (nullable). Backfill via a one-off script that joins on `email_normalized` against portal's `identity_users` table.
