Run the backfill in a dev-then-prod cycle; any user without a portal_sub becomes a deferral case (operator outreach) but doesn't block the migration as long as the population is small.
  - **Acceptance:** `loadFastAuthUser` exists and returns `AuthUser` for a valid `__session` cookie; throws `PortalSessionDeniedError` (or fast-equivalent) for invalid; `User.portal_sub` column added; backfill script run with output showing N rows updated / M rows still null; remaining nulls documented.
  - **Outcome:** authored as a 4-piece slice. (1) `apps/fast/lib/auth/load-fast-auth-user.ts` mirrors heroes-shared `loadHeroesAuthUser` line-by-line: `fetch(${portalOrigin}/api/userinfo)` with the forwarded `__session` cookie, 401-returns-null contract, `PortalSessionDeniedError` thrown when the `apps` claim lacks the `fast` slug, Prisma upsert keyed on `portal_sub`. Returns `{ user, appCatalog }` where `user` carries the nine fields fast call sites read (`id`, `portalSub`, `email`, `name`, `image`, `role`, `teamId`, `portalRole`, `apps`) — same shape T61 will flip the 137 `requireAuth`/`getServerSession`/`useAuth` hits to consume. Cookie reading deliberately stays in the caller (Next.js Server Components/Route Handlers) so the helper itself is server-runtime-agnostic and unit-testable; matches the heroes pattern where `hooks.server.ts` reads the cookie and passes the value in. (2) `apps/fast/prisma/schema.prisma` gains `portal_sub String? @unique` on the `User` model — nullable so existing rows survive the column add; field name kept flat (not `portalSub @map("portal_sub")`) so the Prisma client surface reads identically across the helper, backfill script, and T61 call sites. (3) `apps/fast/prisma/sql/0001_add_portal_sub.sql` records the auditable SQL the operator runs via Cloud SQL Auth Proxy (idempotent `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` + partial unique index) — fast uses `prisma db push` (not migrate) per package.json, so this file is the source-of-truth artefact for the change rather than a Prisma-tracked migration. (4) `apps/fast/scripts/backfill-portal-sub.ts` joins fast's `User.email` against a portal-exported CSV of `(email_normalized, identity_user_id)` pairs and updates each match's `portal_sub`. Cross-database friction (portal's DB has Drizzle, fast's has Prisma; both on the shared Cloud SQL instance but Postgres cross-database SQL is foreign-data-wrapper territory) resolved by the operator-runs-two-steps shape: psql `\copy` from portal first, then bun-run the script against fast. `--dry-run` flag prints the count without writing; unique-index conflicts (two fast users mapped to one portal_sub) surface per-row + don't abort the batch. Final output: `N updated, M still null` with the M emails listed for operator outreach.
  - **Verification in-session:** TDD red→green via `apps/fast/lib/auth/load-fast-auth-user.test.ts` — five bun:test cases covering (a) valid session + `fast` slug returns AuthUser with the upserted row, (b) 401 returns null, (c) valid session without `fast` slug throws `PortalSessionDeniedError`, (d) non-401 server error throws with the status code in the message, (e) `__session=<value>` cookie forwarded on the userinfo fetch. Prisma client mocked via `bun:test`'s `mock.module('@/lib/db', ...)`. Five passing tests; `bun test ./apps/fast/lib/auth/load-fast-auth-user.test.ts` from monorepo root runs in ~120ms. `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` green (Next.js prerenders all 22 routes incl. `/api/*` server-rendered surfaces). Workspace-wide `bun run --filter '*' typecheck` shows zero new errors — only the same FU-11 pre-existing set (regex `s` flag vs ES2017 target, `users/page.tsx` RBAC narrowing, `BottomNav.tsx` discriminated-union drift). `tsconfig.json` `exclude` extended to skip `scripts/` + `**/*.test.ts` so the bun-runtime files don't pull `@types/bun` into the Next.js tsserver pass — Next.js doesn't bundle either path, and adding `@types/bun` workspace-wide conflicts with Next's expected DOM lib shape.
  - **Operator runbook (executed 2026-05-13, prod-applied):** Discovered during the run: fast lives on its own Cloud SQL instance (`aha-fast-db-instance-cd5db712` at `34.101.176.36`, asia-southeast2) with `0.0.0.0/0` authorized — per-app isolation, contrary to the plan's earlier "shared instance" wording. Portal sits on `coms-aha-heroes-db` (`34.50.119.90`, same region, no public allowlist). Two-path access used: Cloud SQL Auth Proxy for portal (port 5433 → `coms-aha-heroes-db`), direct TCP for fast (`34.101.176.36:5432`, password from Secret Manager `aha-fast-db-url`). Steps applied: (1) `psql -f prisma/sql/0001_add_portal_sub.sql` against fast prod — `ALTER TABLE` + `CREATE INDEX` returned without error; column verified via `\d "user"` as `portal_sub character varying(255)` nullable. (2) `\copy (SELECT email_normalized, identity_user_id FROM identity_user_emails) TO /tmp/portal-emails.csv` against portal via proxy — 138 rows exported. (3) Dry-run backfill against fast: `Loaded 138 portal email rows. 13 fast users without portal_sub. 12 updated (dry run — no writes), 1 still null. Emails without a portal match: ahabot@system.local` — the one still-null is the system bot, which intentionally has no portal identity (it's the author-of-record for system messages, never signs in via loadFastAuthUser; the rationale is recorded in `lib/system-bot.ts`'s factory comment). (4) Real apply: same script without `--dry-run` — 12 updated, 1 still null (the system bot, as expected). (5) Verification: `SELECT COUNT(*), COUNT(portal_sub) FROM "user"` returned `total: 13, with_portal_sub: 12`. Backfill complete; the small fast user population (13 vs portal's 138) reflects that most portal-registered users haven't onboarded to fast yet — they'll auto-backfill on first signed-in hit via `loadFastAuthUser`'s upsert when Phase 4 lands. **T64's destructive apply deliberately stays deferred until after T70 deploys** — the current Better-Auth-shaped fast revision in prod still reads session/account/verification tables; dropping those before T70's loadFastAuthUser-only revision deploys would boot every active user and break sign-in for the Phase-4-window. Order: T65–T70 land → fast deploys with no Better Auth code → operator runs `prisma/sql/0002_drop_better_auth_tables.sql` → T64 PK promotion (separate window).

- [x] **T61: Sub-phase (b) — Flip all 127 `requireAuth()` call sites to `loadFastAuthUser` — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** T60
  - **What:** Grep `requireAuth\|getServerSession\|useAuth` across `app/`, `lib/`, `components/` — 137 hits surveyed. Each call site flips to the new helper. Same return shape; same authorization checks (`user.role === 'leader'` etc. stay — that's fast-internal RBAC, contract-orthogonal). The `lib/auth-context.tsx` `useAuth()` hook becomes a Server Component pattern (session lives server-side, not in client React state). `app/api/*/route.ts` routes call `loadFastAuthUser` directly at the top; client-side components that need user info either receive it as a prop from a Server Component parent or fetch their own subset via a new `/api/auth/me`-style route fast adds (fast-internal, doesn't touch portal-api).
  - **Acceptance:** `grep -rn "requireAuth\b\|getServerSession\b\|useAuth\b" apps/fast/app apps/fast/lib apps/fast/components` returns zero hits OUTSIDE the old auth lib files (which still exist in this sub-phase). Every `app/api/*/route.ts` calls `loadFastAuthUser` (or a Server Component pattern). The fast dev server still serves requests; `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` green.
  - **Outcome:** flipped as a 4-piece slice across 113 changed files. (1) New `apps/fast/lib/auth/require-fast-auth.ts` — server-side wrapper: reads `__session` via `cookies()` (next/headers), calls `loadFastAuthUser` with `process.env.PORTAL_ORIGIN` (defaults to `https://aha-coms.web.app`), catches `PortalSessionDeniedError` so denied-access surfaces as `null` instead of a thrown 500. Returns the exact `{ user }` shape Better Auth's `requireAuth()` returned (verified by the grep showing call sites only ever read `session.user.{id,email,name,image,role}` — never `session.session.*`). Mechanical-sweep-compatible by construction. (2) New `apps/fast/app/api/auth/me/route.ts` — JSON endpoint for the client-side `useAuth()` hook; returns `{ user, profile: { team_id, team_name, avatar_url } }` collapsing the two-round-trip (`authClient.getSession()` then `/api/profile`) shape the old auth-context held into one fetch. (3) Rewrote `apps/fast/lib/auth-context.tsx` — `useAuth()`'s external surface unchanged (same `{user, profile, isLeader, isMaster, loading, signOut}` shape, same field types), internal fetch swung from `authClient.getSession()` + `/api/profile` to a single `fetch('/api/auth/me')`. `handleSignOut` redirects to portal's sign-out endpoint (`window.location.assign(`${portalOrigin}/api/auth/sign-out?returnTo=${...}`)`) instead of `authClient.signOut()`; matches heroes' AccountWidget posture. (4) sed-swept 111 `requireAuth` server-side files + 1 `getServerSession` file → `requireFastAuth` (identifier-by-identifier substitution, no `\b` boundary tokens since BSD sed doesn't honour them — verified by post-sweep `grep -c "requireFastAuth"` = 114 files, `grep "requireAuth\b"` = 0). Imports rewritten from `@/lib/auth-server` to `@/lib/auth/require-fast-auth` in the same pass.
  - **What deliberately survives this sub-phase:** `apps/fast/lib/auth.ts` (Better Auth's `betterAuth({...})` config), `apps/fast/lib/auth-server.ts` (now an orphan — sweep renamed its internal `requireAuth` to `requireFastAuth`, no importers remain), `apps/fast/lib/auth-client.ts` (still serves the credential pages' `signIn` / `signUp` / `useSession`), `app/api/auth/[...all]/route.ts` (Better Auth catchall), the five credential routes (`/login`, `/register`, `/forgot-password`, `/activate`, `/complete`), and the `useSession()` consumers (7 files: orbit pages, profile page, activity-log, MyRequestView, LaterPane, ChannelPane). All retire in T62 + T63 + T64 — keeping them through sub-phase (b) means the dev server keeps serving requests today (the build's three `BetterAuthError: default secret` warnings are Better Auth's config-time complaints from those still-active surfaces; they print at build but don't fail the build, and the operator-side env carries the real `BETTER_AUTH_SECRET` in prod).
  - **Runtime caveat (operator-facing):** after T61, the loaded auth path runs through `loadFastAuthUser` → portal-api's `/api/userinfo`. That endpoint is only reachable when fast lives behind the same Firebase Hosting origin as portal-api — which Phase 4 (T65–T70) sets up. In current prod (fast at `<cloud-run>.run.app` with no Hosting rewrite), the new path fails at the network edge: `https://aha-coms.web.app/api/userinfo` returns 401 because the browser's `__session` cookie is for the `aha-coms.web.app` origin, not for the `*.run.app` origin fast served from. **This is intentional** — Phase 3's destructive cascade pre-stages for Phase 4's single-origin flip; reverting auth before T70 means rolling the whole CP14→CP15 corridor back. Operator should not re-deploy fast standalone until T70 lands; CP14 marker explicitly opens Phase 4 to keep the corridor moving forward.
  - **Verification in-session:** T60's five bun:test cases still pass (Prisma + fetch mocks isolated from the new wrapper). `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` green — 22 routes prerender (the three `BetterAuthError` lines are warnings from Better Auth's config-load path at build time, not errors; build still exits 0). `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast typecheck` shows zero new errors — only the pre-existing FU-11 set (regex `s` flag vs ES2017 target, `users/page.tsx` RBAC narrowing, `BottomNav.tsx` discriminated-union drift, `MessagesIndex.tsx` ref-type drift). `grep -rln "requireAuth\b\|getServerSession\b" apps/fast/{app,components,lib}` returns 0 hits outside `lib/auth-server.ts` (which lib still exports `requireFastAuth` and `getServerSession` as orphan functions awaiting T63's deletion). `grep -rln "useAuth\b" apps/fast/{app,components,lib}` still returns the 26-file consumer set, but its underlying impl now reads through `loadFastAuthUser` — same surface, new substrate.

- [x] **T62: Sub-phase (b cont.) — Delete the 5 credential routes — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** T61
  - **What:** Remove `apps/fast/app/{login,register,forgot-password,activate,complete}/` directories entirely. Public routes (`/request`, `/track`, `/api/employees`) stay — they're unauthenticated by design, separate from the credential-route surface. Any user landing on a previously-credential URL gets the eventual Next.js 404; Phase 4's middleware (T68) replaces this with a redirect-to-portal-sign-in shape.
  - **Acceptance:** the 5 directories don't exist; `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` green; the dev server returns 404 for `/login` etc.

Build verified green — the route list shrinks from 22 prerendered routes (T60 baseline) to 17, with `/login`, `/register`, `/forgot-password`, `/activate`, `/complete` no longer listed by Next.js's static-prerender summary. Twelve files still carry absolute string references to those paths (mostly auth-fallback redirects from orbit/profile/messaging pages that route unauthenticated callers to `/login`) — those produce 404s after this commit and are T68's middleware-redirect responsibility per the spec. Phase 4 (T65–T70) turns each of those into a redirect to portal's sign-in; until then the fast app's dev surface for auth-required pages will 404 on unauth, which is correct fail-loud behaviour during the Phase 3 cascade.

- [x] **T63: Sub-phase (c) — Delete the 4 auth lib files + proxy.ts — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** T62
  - **What:** Remove `apps/fast/lib/auth.ts`, `apps/fast/lib/auth-client.ts`, `apps/fast/lib/auth-server.ts`, `apps/fast/lib/auth-context.tsx`, and `apps/fast/proxy.ts`. None of these should have any remaining importers after T61–T62. Verify with grep; if any import survives, fix the consumer before deleting (likely a leftover in tests, scripts, or a less-common component).
  - **Acceptance:** none of the 5 files exist; `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` green; `grep -rn "from '.*auth/auth\|from '.*auth-client\|from '.*auth-server\|from '.*auth-context'" apps/fast/` returns zero hits.
  - **Outcome:** the four auth lib files retired in one window (`proxy.ts` already discarded in T56). The plan's own acceptance line — "None of these should have any remaining importers after T61–T62" — turned out under-scoped: 26 client files still imported `useAuth`/`AuthProvider` from `@/lib/auth-context`, 8 imported `useSession` from `@/lib/auth-client`, 5 imported `auth` from `@/lib/auth`. The fix took shape as a 4-piece slice. (1) New `apps/fast/lib/auth/use-auth.tsx` carries `AuthProvider` + `useAuth` (relocated, behaviour unchanged) **plus** a `useSession()` shim — `() => ({ data: { user } | null, isPending })` — that mirrors Better Auth's hook shape so the 8 `useSession` consumers swap import paths without rewriting `data.user.id` access. (2) Two sed sweeps: `from '@/lib/auth-context'` → `from '@/lib/auth/use-auth'` (26 files); `from '@/lib/auth-client'` → `from '@/lib/auth/use-auth'` (8 files). Post-sweep grep returns zero hits for both old paths. (3) Three credential-route surfaces deleted alongside the 5 page directories from T62: `app/api/auth/[...all]/route.ts` (Better Auth catchall), `app/api/auth/activate/route.ts` (used `auth.api.signUpEmail`), `app/api/auth/reset-password/route.ts` (used `hashPassword` from `better-auth/crypto`), `app/api/profile/password/route.ts` (used `auth.api.changePassword`). The `app/api/users/route.ts` POST — admin-creates-user — rewritten to return 410 Gone pointing operators at portal-side identity management; the route's auth-required surface kept (returns 403 to non-Master callers before the 410, so the error path mirrors the spec). The stale `auth` import in `app/api/profile/route.ts` removed (it was never called from the GET — sweep-induced cleanup). (4) `better-auth` removed from `apps/fast/package.json` dependencies; `bun install` confirms zero installs broken. Final state: `grep -rln "better-auth" apps/fast/{app,components,lib}` returns one hit — a doc comment in `lib/auth/load-fast-auth-user.ts` explaining the history. No runtime importer survives.
  - **What deliberately survives:** `app/api/auth/{approve,forgot-password,google,me,pending,register}` — these don't import the deleted lib files. `approve`/`pending` are admin operator surfaces over fast's own `accountStatus` field, contract-orthogonal. `forgot-password`/`register` generate tokens via Prisma + email — they don't use Better Auth's API surface; their portal-side replacement is a separate cleanup pass (likely an FU after CP14). `google` is the OAuth callback for Google Calendar (T67's scope). `me` is the new endpoint authored in T61. The build's prior three `BetterAuthError: default secret` config-load warnings are gone — Better Auth no longer initialises anywhere in the tree.

Phase 3 sub-phase (c) is sealed on the code-shape axis; T64 remains for the destructive Prisma migration (drop Session/Account/Verification + promote portal_sub to PK).

- [~] **T64: Sub-phase (c cont.) — Drop Session/Account/Verification models; destructive apply sealed 2026-05-14, PK promotion still deferred**
  - **Prerequisites:** T63 + every active user has non-null `portal_sub`
  - **What:** The destructive migration. Author a Prisma schema change that:
    1. Drops the `Session` model entirely.
    2. Drops the `Account` model entirely.
    3. Drops the `Verification` model entirely.
    4. Drops `User.emailVerified` column.
    5. Promotes `User.portal_sub` to the new primary key (or renames `User` → `fast_profiles` per integration contract §2's `<app>_profiles` convention — decide based on whether the cascading rename through Prisma relations is worth the cleaner naming). The 38 product models that reference `User.id` cascade through the rename.
    Run `prisma db push` against dev → staging → prod in sequence. Deploy ordering is **deploy-first-then-migrate** (the destructive shape T46's `DROP TABLE user_config_cache` followed) — the new fast revision must NOT touch the dropped tables before the migration runs. Workflow comment (T81 authors the deploy-fast.yml) names the destructive-migration caveat.
  - **Acceptance:** Prisma schema has no `Session`/`Account`/`Verification` models; `User.emailVerified` gone; primary key is `portal_sub` (or `User` renamed to `fast_profiles` with `portal_sub` as PK). `prisma db push` applies cleanly against the canonical environments. The 38 product models' foreign keys still resolve.
  - **Outcome (code-side, complete):** schema.prisma drops the three Better Auth models (`Session`, `Account`, `Verification`), removes the corresponding `sessions Session[]` + `accounts Account[]` relations on `User`, and drops `User.emailVerified Boolean` from the column list. The `BETTER AUTH REQUIRED MODELS` banner replaced by `IDENTITY / USER (portal-bridged via portal_sub since Phase 3 / T64)`. Four writers of `emailVerified` cleaned in the same window: (a) `lib/auth/load-fast-auth-user.ts`'s upsert no longer sets the field on create; (b) `lib/system-bot.ts`'s system-bot factory drops the line + retitles the comment to reflect the bot's `accountStatus='active'` is what keeps it visible to audit/lookup queries (the bot has no portal_sub and never resolves via loadFastAuthUser — it's the author-of-record for system messages); (c) `app/api/users/route.ts`'s GET list maps `email_confirmed_at` off `accountStatus === 'active'` instead of `emailVerified`; (d) `app/api/users/[id]/confirm/route.ts`'s admin-confirm action flips `accountStatus` to `'active'` (the user-facing intent — "approve this pending account" — unchanged). Auditable destructive SQL lives at `apps/fast/prisma/sql/0002_drop_better_auth_tables.sql` — `DROP TABLE IF EXISTS session/account/verification CASCADE` + `ALTER TABLE user DROP COLUMN IF EXISTS emailVerified`. `bun run db:generate` emits the client cleanly; `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` green; T60's five tests still pass.
  - **Outcome (operator-window, deferred):** the actual `psql -f 0002_drop_better_auth_tables.sql` apply against prod waits on (a) T60's backfill completion — every active user has a non-null `portal_sub` so the next sub-step's PK promotion has no NULL rows to choke on, and (b) the new fast revision deploying first so no code emits queries against the to-be-dropped tables. The deploy ordering follows the destructive-migration rule recorded in plan.md's standing principles (per T46's `DROP TABLE user_config_cache` history). PK promotion (renaming `User.id` → `portal_sub` or renaming `User` → `fast_profiles`) is a separate operator-only step that cascades through 38 product-model FK relations — non-trivial, intentionally not bundled with this commit so the operator can stage it independently. Until PK promotion lands, `User.id` keeps the Better-Auth-issued string id values, `portal_sub` carries the portal UUID, and `loadFastAuthUser` continues upserting against `portal_sub`'s unique index. Task status: `[~]` reflects the code-side seal + operator deferral; promotes to `[x]` once the operator confirms the SQL applied + PK promotion landed.

- [~] **CHECKPOINT 14 — DESTRUCTIVE APPLY SEALED 2026-05-14; PK promotion deferred**: Fast has no Better Auth surfaces. Every auth path runs through `loadFastAuthUser`. The three Better-Auth tables (`session` 70 rows, `account` 12 rows, `verification` 0 rows) dropped; `User.emailVerified` column (13 non-null) dropped via `apps/fast/prisma/sql/0002_drop_better_auth_tables.sql` applied through Cloud SQL Auth Proxy. `to_regclass()` post-apply returns NULL for all three table names; `information_schema.columns` shows zero rows for `user.emailVerified`. **What's still owed for full CP14**: `User.id` promotion to `portal_sub` cascading through 38 product-model FK relations (or `User` → `fast_profiles` rename per integration contract §2). That promotion is intentionally **not bundled** with the destructive drop because the FK cascade is non-trivial and deserves its own commit + window. Until promotion lands, `User.id` keeps the Better-Auth-issued string id values and `loadFastAuthUser` continues upserting against `portal_sub`'s unique constraint. After CP14 closes fully (PK promotion), Phase 4 (single-origin /fast/) closes. **Operator runbook reference:** step 5 of [`apps/fast/docs/runbook-cp14-cp20-window.md`](../apps/fast/docs/runbook-cp14-cp20-window.md) (destructive apply step is sealed; PK promotion stays open).
  - **Status (2026-05-13):** the code-side cascade T60–T64 sealed in five commits on 2026-05-13; Phase 4 (T65, T66, T68, T69) followed on the same day with the basePath flip + path sweep + middleware + firebase.json rewrite, so the **code-side prerequisites for crossing CP14 are met**. CP14 itself stays `[ ]` until the operator window applies the deferred destructive SQL (`apps/fast/prisma/sql/0002_drop_better_auth_tables.sql`) against fast's Cloud SQL instance. The ordering recorded in T60's outcome stands: T65–T70 land → fast's new revision deploys with no Better-Auth-reading code → operator runs the drop SQL → operator decides on PK promotion (`User.id` rename to `portal_sub` cascading through 38 FK relations, or `User` → `fast_profiles` per integration contract §2). T70's runtime verification additionally waits on T81 (`deploy-fast.yml`) before the corridor can be walked end-to-end. CP14's three structural predicates remain: (1) every auth path runs through `loadFastAuthUser` ✓ (T61); (2) no `Session`/`Account`/`Verification` model declarations remain ✓ (T64 code-side); (3) `User` PK promotion to `portal_sub` ⟂ pending operator. Until the destructive SQL lands, fast's prod database still carries the three Better Auth tables as orphaned bytes — no code reads them, but the rows remain until the operator's `psql -f 0002_drop_better_auth_tables.sql` clears them.

### Phase 4: Single-origin migration (mount fast at /fast/)

Spec ref: `docs/spec/05-fast-onboarding.md#phase-4-single-origin-migration-mount-fast-at-fast`. Mirrors heroes T24–T29 + portal-web FU-10, adapted for Next.js's `basePath` config. The risk table flags the absolute-path sweep at High.

- [x] **T65: Configure `basePath: '/fast'` in apps/fast/next.config.ts + `assetPrefix` — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** CP14
  - **What:** Edit `next.config.ts` to set `basePath: '/fast'` and `assetPrefix: '/fast'` so chunk loading honours the prefix. Verify the dev server now serves at `/fast/*` paths.
  - **Acceptance:** `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast dev` serves the dashboard at `/fast/` rather than `/`; assets load from `/fast/_next/*`.
  - **Outcome:** `apps/fast/next.config.ts` gains `basePath: '/fast'` + `assetPrefix: '/fast'`. The build summary lists `┌ ○ /` as the dashboard route (Next.js renders basePath at serve time, so the route table reports app-router-relative paths); the served URL is `/fast/`. The pre-existing `app/fast/page.tsx` (a stray child route that pre-dated basePath) was consolidated into `app/page.tsx` so the post-basePath URL is the clean `/fast/` rather than the doubled `/fast/fast`. The redirect-only `app/page.tsx` (whose sole job was `redirect('/fast')`) retires in the same move — basePath now does the routing the explicit redirect used to. `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` green; assets are emitted under `_next/static/*` and Next.js auto-prefixes them with `/fast` at runtime per `assetPrefix`. The 16 prerendered route slots include `/`, `/orbit`, `/tasks`, `/track`, `/request`, `/users` — five fewer than T60's 22 because T62 deleted the five credential routes and T65 collapsed `/fast` → `/`.

- [x] **T66: Sweep absolute paths through basePath — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** T65
  - **What:** Next.js auto-prefixes `<Link href="/...">`, `router.push('/...')`, and `redirect('/...')` when basePath is set, but NOT `<a href>`, `<img src>`, or `fetch('/api/...')` (the latter is a browser API the framework can't intercept). Audit the three classes plus the carry-overs from T62's deletion of `/login`/`/register`/etc., decide per-site whether the absolute path needs explicit prefixing, conversion to a cross-app `<a>`, or replacement with portal sign-in.
  - **Acceptance:** all greps return zero unreviewed hits; navigation within fast works at the new base path; fast's own API routes are reachable from the client.
  - **Outcome:** the sweep landed in five strokes. **(1) 254 client-side `fetch('/api/...')` / `fetch(\`/api/...\`)` call sites** rewritten to `fetch('/fast/api/...')` / `fetch(\`/fast/api/...\`)` via two sed sweeps (single-quote + backtick variants; no double-quote variants in the tree). All 254 sites are in `'use client'` files; no server-side route handler issues absolute fetches (`grep --include=route.ts` returned zero hits). The one cross-app fetch — `lib/auth/load-fast-auth-user.ts`'s `${portalOrigin}/api/userinfo` — uses an explicit origin prefix and isn't matched by the sweep. **(2) 8 page-level `router.push('/login')` sites** rewritten to `window.location.href = '/portal?app=fast'`. These were the auth-fallback escapes T62 marked as middleware's responsibility; the hard-navigation form bypasses Next.js's auto-prefixing (which would have produced `/fast/portal`, a 404) and lets Firebase Hosting route `/portal/**` to `coms-portal-web` directly. **(3) 2 `<Link href="/login">` sites** (`app/track/page.tsx` public-page CTA + `components/layout/TopNav.tsx` unauthed dropdown) converted to plain `<a href="/portal?app=fast">` for the same cross-app-navigation reason. **(4) 3 `<img src="/aha-logo.png">` sites** in track + request + TopNav rewritten to `<img src="/fast/aha-logo.png">` — raw `<img>` tags don't go through Next.js's basePath machinery; the asset moves with the app. **(5) 2 server-side absolute-URL emitters** updated: `app/api/auth/google/callback/route.ts`'s three `NextResponse.redirect(${appUrl}/tasks?...)` callers now build `${appUrl}/fast/tasks?...` URLs (and the fallback origin moved from the bare Cloud Run URL to `https://aha-coms.web.app`); `app/api/slack/notify/route.ts`'s outgoing Slack-button URL gains the `/fast` prefix. All five sweeps verified by a final grep round that returned zero hits across `href="/login"`, `router.push('/login')`, `href="/fast"` (the bare literal), `fetch('/api/`, `redirect('/fast')`, and `<img src="/[non-fast-prefix]"`. `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` stays green. The cleanest residue: in-fast `<Link href="/...">` and `router.push('/...')` calls survive unchanged because Next.js's framework primitives auto-prefix at serve time — no helper wrapper required.

- [x] **T67: Register Google Calendar OAuth redirect URI for /fast/ in Google Cloud Console — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** T66, **operator-only** (Google Cloud Console UI)
  - **What:** Add `https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/auth/google/callback` to the OAuth 2.0 client's authorized redirect URIs in Google Cloud Console. **Keep the old URI registered through one rollback window** — if the post-Phase-4 deploy needs reverting, the old callback still works. Update `apps/fast/.env.example` to document the new `GOOGLE_REDIRECT_URI`; operator updates the Cloud Run env var separately.
  - **Acceptance:** Google Cloud Console shows both old + new redirect URIs registered; `.env.example` updated. Acceptance is operator-confirmed; the task body records the screenshot or list output as proof.
  - **Outcome (code-side, complete):** `apps/fast/.env.example` authored from scratch (fast had no env template in the tree — the only prior documentation was `process.env.*` references scattered through 17 source files). The file inventories the 17 env vars `grep -rohE 'process\.env\.[A-Z_]+' app components lib | sort -u` surfaced, documents the basePath constraint each carries (notably `GOOGLE_REDIRECT_URI=https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/auth/google/callback`), and names the rollback-window expectation so a future operator running the GCC step doesn't unregister the old URI by mistake. The OAuth callback path itself — `app/api/auth/google/callback/route.ts` — is unchanged at the source level (the route still lives at `app/api/auth/google/callback`); Next.js's basePath maps it to `/fast/api/auth/google/callback` at serve time without a source-file move. T66's same-session work mended the three internal redirect destinations the callback emits (the gcal-error/success redirects) so they land on `/fast/tasks?gcal=...` rather than the bare `/tasks?...` that would have routed to portal-web post-Phase-4.
  - **Outcome (operator action, complete 2026-05-13):** operator opened the "AHA Fast" OAuth 2.0 Client in Google Cloud Console (project `fbi-dev-484410` → APIs & Services → Credentials) and added `https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/auth/google/callback` to the Authorized redirect URIs list. The pre-existing Cloud Run-hosted URI (`https://aha-fast-app-908739514002.asia-southeast2.run.app/api/auth/google/callback`) stays registered through one rollback window — until the post-T70 revision has served at least one real OAuth round-trip successfully, after which the old URI retires in a separate operator visit. Acceptance criteria (`GCC shows both URIs registered` + `.env.example updated`) both met, so T67 promotes to `[x]`. The orthogonal Cloud Run env-var update (`GOOGLE_REDIRECT_URI` on the live `coms-fast-web` service) lives downstream of T80's `infra/fast/cloud-run.tf` shape — it will land on the same operator window T81's deploy workflow runs.

- [x] **T68: Author `apps/fast/middleware.ts` — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** T66
  - **What:** Next.js middleware at the edge: let the public allowlist through, check `__session` cookie presence on the rest, redirect unauthed callers to portal sign-in.
  - **Acceptance:** unauthed request to a fast page redirects to portal sign-in with proper query params; unauthed request to a public page renders normally; the middleware doesn't introduce a per-request DB or HTTP roundtrip (it only reads cookie presence).
  - **Outcome:** `apps/fast/middleware.ts` authored with the PUBLIC_PATH_PREFIXES list pulled from the actual route shape (`/request`, `/track`, `/api/employees` from the spec; plus `/api/auth/google/callback` so the OAuth round-trip survives, `/api/webhooks` so T77's portal webhook consumer lands on a public surface, `/api/cron` for the routine-scheduler that pre-exists in the tree, `/api/health` so the Cloud Run + portal probe T79 authors lands public, `/api/heartbeat` because the page-level guard already enforces auth and a middleware-side redirect would just produce a 401 path the JS bundle can't read). Path matching runs against `req.nextUrl.pathname`, which Next.js strips of the `/fast` prefix in middleware context — the allowlist stays basePath-agnostic. Two failure shapes: API callers under `/api/*` get a `401 { error: 'Unauthorized' }` JSON response (a redirect chain to portal HTML would just confuse a JSON consumer); page callers get `NextResponse.redirect('https://aha-coms.web.app/portal?app=fast&redirect_to=<encoded-original-path>')` with the original-path encoding constructed as `/fast${pathname}` so portal-side post-sign-in routing lands the user back where they were. The matcher config skips `_next/static`, `_next/image`, `favicon.ico`, `manifest.webmanifest`, and any `.png`/`.svg` asset so the cookie check doesn't fire on every static-asset hit. The `proxy.ts` that T56 discarded is now structurally replaced. `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` green; the build summary reports `ƒ Proxy (Middleware)` confirming registration.

- [x] **T69: Update firebase.json — add `/fast/api/**` + `/fast` + `/fast/**` rewrites — sealed 2026-05-13**
  - **Prerequisites:** T65, T68
  - **What:** `firebase.json` gains three rewrites (analogous to heroes' triple): `/fast/api/**` → `coms-fast-web` (most specific), then `/fast` (bare, mirrors how `/heroes` and `/portal` carry their own root rewrite), then `/fast/**` (catch-all for sub-paths). All three target the single Cloud Run service (Open Question §3 Option A — fast's API and pages share one Next.js runtime). `scripts/verify-firebase-json.mjs` updated to assert the new triple in the right precedence order between heroes and `/api/**`. The redirect block doesn't change (FU-10's `/ → /portal` 301 stays). The fallback `**` → `coms-portal-web` stays as the catch-all for anything unmatched.
  - **Acceptance:** `bun scripts/verify-firebase-json.mjs` passes with the updated expectations.
  - **Outcome:** the rewrite triple lands at indexes 3, 4, 5 of the rewrites array (after heroes' triple, before `/api/**`). The verifier's `expected` array grows to 10 entries (was 7); `bun scripts/verify-firebase-json.mjs` returns `OK — site, rewrite ordering, and Cloud Run targets all match the contract`. The Cloud Run service `coms-fast-web` referenced by the rewrites doesn't exist yet — T80 (infra/fast/) authors the Tofu module that creates it. Firebase will tolerate the rewrite pointing at a not-yet-existing service (the routing only resolves at request time), but a deploy attempted before T80 + T81 land will 502 on `/fast/*` until the service is up.

T70's corridor is live + walkable.

### Phase 6: Chrome mounting in fast

Spec ref: `docs/spec/05-fast-onboarding.md#phase-6-chrome-mounting`. Replace fast's local AppShell/Sidebar/Header with the React chrome packages CP12 produced. The brand mark renders into the `brand` slot; theme tokens flow through `@coms-portal/design-tokens/css`.

- [x] **T72 + T73: Hybrid chrome mount — ServiceBar above fast's existing TopNav — sealed 2026-05-14 (operator-verified + cleaned)**
  - **Prerequisites:** CP15 (code-side) + CP12
  - **What (revised from plan body):** the original framing — "delete `components/AppShell.tsx` + `components/layout/Sidebar.tsx` + `components/layout/Header.tsx`" — didn't survive contact with fast's tree. AppShell isn't pure chrome: it orchestrates app-wide modals (`DirectAssignModal`), the app-wide profile panel (`UserProfilePanel`), the Breadcrumb, the layout reflow logic (sidebar widening + profile-pane right-pad), and the public-route bypass (`/request`, `/track`). TopNav.tsx (657 lines) carries the in-app module tabs (Fast / Request Form / User Control Panel) with hover-revealed sub-items, the notification system (EventSource real-time stream, All/DMs tabs, mark-read, clear, toast popups for high-signal events), the theme toggle, and the profile menu. Sidebar.tsx (458 lines) is per-module contextual nav (each module gets its own section list). BottomNav.tsx (227 lines) carries badge-polling + a slide-up "More" sheet. None of these are platform-chrome primitives — they're fast-internal UX surfaces the React chrome packages (`ServiceBar`, `Sidebar`, `MobileTopBar`, `MobileBottomNav`, `SlideOverNav`) don't replicate. **Hybrid mount adopted instead:** add `ServiceBar` at the very top of fast's shell as the cross-app cookie crumb (portal / heroes / fast), keep fast's TopNav + Sidebar + BottomNav unchanged. ServiceBar is mobile-hidden by design (`hidden md:flex`), so the mobile chrome stays identical; on desktop, fast's TopNav shifts down 36px (`sticky top-0 md:top-9`) to make room for the 36px-tall ServiceBar above it.
  - **Acceptance:** ServiceBar visible on desktop above TopNav; theme toggle in ServiceBar's right slot wires to fast's `useTheme()`; no visual regression on mobile; `bun --filter '@coms-portal/fast' typecheck` + `build` green; all 12 workspace packages typecheck green.
  - **Outcome:** four files changed in one commit. (1) `apps/fast/package.json` gains three workspace deps: `@coms-portal/ui-react`, `@coms-portal/account-widget-react`, `@coms-portal/design-tokens`. (2) `apps/fast/app/globals.css` adds three `@import` lines after the existing Tailwind import — design-tokens for the brand palette (`--color-deep-navy`, `--color-primary-dark`, `--color-primary-light`) ServiceBar's gradient + text classes require, ui-react/styles.css for the Tailwind v4 `@source` directive that scans the chrome components' class strings (Tailwind v4's auto-discovery skips node_modules), and account-widget-react/styles.css for the same `@source` shape — fast's own `:root` + `.dark` blocks immediately below the imports override design-tokens' semantic surfaces (`--background`, `--foreground`, `--card`, ...) so the visual feel stays fast-native. Four chrome-contract helper classes (`.sidebar-link-active`, `.bnav-active`, `.section-label`, `.tap-active`) appended at the end of globals.css per the smoketest's template — mirrors `packages/ui-react/examples/smoketest/src/app/globals.css`. (3) `apps/fast/components/layout/SuiteServiceBar.tsx` authored as a thin client-component wrapper — imports `ServiceBar` from `@coms-portal/ui-react/chrome`, defines a static three-entry `SUITE_SERVICES` array (portal / heroes / fast), wires `theme` + `onToggleTheme` from fast's `useTheme()`. The static services-list shape is the **right call for now**: T47 Finding 5's hub-knowledge-in-`/api/userinfo` lesson means fast doesn't prepend portal; portal is already in `appCatalog` from the launcher response; but until T74 wires the dynamic catalog, a static list of the three known apps gives the user the cross-app navigation surface without waiting on a separate session. A code comment names T74 as the lift point. **AccountWidget mount deliberately deferred** to T74 — fast's TopNav already carries a profile menu with fast-specific destinations (Profile Settings, Changelog), and adding an AccountWidget avatar to ServiceBar's right slot would put two profile entry points on desktop. T74's window can deduplicate the two paths against the live appCatalog. (4) `apps/fast/components/AppShell.tsx` adds the import + mounts `<SuiteServiceBar />` above the existing `<TopNav />`. (5) `apps/fast/components/layout/TopNav.tsx` shifts from `sticky top-0` to `sticky top-0 md:top-9` so the 64px-tall TopNav sits below the 36px-tall ServiceBar on desktop; on mobile (`< md`) ServiceBar is invisible and TopNav stays at `top-0` unchanged. **Verification:** `bun install` resolves the three new workspace deps cleanly; `bun --filter '@coms-portal/fast' typecheck` green; `bun --filter '@coms-portal/fast' build` green (route count + middleware registration unchanged from pre-mount); `bun run --filter '*' typecheck` green across all 12 packages. **What stays for T74 + T75:** T74 wires `data.appCatalog` from `/api/userinfo` so SUITE_SERVICES becomes dynamic (and a new app onboarding surfaces in fast's ServiceBar without code change), and lifts AccountWidget into the ServiceBar's `right` slot — same window can decide whether fast's TopNav profile menu collapses into AccountWidget or stays as a fast-specific surface. T75 captures the desktop+mobile+light+dark screenshot grid against heroes' T54 baseline; the **hybrid mount's visual parity claim is weaker than the original plan** — fast keeps its in-app navigation shape (top tabs vs heroes' sidebar) — and T75's outcome should record where parity is intentional vs. accidental divergence. Status `[~]` because acceptance lists "visual parity check against heroes" which is operator-led; promotes to `[x]` after T75 produces the screenshot grid.

- [x] **T74: Wire `data.appCatalog` from /api/userinfo — sealed 2026-05-14 (operator-verified)**
  - **Prerequisites:** T73
  - **What:** Fast's Server Component (or root layout) calls `loadFastAuthUser` (T60) and projects the response's `apps` array into the chrome's `services` prop + the AccountWidget's `appSwitcher` prop. T47 Finding 5's lesson stands — the portal-hub prepend lives in `apps/portal-api/src/routes/userinfo.ts`, NOT in fast's layout. Fast reads `data.appCatalog` and iterates; no special-casing for portal.

  - **Outcome:** four files changed in one commit (along with the prior T72/T73 chunk's SuiteServiceBar surface). The shape took the `useAuth` path rather than a Server Component layout split — fast's auth-context already fetches `/fast/api/auth/me` client-side, so plumbing the appCatalog through that round-trip keeps the data flow flat. (1) `apps/fast/lib/auth/require-fast-auth.ts` extends `FastSession` to carry both `user` and `appCatalog` — the helper already had `result.appCatalog` from `loadFastAuthUser` and was discarding it. (2) `apps/fast/app/api/auth/me/route.ts` includes `appCatalog: session.appCatalog` in its 200 response; the JSDoc preamble names T74 explicitly. (3) `apps/fast/lib/auth/use-auth.tsx` gains an `AppCatalogEntry` exported type + an `appCatalog: readonly AppCatalogEntry[]` field on the context — fetchSession now sets it from the response payload alongside the existing user/profile setters. The `UserProfile` interface also gains `portalRole: string` + `apps: readonly string[]` (the two AuthUser fields the AccountWidget needs that the legacy useAuth was discarding). (4) `apps/fast/components/layout/SuiteServiceBar.tsx` swaps the static SUITE_SERVICES array for a dynamic projection: when `appCatalog.length > 0`, `services` derives from `appCatalog.map(...)` and `appSwitcher` derives from the same; when empty (pre-auth or first paint), the static three-entry fallback keeps the strip rendered honestly. AccountWidget mounts into ServiceBar's `right` slot with `currentApp="fast"`, the portal origin from `NEXT_PUBLIC_PORTAL_ORIGIN` (falls back to `https://aha-coms.web.app`), `user` projected from `useAuth`'s profile (name + email + portalRole + apps), and `appSwitcher` from the same dynamic catalog. Sign-out flows through AccountWidget's own `signOut.ts` helper (POST to portal's `/api/auth/sign-out` then redirect to the post-logout destination) — duplicates fast's existing `useAuth().signOut` path, but the two are equivalent and AccountWidget's button is the cleaner surface on the cross-app strip. **TopNav's in-app profile menu is deliberately kept** — it carries fast-specific destinations (Profile Settings, Changelog) that AccountWidget doesn't replicate, and removing it forces those surfaces into the cross-app launcher where they don't structurally belong. The two-avatar visual artifact on desktop is documented as intentional in the SuiteServiceBar comment; T75's parity review decides whether the in-app profile menu can collapse into AccountWidget via a follow-up cleanup. **Verification:** `bun --filter '@coms-portal/fast' typecheck` green; `bun --filter '@coms-portal/fast' build` green; `bun test apps/fast/lib/auth/load-fast-auth-user.test.ts apps/fast/app/api/health/route.test.ts` 8/8 pass (5 from T60 + 3 from T79; the appCatalog wiring didn't touch the loadFastAuthUser shape it was already returning). **What stays for T75:** the live capture — sign in to fast on a feature-branch deploy, screenshot the four breakpoint+theme combos (desktop+mobile × light+dark), compare against heroes' T54 baseline. Status `[~]` because acceptance's "appCatalog is the source of truth in prod" needs an authenticated walk against `aha-coms.web.app/fast/*` (operator-led); promotes to `[x]` once the operator confirms portal appears first in both the ServiceBar tab strip + the AccountWidget launcher dropdown.

- [x] **T76: Update `app_registry` URLs to single-origin shape — sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Prerequisites:** CP17
  - **What:** Run the existing `apps/portal-api/scripts/spec07-register-fast.ts` with the new single-origin URLs: `FAST_APP_URL=https://aha-coms.web.app/fast`, `FAST_WEBHOOK_URL=https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/webhooks/portal`, `FAST_HEALTH_CHECK_URL=https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/health`, `FAST_APP_SA=coms-fast-web-sa@fbi-dev-484410.iam.gserviceaccount.com`, `FAST_BROKER_ORIGIN=https://aha-coms.web.app`, `FAST_WEBHOOK_HMAC=$(gcloud secrets versions access latest --secret=aha-fast-broker-signing-secret 2>/dev/null || echo dev-fast-hmac)`. The script doesn't update existing rows; the operator window resolved via direct SQL `UPDATE`. (a) Pre-state: `url='https://aha-fast-app-45tyczfska-et.a.run.app'`, `broker_origin='https://coms-portal-app-45tyczfska-et.a.run.app'`, `service_account_email='aha-fast-run-sa@…'`, `health_check_url=NULL`; webhook `url='https://aha-fast-app-…/api/webhooks/portal'`. (b) Post-state: `url='https://aha-coms.web.app/fast'`, `broker_origin='https://aha-coms.web.app'`, `service_account_email='coms-fast-web-sa@fbi-dev-484410.iam.gserviceaccount.com'`, `health_check_url='https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/health'`; webhook `url='https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/webhooks/portal'` (status stays `disabled` until T77 lands). - [x] **T77: Author fast's webhook consumer at `app/api/webhooks/portal/route.ts` — sealed 2026-05-14 (code-side)**
  - **Prerequisites:** T76
  - **What:** Author the Next.js Route Handler that receives portal-issued webhooks at `POST /fast/api/webhooks/portal`. Verify inbound requests via Google ID-token validation against `PORTAL_SERVICE_ACCOUNT_EMAIL` (the same pattern heroes uses at `apps/heroes-api/src/routes/portal-webhooks.ts`). Subscribed events: `user.provisioned`, `user.updated`, `employment.updated`, `user.offboarded`, `taxonomy.upserted`, `taxonomy.deleted`. Plus fast-specific `app_config.updated` if fast actually reads any app_config (the `role` claim is likely the only one). Idempotent on `event_id` via the `portal_webhook_events` dedup table (fast adds this table via a Prisma migration in the same change). The handlers update fast's `User` (or `fast_profiles`) per integration contract §11.
  - **Acceptance:** `POST /fast/api/webhooks/portal` returns 200 for a properly-signed test event; the dedup table prevents double-processing; a `user.provisioned` event creates a `User` row in fast's DB; `user.offboarded` marks the row inactive (or whatever fast's offboarding semantics dictate).
  - **Outcome:** authored as a 12-piece slice mirroring heroes' shape adapted for Next.js Route Handler + Prisma. (1) Prisma schema gains the `PortalWebhookEvent` model (eventId PK, receivedAt default-now) under a new "PORTAL BRIDGE" section; `prisma db push` applies additively on next deploy. (2) `apps/fast/lib/portal/oidc.ts` — module-level `OAuth2Client` singleton + `verifyGoogleIdToken({idToken, expectedAudience, expectedSAEmail})` that throws on signature / expiry / unverified-email / SA-mismatch, mirrors `apps/heroes-api/src/lib/oidc.ts`. (3) `apps/fast/lib/portal/unwrap-envelope.ts` — pure helper that JSON-parses the inbound body, returns a discriminated `{ok, payload, appSlug}` vs. `{ok:false, reason:'malformed_json'|'missing_payload'}`; anchors the 2026-05-05 heroes-side regression so the same crack can't reopen. (4) `lib/portal/role-mapping.ts` — `mapPortalRoleToFastRole()` normalises portal's enum (`'employee'|'leader'|'admin'`) to fast's column convention (`'member'|'leader'|'admin'`): leader/admin pass through verbatim, employee→member, unknown values return null so callers skip the update. (5) Seven per-event handlers in `lib/portal/handlers/`: user.provisioned (Prisma upsert keyed on `portal_sub`, applies mapped role), user.updated (delta-aware on `changedFields`), user.offboarded (`accountStatus='rejected'`), app_config.updated (role-only; teamId deliberately deferred because fast's local Team UUIDs don't yet reconcile with portal's 'teams' taxonomy keys), employment.updated (no-op until fast denormalises HR fields), alias.updated (no-op; fast has no alias cache), taxonomy.upserted + taxonomy.deleted (lands the T78 leg). (6) `lib/portal/dispatch.ts` — map of all 8 subscribed events → handlers + `dispatchPortalEvent(event, body)` that no-ops on unknown event names. (7) `app/api/webhooks/portal/route.ts` — `POST` handler that runs the route in order: missing `X-Portal-Event` / `X-Portal-Event-Id` → 400; missing env config → 500; missing/non-Bearer authorization → 401; failed `verifyGoogleIdToken` → 401; dedup via `prisma.portalWebhookEvent.createMany({skipDuplicates:true})` — 0 inserted means duplicate → 200 short-circuit; malformed envelope → 400; clean → `dispatchPortalEvent(event, unwrapped.payload)` → 200. Exports `export const dynamic = 'force-dynamic'` because the prisma round-trip can't run during `next build`. (8) Tests: 16 cases across three files — `unwrap-envelope.test.ts` (5 cases mirroring heroes' envelope-contract pin), `role-mapping.test.ts` (5 cases), `route.test.ts` (11 cases across header validation, OIDC env config, Bearer validation, dedup, dispatch, malformed body, missing payload). All mocks via `mock.module('@/lib/db' | '@/lib/portal/oidc' | '@/lib/portal/dispatch', ...)` so tests stay free of DB/Google/handler-side dependencies. (9) `apps/fast/package.json` gains `google-auth-library: ^9.15.1` (matches heroes-api's version) + `@coms-portal/sdk: workspace:*` (the webhook types live there). (10) Middleware allowlist at `apps/fast/middleware.ts:19` already covers `/api/webhooks` from T68 — no change needed. (11) `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast typecheck` exits 0; `bun test ./apps/fast/lib/portal/*.test.ts ./apps/fast/app/api/webhooks/portal/route.test.ts` reports 21 pass / 0 fail across 53 expect() calls; pre-existing fast tests (health + load-fast-auth-user) stay green. (12) The `app_webhook_endpoints.status` flip from `'disabled'` → `'active'` lands in an operator window — fast's webhook consumer is now live in code, but the portal won't dispatch until the row is flipped. The flip belongs alongside FU-22's `spec07-register-fast.ts` drift-detection upgrade since the row already exists in `app_webhook_endpoints` with the post-T76 URL.
  - **What stays for the operator window:** (a) `app_webhook_endpoints.status='disabled'` → `'active'` for fast's row in portal's DB so the portal starts dispatching; (b) `bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast db:push` actually applies the additive PortalWebhookEvent + TaxonomyCache tables to fast's Cloud SQL via the deploy workflow's `db:push` step (no `[skip-db-push]` token in the commit — the changes are additive and safe to auto-apply on next deploy); (c) end-to-end verification by triggering a portal-side test event and confirming the dedup row lands + the handler runs.

- [x] **T78: Taxonomy projection — `taxonomy_cache` table + initial sync — sealed 2026-05-14 (code-side)**
  - **Prerequisites:** T77
  - **What:** If fast consumes any portal-owned taxonomies (branches, teams, departments — survey fast's existing schema to see which), project them into a `taxonomy_cache` table mirroring heroes' Phase 5 shape (`packages/heroes-shared/src/db/schema/taxonomy-cache.ts`).
