  - **Acceptance:** `taxonomy_cache` table exists in fast's DB; initial sync populates entries; a `taxonomy.upserted` webhook updates the projection.
  - **Outcome:** four-piece slice landed alongside T77 (the taxonomy handlers + dispatch already needed the table, so bundling kept the commit cohesive). (1) Prisma schema gains the `TaxonomyCache` model with composite PK `(taxonomyId, key)` + `value` + `metadata Json?` + `cachedAt`, mapping to `taxonomy_cache` table; mirrors the heroes Drizzle shape at `packages/heroes-shared/src/db/schema/taxonomy-cache.ts` ported to Prisma. (2) `lib/portal/handlers/handle-taxonomy-upserted.ts` — per-row Prisma `upsert` keyed on the composite PK (Prisma doesn't surface multi-row INSERT-ON-CONFLICT cleanly; batch sizes stay in the tens per Spec 07's per-taxonomy-batch shape, so per-row cost is fine); `cachedAt` refreshes on every write so future TTL checks have a fresh anchor; metadata cast as `Prisma.InputJsonValue` because Prisma's Json type rejects `Record<string, unknown>` without an explicit assertion. (3) `lib/portal/handlers/handle-taxonomy-deleted.ts` — single `deleteMany({where: {taxonomyId, key: {in: keys}}})` in one round-trip; rows that no longer exist no-op silently. (4) `apps/fast/lib/portal/portal-api-client.ts` — outbound client mirrors `apps/heroes-api/src/lib/portal-api-client.ts`: cached `GoogleAuth` + per-audience `IdTokenClient` map; `fetchTaxonomySync()` calls `GET /api/taxonomies/sync` against `PORTAL_BASE_URL` and returns the typed response. Note: the actual portal-api endpoint is `/api/taxonomies/sync` (not `/api/v1/taxonomies/:id/entries` as the original task body imagined) — it returns all subscribed taxonomies in one call, gated by the caller's app-token (`requireAppToken()`) which authenticates the runtime SA's ID token against `app_registry.service_account_email`. (5) `apps/fast/scripts/sync-taxonomies.ts` — operator-runnable one-shot that iterates `fetchTaxonomySync().taxonomies` and upserts every entry via the same code path the webhook handler uses, so re-running is idempotent; runbook embedded as a header comment (impersonate `coms-fast-web-sa`, open Cloud SQL Auth Proxy on 5435, `PORTAL_BASE_URL=https://aha-coms.web.app`, `bun run apps/fast/scripts/sync-taxonomies.ts`). Typecheck + tests green alongside T77's verification.
  - **What stays for the operator window:** (a) initial sync run — `bun run apps/fast/scripts/sync-taxonomies.ts` against fast's prod DB with the runtime SA's ADC, after T77's `app_webhook_endpoints.status` flip so subsequent deltas ride the webhook; (b) verification — `SELECT taxonomy_id, COUNT(*) FROM taxonomy_cache GROUP BY taxonomy_id` returns one row for 'teams' with the entry count matching portal's count; (c) one full delta cycle — operator confirms a `taxonomy.upserted` webhook from portal updates the cache.

- [x] **T79: Health check endpoint — `GET /fast/api/health` — sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Prerequisites:** T76 (listed for the portal-side consumer; the route handler itself has no T76 dependency and lands ahead-of-schedule because T80's Cloud Run probe needs the route to exist before the first real GHA deploy)
  - **What:** Author `apps/fast/app/api/health/route.ts` returning 200 + a small JSON body (e.g., `{ status: 'ok', dbReachable: true, webhookSubscriptionActive: true }`) when fast's DB is reachable and the webhook subscription is registered. The endpoint serves two consumers: portal's dashboard probe (60-second polling) and Cloud Run's startup probe (`infra/fast/cloud-run.tf` startup_probe block).
  - **Acceptance:** `curl https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/health` returns 200; portal's dashboard card for fast flips to "healthy" within 60s; Cloud Run's startup probe succeeds.
  - **Outcome (code-side, complete):** `apps/fast/app/api/health/route.ts` authored with `export const dynamic = 'force-dynamic'` (the prisma round-trip can't run during `next build` — no DATABASE_URL, no Cloud SQL proxy — and force-dynamic stops Next.js from trying to prerender it), a `GET` handler that runs `await prisma.$queryRaw\`SELECT 1\`` (cheapest possible Postgres round-trip, no table scan, no lock) inside try/catch, and returns `{ status: 'ok' | 'degraded', dbReachable: boolean, timestamp: string }` with status code 200 on success, 503 on failure, and `Cache-Control: no-store, max-age=0` so Firebase Hosting's default CDN doesn't cache the body — a stale `ok` response would mask a real outage. **The `webhookSubscriptionActive` field T79's task description named is deliberately omitted** rather than reported as `false` while T77 is unwritten, so future consumers can read absence as "not yet implemented" vs. "actively broken" — adding the field as `false` today would mislead the portal dashboard into showing fast as degraded for a perfectly healthy state. **Three bun:test cases at `apps/fast/app/api/health/route.test.ts`** (TDD red→green via `mock.module('@/lib/db', ...)` replacing prisma's `$queryRaw`): valid query returns 200 + dbReachable:true; throwing query returns 503 + dbReachable:false; no-auth scenario confirms the handler works without `__session` (middleware at `apps/fast/middleware.ts:19` already allowlists `/api/health` for the container-direct probe path). **Same-commit crack-mend on `infra/fast/cloud-run.tf`:** T80 set the startup + liveness probe paths to `/api/health` (bare) on the theory that Next.js's basePath stripping would internalise external `/fast/api/health` to in-container `/api/health` — but the basePath stripping only applies when the external URL ARRIVES with the prefix. Cloud Run's probe machinery hits `localhost:3000` directly with no Firebase Hosting hop, so Next.js sees bare `/api/health`, finds no matching route (basePath '/fast' requires the prefix), and 404s the probe. Heroes-api uses the prefix-included shape (`/heroes/api/healthz`) for the same reason. Probe paths flipped to `/fast/api/health` in both `startup_probe` and `liveness_probe` blocks. The bootstrap hello-world image still responds 200 to any path, so the first apply's probe passes during the brief window before the GHA deploy swaps in a real revision; the corresponding comment in cloud-run.tf rewrote itself to explain why the prefix is required. The monitoring module's uptime check comment also rewrote — the check fires through Firebase Hosting (host `aha-coms.web.app`), which preserves the path verbatim through the rewrite to coms-fast-web, so the uptime probe path `/fast/api/health` was correct as authored; only the explanatory comment needed updating to record the post-T79 state.
  - **What stays for the operator window:** (a) full acceptance — `curl https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/health` returns 200 — cannot run until T83 brings the Cloud Run service up; (b) portal-side row two — after T76 registers fast in `app_registry` with `healthCheckUrl=https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/health`, the dashboard card flips green within 60 seconds; (c) the monitoring uptime alert stays `enabled = false` until the operator confirms one full check cycle returns success post-T83. T79 promotes to `[x]` once an operator records the curl probe + dashboard flip in this entry.
  - **Sealed (operator-window verified, 2026-05-14):** with T83 applied + the deploy-fast.yml workflow's `bd34483` deploying the real revision after the Prisma libssl pinning chain (commits `4723bf4` → `bd34483`), the live URL responds: `curl -sS https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/health` returns HTTP 200 with body `{"status":"ok","dbReachable":true,"timestamp":"…"}` — the prisma `SELECT 1` round-trip lands and the response shape matches the in-session test cases. The portal-dashboard row of the acceptance (T76's `healthCheckUrl` upsert + the 60-second probe flip) carries forward to the post-T76 operator window — `app_registry` doesn't yet hold fast's row so no portal-side consumer is firing the probe today; once T76 runs the registration script the dashboard will pick the route up automatically without another T79 touch. Monitoring uptime alert stays `enabled = false` for the same reason — once T76 lands and one full check cycle returns success, the operator flips the toggle in `infra/fast/main.tf`'s monitoring module call and re-applies. T79's code-side artefacts hold without further work; the route, the test file, and the IaC probe path mend remain in place.

- [x] **CHECKPOINT 18 — CROSSED 2026-05-14**: Fast is in `app_registry`. Cross-app navigation surfaces fast everywhere. Webhooks deliver and process correctly. Fast's profile shape stays in sync with portal's identity. After CP18, Phase 8 opens. **Operator window closed in three steps:** (1) `app_webhook_endpoints.status` flip from `disabled` → `active` via direct SQL UPDATE on portal's DB (FU-22 would have done it cleanly through `spec07-register-fast.ts`; deferred for the post-CP18 window — raw SQL got us there in this session). (2) `taxonomy_cache` seed via SQL-to-SQL copy from portal's `org_taxonomies` (13 rows for the `'teams'` taxonomy) — bypassed the `sync-taxonomies.ts` script entirely because the ADC impersonation path required `roles/iam.serviceAccountTokenCreator` on `coms-fast-web-sa` which the operator account didn't carry pre-window; granted the role + verified the impersonation works, but the SQL-to-SQL path was already complete by then so the script run rolls to a future operator window as a regression check. (3) End-to-end webhook delivery verified via `coms-portal-cli smoketest fast` (Spec 06 Rev 4 PR B): portal-api's `POST /api/v1/apps/fast/smoketest` dispatched an `app.smoketest` envelope to fast's webhook URL; first attempt 401'd at fast's verifier due to a `SELF_PUBLIC_URL`/audience mismatch (cloud-run.tf had it as `${fast_public_origin}/fast` but portal mints `aud=new URL(endpoint.url).origin=https://aha-coms.web.app`, no path suffix); fixed in two parts — (a) live `gcloud run services update --update-env-vars=SELF_PUBLIC_URL=https://aha-coms.web.app` got the verifier passing within seconds, (b) IaC follow-up commit aligned `infra/fast/cloud-run.tf` so the next deploy doesn't revert; smoketest retry returned `{"ok":true,"endpoints":[{"status":200,"latencyMs":303}]}` and `portal_webhook_events` now holds one dedup row for the test event. **Heroes-side crack filed as FU-24** — heroes' `SELF_PUBLIC_URL` carries the same suffix mismatch (set to its Cloud Run URL, not the Firebase Hosting origin); heroes' endpoint is currently `status='disabled'` so the crack hasn't surfaced through real traffic, but heroes' eventual re-enable will trip the same 401 unless the env is realigned first. **Operator-window grants applied:** `roles/iam.serviceAccountTokenCreator` on `coms-fast-web-sa` granted to `handers.the@ahacommerce.net` — operator-window-only utility for future smoketest runs from the dev workstation; if security policy wants this revoked after the session, it's a clean revoke.

### Phase 8: Per-service IaC + deploy workflows

Spec ref: `docs/spec/05-fast-onboarding.md#phase-8-per-service-iac--deploy-workflows`. Per-app principle: fast gets its own Tofu state bucket, runtime SAs, monitoring filters, Artifact Registry repo. Mirrors `infra/heroes/`'s shape exactly.

- [x] **T80: Author `infra/fast/` mirroring `infra/heroes/` — sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Prerequisites:** CP18 (or parallel after CP15)
  - **What:** Create `infra/fast/` with: per-app Tofu state bucket (`gs://coms-fast-tofu-state-XXXX`), `cloud-run.tf` defining `coms-fast-web` (unified per Option A — no separate `coms-fast-api`), `iam-fast-runtime.tf` declaring runtime SAs (`coms-fast-web-sa`), Artifact Registry repo (`coms-fast-registry`), monitoring filters + uptime check on `/fast/api/health`, the standard label set (`app="fast"`, `service="fast-web"`, `environment="prod"`, `managed-by="opentofu"` per standing principle 4). The existing `aha-fast/terraform/` is REFERENCE MATERIAL — the new IaC follows the `coms-<app>-<resource>` naming from standing principle 2, not aha-fast's legacy `aha-fast-*` shapes. Don't copy-paste; reauthor against the standing principles.
  - **Acceptance:** `cd infra/fast && tofu init` succeeds; `tofu plan -var alert_email=...` shows the new resources; no resource references `aha-fast-*` legacy names.
  - **Outcome:** `infra/fast/` lands as a 16-file Tofu state — `backend.tf` (bucket `coms-fast-tfstate`, prefix `tofu/state`), `providers.tf` (google ~> 7.0), `variables.tf` (project + region + Cloud SQL instance name + seven Secret Manager IDs + the public OAuth client ID and HR sheet identifiers as plaintext defaults), `labels.tf` (`fast_labels` + `fast_labels_web` per standing principle 4), `cloud-run.tf` (the single `coms-fast-web` service + runtime SA `coms-fast-web-sa` + Cloud SQL client grant + seven Secret Manager accessor bindings + GCS objectUser on the uploads bucket + iamcredentials API enabled), `main.tf` (wires artifact-registry, monitoring, github-wif modules), `outputs.tf` (Cloud Run URL + AR hostname + SQL connection name + runtime SA + WIF provider + deployer SA), `terraform.tfvars.example`. Three modules at `modules/{artifact-registry,monitoring,github-wif}/` mirror heroes' shape adapted for the single-service case: artifact-registry creates `coms-fast-registry`; monitoring takes a single `cloud_run_service_name` string (heroes takes a list because heroes is two services) and ships the uptime alert `enabled = false` until T79 lands `/fast/api/health`; github-wif declares `coms-fast-wif-pool` + `coms-fast-deployer-sa` + per-principal IAM bindings + act-as on the single runtime SA. **Cloud SQL is a data source, not a resource** — fast's existing `aha-fast-db-instance-cd5db712` (provisioned pre-merge under aha-fast's legacy terraform; per standing principle 1's recorded artefact) is referenced via `data.google_sql_database_instance.fast`, and the Cloud Run service mounts the proxy at `/cloudsql/<connection-name>`. The naming wart (`aha-fast-` prefix) stays — Cloud SQL rename in place is unsupported, and DMS migration to a `coms-fast-db-instance` would cost an outage the principle benefit doesn't justify. **`apps/fast/Dockerfile` authored alongside** — fast carried no Dockerfile in the tree (the legacy aha-fast repo had one at root, npm-based with node:20; not portable to the monorepo Bun workspace). New Dockerfile mirrors heroes-web's three-stage shape: `oven/bun:1` deps stage (workspace-aware COPY of all per-service package.jsons + the Prisma schema before `bun install --frozen-lockfile` triggers `prisma generate` via the postinstall hook), `oven/bun:1` builder stage (`bun run --filter @coms-portal/fast build` runs `next build` with the `output: 'standalone'` config landed at T65), `node:20-slim` runtime stage (Next.js standalone output is a Node entry, not a Bun one) serving `apps/fast/server.js` on port 3000. **Verification:** `tofu fmt -check -recursive` clean across `infra/`; `tofu init -backend=false && tofu validate` returns "Success! The configuration is valid." inside `infra/fast/`; YAML parse of the new workflow passes; `bun --filter '@coms-portal/fast' typecheck` stays green (IaC-only change shouldn't move it; this confirms). **What stays operator-only:** T83 — the first `tofu apply` window. The plan call is to apply WITHOUT a destroy of the legacy `aha-fast-app` Cloud Run service or the four `aha-fast-*` Secret Manager secrets that already hold live values — the new state references those secrets by ID, not by resource block, so the apply is purely additive (creates `coms-fast-web` + `coms-fast-web-sa` + WIF pool + AR repo + monitoring; touches nothing else). The legacy `aha-fast-app` service stays alive on its own state until T70 verifies the new corridor against `aha-coms.web.app/fast/*`, then a separate operator window retires it. **Secrets the operator must create before the first `coms-fast-web` revision serves real traffic** — the existing `aha-fast-db-url` carries a valid DSN (legacy aha-fast wrote it), and `aha-fast-broker-signing-secret` + `aha-fast-auth-secret` + `aha-fast-webhook-hmac` are pre-existing; the remaining five (`aha-fast-google-client-secret`, `aha-fast-resend-api-key`, `aha-fast-apps-script-secret`, `aha-fast-slack-webhook-url`, `aha-fast-cron-secret`) currently live as plaintext env vars on the legacy `aha-fast-app` service and need migrating to Secret Manager in the same operator window. FU-15's password-rotation chain folds into the same window — the `aha-fast-db-url` value carries the prod DB password in cleartext; rotating it across DB + Secret Manager + redeploy is the canonical sequence.

- [x] **T81: Author `.github/workflows/deploy-fast.yml` — path-filtered + WIF + db:push step — sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Prerequisites:** T80
  - **What:** Mirror `.github/workflows/deploy-heroes-api.yml` and `deploy-heroes-web.yml`'s shape, combined into one workflow since fast is unified. Path filters on `apps/fast/**` (excluding test-only paths if any). WIF auth via fast's WIF deployer SA (`coms-fast-deployer-sa`). The `db:push` step (using Prisma's `prisma db push --skip-generate` since fast doesn't carry a migrations folder) runs BEFORE the docker build, mirroring portal-api's FU-3 + heroes-api's FU-5 ordering. The workflow comment NAMES the destructive-migration caveat — T64's `DROP TABLE` shape needs deploy-first-then-migrate ordering and that doesn't fit the migrate-first-then-deploy default; operator handles destructive migrations manually outside the workflow.
  - **Acceptance:** `gh workflow view deploy-fast.yml` shows the file is registered; a probe push touching `apps/fast/README.md` triggers ONLY the fast workflow (path filter isolation proven).
  - **Outcome:** `.github/workflows/deploy-fast.yml` authored at 6.7 KB. Path filters on `apps/fast/**`, `packages/ui-react/**`, `packages/account-widget-react/**`, `packages/design-tokens/**`, `packages/sdk/**`, `packages/shared/**`, `package.json`, `bun.lock`, the workflow file itself. Concurrency group `deploy-fast` with `cancel-in-progress: false` (deploys serialise per service). Env block names the constants (`SERVICE_NAME=coms-fast-web`, `ARTIFACT_REPO=coms-fast-registry`, `RUNTIME_SA=coms-fast-web-sa@…`, `CLOUD_SQL_INSTANCE=fbi-dev-484410:asia-southeast2:aha-fast-db-instance-cd5db712`, `DB_URL_SECRET=aha-fast-db-url`). Six steps: checkout → WIF auth (against `WIF_PROVIDER_FAST` + `WIF_SA_FAST` repo vars T82's outputs surface) → setup-gcloud → setup-bun → cache bun install → `bun install --frozen-lockfile` → `prisma db push` via Cloud SQL proxy on port 5433 (`timeout-minutes: 5`; sed rewrites the host:port segment of fast's DSN from `34.101.176.36:5432` to `127.0.0.1:5433` rather than heroes' Unix-socket rewrite shape — fast's stored DSN uses the public-IP form per legacy aha-fast/terraform/main.tf's outputs.tf; the proxy intercepts the IPV4 host) → docker build via `apps/fast/Dockerfile` → docker push → `gcloud run deploy coms-fast-web --service-account=coms-fast-web-sa@…`. Workflow comment names the destructive-migration caveat in three sentences — fast carries no migrations directory; `prisma db push` is non-destructive for additive shapes; a `DROP TABLE` (T64's drop of Session/Account/Verification is the canonical exception) needs deploy-first-then-migrate ordering that this workflow's migrate-first-then-deploy default doesn't cover. The comment also names "fail fast at 5 minutes" as a stuck-proxy / runaway-DEFAULT signal — pattern carries from heroes-api. **YAML parse passes** via `python3 -c "import yaml; yaml.safe_load(...)"`. **What stays for the operator window:** path-filter isolation proof — push a no-op commit to `apps/fast/README.md` (currently exists in the tree per T56's subtree merge), confirm only `Deploy — fast` fires in `gh run list`, no portal-* or heroes-* runs. Cannot probe until T83 creates the WIF pool the workflow authenticates against; sequence is `tofu apply infra/fast/` first, then set the two repo vars (`gh variable set WIF_PROVIDER_FAST --body "projects/908739514002/locations/global/workloadIdentityPools/coms-fast-wif-pool/providers/github-oidc"` and `gh variable set WIF_SA_FAST --body "coms-fast-deployer-sa@fbi-dev-484410.iam.gserviceaccount.com"`), then the probe push.

- [x] **T82: Register fast's WIF deployer SA — `coms-fast-deployer-sa` + IAM bindings — sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Prerequisites:** T80
  - **What:** IaC declaration of the WIF deployer SA + workload-identity-pool + provider, bound to the GitHub repo + ref pattern matching `mrdoorba/aha-coms`. Per-service runtime SA (`coms-fast-web-sa`) is separate from the deployer (per-app principle 5's runtime-SA distinction). Grant the runtime SA: Cloud SQL Client (for the Cloud SQL Postgres connection), Secret Manager Secret Accessor (for DATABASE_URL + any other secrets), Cloud Storage Object Viewer (if fast reads from a GCS bucket — survey fast's existing terraform for the binding shape).
  - **Acceptance:** `gcloud iam service-accounts list --project=fbi-dev-484410 | grep coms-fast` shows both `coms-fast-deployer-sa` + `coms-fast-web-sa`; the WIF provider is bound to the GitHub repo.
  - **Outcome:** WIF declarations folded into `infra/fast/modules/github-wif/` (the IaC equivalent of "register the SA"). Pool `coms-fast-wif-pool` with provider `github-oidc` (`attribute.repository == 'mrdoorba/aha-coms'`); deployer SA `coms-fast-deployer-sa` with `roles/iam.workloadIdentityUser` granted to the WIF principalSet, `roles/run.admin` + `roles/artifactregistry.writer` + `roles/cloudsql.client` + `roles/secretmanager.secretAccessor` at project scope, and `roles/iam.serviceAccountUser` + `roles/iam.serviceAccountTokenCreator` on the single runtime SA `coms-fast-web-sa` (heroes' module takes a list of runtime SAs because heroes is two services; fast's takes a single string). Module outputs `provider_name` + `deployer_service_account_email` surface at the parent state's `outputs.tf` as `wif_provider` + `wif_service_account` — these are what `gh variable set WIF_PROVIDER_FAST` and `gh variable set WIF_SA_FAST` consume after `tofu apply`. Runtime SA `coms-fast-web-sa` lives in `cloud-run.tf` (not the WIF module — it belongs to the service, not the deploy mechanism) with three IAM grants: Cloud SQL Client at project scope, Secret Manager Secret Accessor (for_each across the seven secret IDs the Cloud Run env block references), GCS objectUser on the legacy `aha-fast-uploads-prod` bucket. **Verification: same as T80** (validate + fmt; module structure verified by `tofu init -backend=false` resolving all three modules without error).

- [x] **T83: First IaC apply window — `tofu apply` in infra/fast/ — sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Prerequisites:** T80, T81, T82, **operator-only**
  - **What:** Operator runs `cd infra/fast && tofu init && tofu plan -var alert_email=... && tofu apply` per the laptop-CLI runbook (`infra/README.md`). New Cloud Run service `coms-fast-web` comes up with a bootstrap image (hello-world). First GHA deploy via `deploy-fast.yml` lands fast at the new infra.
  - **Acceptance:** `gcloud run services list --project=fbi-dev-484410 | grep coms-fast` shows the new service; the GHA deploy completes green; `curl https://coms-fast-web-XXX.run.app/fast/api/health` returns 200.
  - **Outcome:** the first-apply walked twelve operator windows (Op-1 through Op-12) across 2026-05-14. **Op-1**: state bucket precreate (`gcloud storage buckets create gs://coms-fast-tfstate --location=asia-southeast2 --uniform-bucket-level-access`) + `tofu init` + first `tofu plan -var alert_email=...` — surfaced four resource cracks that the next four ops mended in-place rather than in destructive recreation. **Op-2** (`a39d115`): trimmed `infra/fast/`'s secret references from the original audit's seven IDs to what `cloud-run.tf` actually wires — Resend deliberately excluded (FU-18 retiring), Slack deliberately excluded (FU-17 uncalled), cron moved to plaintext-via-tfvars per `variables.tf`'s threat-model note, inbound webhook HMAC dormant until T77 lands the consumer. Final wired set is three Secret Manager IDs (`aha-fast-db-url` + `aha-fast-google-client-secret` + `aha-fast-apps-script-secret`); the audit comment in `variables.tf` records what was excluded and why. **Op-3** (folded into the same window): FU-15's prod DB password rotation alongside `aha-fast-db-url`'s Secret Manager refresh — the cleartext password the seed scripts had leaked at commit `03a31f0`'s working-tree scrub got rotated in Cloud SQL + the secret's new version written, so the live DSN no longer matches the historical leak. The git history rewrite (FU-19) stays separate. **Op-4** (`7a865d7`): the uploads bucket default in `variables.tf` started as `coms-fast-uploads-prod` per principle 2's naming, but the live bucket is `aha-fast-uploads-prod` (legacy aha-fast/terraform created it; rename in place is non-trivial on GCS for a bucket with live objects). Default corrected to match reality; the naming wart stays as-is per principle 1's recorded artefact. **Op-5**: `tofu apply` against the corrected plan — created `coms-fast-web` Cloud Run service + `coms-fast-web-sa` + `coms-fast-deployer-sa` + `coms-fast-wif-pool` + `github-oidc` provider + `coms-fast-registry` Artifact Registry repo + monitoring uptime check (`enabled = false`) + the iamcredentials API enablement. **Op-6** (`805ee0f` + `4723bf4`–`bd34483`): path-filter isolation probe + the Dockerfile chain. The probe push touched `apps/fast/README.md`; only `Deploy — fast` fired in `gh run list` (no portal-* or heroes-* runs) — path-filter isolation proven. Then the deploy-fast workflow's first six runs failed in succession on Dockerfile cracks: workspace resolution across all five Dockerfiles (`4723bf4`), the postinstall hook running inside the workspace (`3666880`), missing root `package.json` in the builder stage (`83efe36`), Prisma's binary-targets mismatch between Debian 12 builder and Debian 11 runtime (`43fbafd`), and finally the libssl1.1 / Debian Bullseye pin (`bd34483`) — Prisma 5.22.0's runtime detection picks the `debian-openssl-1.1.x` query engine binary even on a Bookworm host, so the runtime stage pinned to `node:20-bullseye-slim`. Seventh run green. **Op-7** (`84dab7c`): match legacy `aha-fast-app`'s always-warm shape — Path X (`min_instance_count = 1`, `cpu_idle = false`) — recorded inline as the deliberate choice for fast (vs. portal/heroes' `min=0` + uptime-probe-induced warmth Op-12 surfaced). **Op-8**: WIF repo-var registration via `gh variable set WIF_PROVIDER_FAST` + `gh variable set WIF_SA_FAST` from the apply's outputs; verified by `gh variable list` showing both with the asia-southeast2 provider path + the deployer SA email. **Op-9**: not numbered separately — folded into Op-6's deploy retries. **Op-10** (`4fc602d`): destructive-migration escape hatch — the deploy workflow's `prisma db push` step now respects a `[skip-db-push]` token in the commit message that the Op-6 chain used to avoid running migrations during Dockerfile iteration; the same token will gate T64's eventual operator-driven destructive apply. **Op-11**: live verification — `curl -sS https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/health` returns HTTP 200 with `dbReachable:true`; `curl -sS -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code} %{redirect_url}" https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/dashboard` returns 307 → `https://aha-coms.web.app/portal?app=fast&redirect_to=%2Ffast%2Fdashboard` (middleware T68 firing correctly for unauthed page requests). **Op-12** (`d1770a0`): the uptime-probe-induced always-warm finding surfaced during monitoring discussion and queued against FU-21's cost audit; structural finding, no infra change in the same commit. **What stays open from the T83 surface:** (a) full T70 corridor walk — the sign-in chain (portal sign-in → land at `/fast/` → cross-app navigation → logout) is operator-led and waits on the next operator window. The middleware redirect on the unauthed page request was verified by curl in this session, so the structural path holds; only the authenticated journey is unwalked. (b) CP14 destructive apply — `prisma/sql/0002_drop_better_auth_tables.sql` runs separately against fast's Cloud SQL via Cloud SQL Auth Proxy; gated on T60's backfill having populated `portal_sub` for every active user.

- [x] **CHECKPOINT 19 — CROSSED 2026-05-14**: `coms-fast-web` Cloud Run service live. Deploy workflows run end-to-end. Path-filter isolation proven by Op-6's single-file probe push (commit `805ee0f`, only `Deploy — fast` fired in `gh run list`). After CP19, Phase 9 opens — but T72–T75 (Phase 6 chrome mount) is the next code-side pickup since CP15's authenticated walk waits on an operator window and Phase 6 doesn't.

### Phase 9: PWA installability + service worker

Spec ref: `docs/spec/05-fast-onboarding.md#phase-9-pwa-installability--service-worker`. The third PWA on the shared origin. Per FU-10's structural fix, scope-overlap collisions are prevented at the manifest layer — fast's `start_url`/`scope`/`id` all at `/fast/` are disjoint from portal's `/portal/` and heroes' `/heroes/`.

- [x] **T84: PWA manifest — start_url + scope + id all `/fast/` — sealed 2026-05-14 (live curl verified)**
  - **Prerequisites:** CP19
  - **What:** Author the manifest with `name: "AHA Fast"`, `short_name: "Fast"`, `start_url: "/fast/"`, `scope: "/fast/"`, `id: "/fast/"`, `display: "standalone"`, `theme_color` + `background_color` matching fast's brand (indigo/purple gradient — survey existing brand colors), `icons` declared at 192×192 + 512×512 sizes pointing at `/fast/icons/icon-{192,512}.png`. Generate the icons via the same ImageMagick pattern FU-6 used for portal-web + heroes-web — fast-branded variant (indigo gradient `#XXXX → #YYYY` + bold "F" letter). Reference the manifest from `apps/fast/app/layout.tsx`'s `<head>` (Next.js metadata API).
  - **Acceptance:** the manifest file exists at the right path; icons exist at the declared paths; `curl https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/manifest.webmanifest` returns the JSON; Lighthouse PWA audit's "manifest" check passes.
  - **Outcome:** `apps/fast/app/manifest.ts` rewritten — fast had a manifest in the tree already, but it predated the basePath flip (T65) and carried the polyrepo-era "AHA COMSS" branding with `start_url: '/'` and unprefixed icon paths. New shape: `name: 'AHA Fast'`, `short_name: 'Fast'`, `start_url`/`scope`/`id` all `'/fast/'` (closes the FU-10 scope-overlap collision at the manifest layer for the three-PWA case), `background_color` flipped from `#ffffff` to `#0F0E7F` matching fast's brand deep-navy (alongside the existing `theme_color`), icon `src` paths carry the `/fast/` prefix explicitly because Next.js's metadata API doesn't auto-prefix manifest values (FU-10 lesson held). The existing 192/512 icons at `apps/fast/public/icon-{192,512}.png` stay — they're fast-blue gradients already; the rebranding from "AHA COMSS" → "AHA Fast" is the only naming move (no fresh ImageMagick run needed). **What stays for T86:** the operator's Lighthouse audit + on-device install verification. Manifest acceptance via `curl https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/manifest.webmanifest` waits on the next deploy; the existing 2026-05-14T08:00:40 deploy didn't include this change, so an operator who curls today still gets the pre-T84 JSON. Status `[~]` until the deploy lands + operator confirms the manifest shape against the live URL.

- [x] **T85: Service worker — `/fast/`-prefixed paths + API skip guard — sealed 2026-05-14 (live curl verified)**
  - **Prerequisites:** T84
  - **What:** Author the SW: cache `[build, files]` on install, prune stale caches on activate, cache-or-network on fetch with API skip-guard reshaped for `/fast/api/*` (so authenticated API calls never serve stale). The FU-10 lesson stands: SW scope is automatically `/fast/` (from the manifest scope) so heroes/portal fetches don't transit fast's worker. Register the SW from `app/layout.tsx` (client-side `useEffect` or a small client component).
  - **Acceptance:** the SW file exists; `curl https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/service-worker.js` returns the JS; visiting `/fast/` registers the SW; Chrome DevTools → Application → Service Workers shows the worker at `/fast/` scope.
  - **Outcome:** `apps/fast/public/sw.js` rewritten + `apps/fast/components/PWAInstaller.tsx` updated. The pre-existing `sw.js` carried unprefixed paths (`/`, `/aha-logo.png`, `/icon-192.png`, etc.) under cache name `aha-comss-v48` — every reference broke after T65's basePath flip because Firebase Hosting serves under `/fast/*` and the worker fetched the un-rewritten roots. Cache name flipped to `aha-fast-v1` (semantic rename surfaces the boundary cleanly; activate handler's prune list eats the old `aha-comss-v*` cache shape on next install). STATIC_ASSETS list re-prefixed: `/fast/`, `/fast/aha-logo.png`, `/fast/icon-192.png`, `/fast/icon-512.png`, `/fast/manifest.webmanifest`. Fetch handler's API skip-guard flipped from `/api/` to `/fast/api/` so authenticated calls bypass the worker; the SSE skip stays as-is (header-based, basePath-orthogonal). Static-asset cache-first match adjusted: `/fast/aha-logo.png` literal plus `/fast/_next/static/` prefix. HTML offline fallback returns the cached `/fast/` shell instead of `/`. Worker `scope` inherits from the manifest's `/fast/` scope so heroes/portal fetches stay outside fast's worker — FU-10's structural fix holds at the worker layer too. **PWAInstaller.tsx** registration path flipped from `/sw.js` to `/fast/sw.js` — Next.js client-side fetch calls aren't auto-prefixed by basePath, so the literal string had to update. **Verification:** `bun --filter '@coms-portal/fast' typecheck` green; `build` green (manifest route still emits at `○ /manifest.webmanifest`, public file count unchanged). **What stays for T86:** live worker registration + Chrome DevTools → Application → Service Workers showing scope `/fast/`; operator confirms during the same window the manifest audit runs. Status `[~]` until the deploy lands + operator records the live scope.

- [x] **T86: Lighthouse PWA audit + on-device install verification — sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Prerequisites:** T85, **operator-only** (mobile device)
  - **What:** Run Lighthouse PWA audit against `https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/` — installability, manifest, service-worker categories all pass. Fix whatever the audit flags. Operator on-device verification on Chrome mobile + Brave mobile: install fast as PWA from the browser → home-screen tile renders with the fast icon → open from home screen → splash + standalone chrome render correctly. **Crucially, install all three PWAs (portal, heroes, fast) on the same device** — confirm each appears as a distinct tile with its own icon + scope (closes the multi-app PWA model FU-10 unlocked).
  - **Acceptance:** Lighthouse PWA audit passes all three categories; mobile install succeeds; three distinct tiles on the home screen render correctly when launched.
  - **Outcome — captured during T87 walk's Step 8 (2026-05-14):** Lighthouse 100% PWA against `/fast/track` (the public surface; `/fast/` auth-redirects to portal/login for unauthenticated Lighthouse runs which would audit portal's PWA properties rather than fast's). Canonical artifact at `apps/fast/docs/t86-lighthouse.report.html`. Every audit green: installable-manifest, splash-screen, themed-omnibox, viewport, maskable-icon, plus three manual audits informational. `/fast/request` audited separately scored 88% with one failing audit (`content-width`, viewport 439px vs window 412px → 27px overflow on the form layout) — tracked as T87 Finding 11, deferred (cosmetic, single-page, not a PWA infrastructure break). Evidence at `apps/fast/docs/t86-lighthouse-request.report.html`. **Lighthouse-12 caveat:** the smoke checklist's original `--only-categories=pwa` flag threw on `lighthouse@latest` (Lighthouse 12 retired the bundled PWA category in 2024); checklist now pins `lighthouse@11` with a migration note — T87 Finding 10, mended in same commit. **On-device install (Android Chrome):** fast installs via "Add to home screen → Install" with tile labeled "Fast" (manifest's `short_name`) carrying the AHA brand mark icon (deep-navy circular gradient); launches in standalone mode (no browser address bar); empty dashboard while unauthenticated, populated post-sign-in (normal middleware redirect flow). Heroes installs as a full PWA with H icon and "AHA Heroes" tile. **Portal only offers "Add shortcut"**, not the full install — portal-web lacks PWA installability requirements (missing manifest fields or unregistered service worker). Logged as T87 Finding 14, deferred — CP21 is Spec 05 (fast onboarding), not portal cleanup; track separately as portal-web Phase-7-or-later work for full three-app PWA install symmetry. **FU-10 three-tiles-one-device proof:** three distinct tiles on the home screen with three distinct icons + names — spirit holds, even with portal as a shortcut (portal's tile still distinct from fast + heroes; cross-scope behavior remains as Chrome's scope_extensions heuristics handle it). Brave repeat skipped per operator triage — same browser engine class, Chrome verification is enough for CP21 acceptance.

- [ ] **CHECKPOINT 20: Fast is installable as a distinct PWA from portal-web and heroes-web.** Three install registrations live on the shared origin, scoped by start_url. After CP20, Phase 10 opens. **Code-side prerequisites sealed 2026-05-14 (T84 + T85).** Operator-side closer: step 6 of [`apps/fast/docs/runbook-cp14-cp20-window.md`](../apps/fast/docs/runbook-cp14-cp20-window.md) — Lighthouse PWA audit + on-device install of all three PWAs on Chrome (Android) + Brave for the three-tiles-one-device proof FU-10 promised.

### Phase 10: Verification + documentation

Spec ref: `docs/spec/05-fast-onboarding.md#phase-10-verification--documentation`. The closing checklist before CP21 seals Spec 05.

- [x] **T87: End-to-end smoke (mirrors T47's checklist for heroes) — code-side authored 2026-05-14; operator walk sealed 2026-05-14**
  - **Prerequisites:** CP20, **operator-led** for the walk
  - **What:** Execute the full smoke checklist against prod:
    - Sign in via portal → land on fast (when portal launcher links to fast).
    - Navigate within fast (dashboard, channels, tasks, analytics, orbit, etc.).
    - Cross-app navigation: portal → fast, heroes → fast, fast → portal, fast → heroes — every direction.
    - Logout from one app → verify logged out everywhere (cross-app session invalidation).
    - Mobile chrome: install PWA from a clean device, log in, verify chrome looks identical to portal's + heroes'.
    - Admin operations: fast's leader-only views (analytics, user control panel) work post-cutover; the gating logic in T73's SlideOverNav prop respects the `user.role === 'leader'` check.
    - Public surfaces: `/fast/request` + `/fast/track` + `/fast/api/employees` reachable without authentication (middleware T68 doesn't gate them).
    - Google Calendar OAuth: connect a calendar, list events, create a meeting — all green after the redirect-URI update (T67).
    - Slack webhook: submit a request, confirm Slack delivery (app-internal, unchanged by the migration).
  - **Acceptance:** every checklist item passes; any regressions documented as Findings (mirror T47's Finding-N pattern). Findings that block CP21 get mended same-session; cosmetic findings can land as separate follow-ups.
  - **Outcome (code-side, complete):** authored `apps/fast/docs/smoke-checklist.md` as the operator-facing standalone document T47 never had on heroes' side (heroes' T47 lived as a long todo.md entry — fast carries a parallel checklist file so the operator can walk it without scrolling through this todo). The checklist covers eight surfaces mapped to integration-contract clauses: §1 sign-in, §3 chrome render (desktop + mobile), §3+§5 cross-app navigation, §7 admin operations (load + write), §1 escape hatch public surfaces (`/request` + `/track`), §5 OAuth round-trip, §11 webhook delivery (sub-steps 7a/7b/7c), §9 PWA install. Each step has the URL, expected output, recording shape, and a "findings to expect" preamble naming the most likely failure mode at that step. A recovery table mirrors the runbook's "When things go sideways" pattern with eight rows covering the known cracks (e.g., step 4's loopback-fetch trap is the heroes-T47-Finding-1 mirror — Server Components calling `/fast/api/*` from inside fast's own server-side rendering pass; the recovery row points the operator at converting the loader to a direct `lib/` import). FU-24's `SELF_PUBLIC_URL` audience check + the heroes-side patterns lifted from T47 (mobile two-bar artifact, public-surface allowlist, OAuth redirect-URI registration) are folded into the relevant steps so the operator hits each known crack with the recovery in front of them. The doc ends with a "Closer — sealing CP21" section naming what flips in todo.md when every step passes (T87 + CHECKPOINT 21 + optionally T75 closer + T86 if covered during step 8).
  - **What stays for the operator window:** execute the eight-step walk live against `https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/*`. Estimated 30–45 minutes if no findings surface. Record outcome per step in this entry's body; flip T87 + CP21 to `[x]` once the walk passes cleanly.
  - **Operator walk 2026-05-14 — twelve findings surfaced across the eight steps; six mended in-session, six deferred.** F1 / F3 / F4 / F6 / F8 / F10 mended in commits `3f00375` + `a1f4557` + the CP21 seal commit (the third for F10's docs pin). F2 / F5 / F9 / F11 / F14 deferred as documented follow-ups. F7 is informational (Google infrastructure observation, not an app concern). The pattern echoes heroes' T47 (which surfaced five findings); fast's brownfield context produced more — two basePath-drift classes (F4 + F8 + F9, all stemming from the same Phase-4 migration), three documentation drifts (F6 / F10 / the icon-description docs nit folded into the seal commit), and the rest split between auth-broker (F2), brand cleanup (F5), Lighthouse 12 ergonomics (F10), responsive layout (F11), GCloud infrastructure (F7), and portal-web PWA install gap (F14). Two findings (F12 / F13) were named during triage and dismissed before logging — F12 was the operator's tile-label observation ("Fast" not "AHA Fast" — by design, manifest's `short_name`), F13 was a misread of normal middleware redirect flow.
    - **Finding 1 — `auth/unauthorized-domain` blocking sign-in (mended in-session).** Step 1 opened `/fast/dashboard` in incognito → 307 to portal sign-in → "Continue with Google" threw `Firebase: Error (auth/unauthorized-domain)` before the OAuth consent screen could render. The Identity Platform's `authorizedDomains` list for project `fbi-dev-484410` carried only `localhost`, `fbi-dev-484410.firebaseapp.com`, `fbi-dev-484410.web.app`, and `coms-portal-app-45tyczfska-et.a.run.app` — **the named hosting site `aha-coms.web.app` was missing**. Default-project `.web.app` and `.firebaseapp.com` domains are auto-allowed, but `aha-coms` is a *named* Firebase Hosting site under the project (the hosting-site name diverges from project ID `fbi-dev-484410`), so the named-site domain was never auto-added. Mended via Identity Platform admin API PATCH (`identitytoolkit.googleapis.com/admin/v2/projects/fbi-dev-484410/config?updateMask=authorizedDomains`) appending `aha-coms.web.app` to the list under `handers.the@ahacommerce.net`'s access token; verified via independent read-back. **Why this didn't surface in CP14–CP20:** earlier authenticated walks must have run against the default-project URL (`fbi-dev-484410.web.app`) or the Cloud Run direct URL, not the named hosting site. The smoke checklist's "Sign-in loops back to portal" recovery row should grow an `auth/unauthorized-domain` recovery line for the named-hosting-site case — logged as a small follow-up.
    - **Finding 2 — `portal_code` + `portal_redirect_to` linger in URL after sign-in (deferred).** Post-auth, the user lands at `/fast?portal_code=heL4xtyxCrZhEEhkuzwUmpNBJQemZNmH&portal_app=fast&portal_redirect_to=%2Ffast%2Fdashboard` with the broker code visible in the URL bar and the `redirect_to` silently dropped. Auth still works because the `__session` cookie is set portal-side during the OAuth flow, but fast has no consumer for the auth-broker exchange params: `grep -rn 'portal_code\|portal_redirect_to\|portal_app' apps/fast/` returns zero hits; the emission lives in `apps/portal-api/src/services/auth-broker.ts`. **Why deferred:** not a CP21 blocker (auth functionally works); proper mend requires the auth-broker exchange handler in fast (server-side route or middleware add at `app/page.tsx` that consumes `portal_code`, calls portal-api's broker exchange endpoint, strips the params, redirects to `portal_redirect_to`). Picks up post-CP21 with proper scope. Open as a Phase 11 follow-up — likely tracked alongside the auth-broker dual-mode cleanup window.
    - **Finding 3 — `/fast/dashboard` returned 404 (mended in-session).** Pre-mend: typing `https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/dashboard` directly returned Next's 404 with chrome attached. Root cause: fast's dashboard implementation lived at `apps/fast/app/page.tsx` → `/fast/` (after basePath), not at `app/dashboard/page.tsx`. The runbook + smoke checklist + portal's `redirect_to` parameter all expected `/fast/dashboard` to be canonical; heroes' parity is at `/heroes/dashboard` (`apps/heroes-web/src/routes/(authed)/dashboard/+page.svelte`), so fast was the parity outlier. **Mend:** `git mv apps/fast/app/page.tsx apps/fast/app/dashboard/page.tsx` (clean rename, content unchanged); the new `apps/fast/app/page.tsx` is a server component that calls `redirect('/dashboard')` from `next/navigation` — Next's basePath-aware redirect emits `Location: /fast/dashboard` (308). `bun --filter '@coms-portal/fast' typecheck` exits 0; `build` exits 0 with route table showing `┌ ○ /` (the new redirect page) + `├ ○ /dashboard` (the moved implementation), both prerendered as static content.
    - **Finding 4 — Sidebar Dashboard link resolved to `/fast/fast` (mended in-session).** Pre-mend: clicking the Dashboard tile in the contextual sidebar took the operator from `/fast?portal_code=…` to `/fast/fast` (404). Root cause: `apps/fast/components/layout/Sidebar.tsx` line 63 had `{ href: '/fast', icon: LayoutDashboard, label: 'Dashboard' }`; under `basePath: '/fast'` Next.js's `<Link>` prepends basePath to absolute paths, yielding `/fast/fast`. All other sidebar entries (`/tasks`, `/messages`, `/analytics`, `/activity-log`, `/changelog`, `/users`, `/orbit`, `/profile`) correctly used module-relative paths without the prefix; only Dashboard had the prefix bug — a single-line drift from when basePath was introduced (T65). **Mend:** changed `href: '/fast'` → `href: '/dashboard'` so Next's basePath prepend lands the user at `/fast/dashboard` (the F3 canonical URL). The `isActive` check on line 248 (`pathname === itemPath`) continues to work: `usePathname()` returns paths without basePath, so `/dashboard === /dashboard` matches when the user is at `/fast/dashboard`. TopNav's brand `<Link href="/">` (line 313) is correct as-is — basePath prepends to give `/fast/`, which then redirects to `/fast/dashboard` via the F3 mend.
    - **Finding 5 — Legacy "AHA COMSS" brand text in 9 places (deferred).** The polyrepo-era brand "AHA COMSS" (double-S) survives across fast in nine touch points: `components/layout/TopNav.tsx:319` (brand text in TopNav header), `app/layout.tsx:13` + line 19 (page `title` + Open Graph title), `components/PWAInstaller.tsx:64` ("Install AHA COMSS" prompt), `components/CalendarMeetingSection.tsx:1097` (calendar disconnect copy), `app/changelog/page.tsx:130` (changelog subtitle), `app/request/page.tsx:524` (back-link label), `app/api/tasks/[id]/comments/route.ts:172` (task-comment email footer), `app/manifest.ts:18` (manifest comment naming the rename). T84 only rebranded the PWA manifest's user-visible name (`name: 'AHA Fast'`, `short_name: 'Fast'`); the in-app strings were untouched. **Why deferred:** cosmetic, not a corridor break; CP21 can seal with this open. Scheduled as a separate task — straightforward 9-place find-and-replace once a brand-cleanup window opens.
    - **Finding 6 — Smoke checklist's Step 4 admin URLs didn't match fast's actual routes (mended in-session).** Pre-mend: Step 4's checklist named `/fast/admin`, `/fast/admin/teams`, `/fast/admin/changelog`, `/fast/admin/audit-log` — none of which exist as user-navigable routes in fast (only `apps/fast/app/api/admin/sync-hr/route.ts` exists, a single internal HR sync endpoint). The actual admin-equivalent surfaces in fast live flat: `/fast/users` (User Control Panel landing, leader-gated via `requireLeader: true`), `/fast/users?tab=teams`, `/fast/users?tab=roles`, `/fast/changelog`, `/fast/activity-log`. **Mend:** rewrote Step 4's URL list in `apps/fast/docs/smoke-checklist.md` against the actual route shape; the heroes-T47-Finding-1 loopback-fetch context was preserved as the recovery row since the pattern still applies to any future Server Component additions in fast. The underlying architectural decision — whether fast should grow a structural `/admin/*` namespace mirroring heroes' `/heroes/admin/*` for symmetry — is deferred as an open question alongside the Phase 11 review; current flat-admin shape is what's deployed and what Step 4 now walks against.
    - **Finding 7 — `GAESA` cookie set by Google Cloud Run session affinity (informational).** Surfaced during Step 1's DevTools cookie check alongside the expected `__session`. Verified via `curl -sSI https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/` showing `Set-Cookie: GAESA=...` from `Server: Google Frontend`. Set by Google's edge infrastructure when a Cloud Run service has `--session-affinity` enabled; routes subsequent requests from the same client to the same Cloud Run instance — almost certainly for fast's SSE notification stream continuity (the dashboard's notification bell consumes a long-lived SSE connection; stickiness avoids reconnecting on every backend hop). 237 bytes/request overhead. `HttpOnly=false / Secure=false / SameSite=blank` is correct for an affinity routing hint (not a security boundary). Portal's `/portal/*` responses don't carry the cookie — portal's Cloud Run service doesn't have session affinity enabled. **Why informational, not a finding to mend:** GAESA is infrastructure, not app-local; doesn't violate the spirit of the auth-corridor "one `__session` only" rule (which targeted `coms_session` / `better-auth.session` revival). The fast vs portal asymmetry is an open question for post-CP21 review — either disable affinity on fast (if SSE has graceful reconnect handling, the routing overhead becomes unnecessary) or enable it on portal (consistency across the suite). Logged so CP22+ doesn't re-investigate from scratch.
    - **Finding 8 — basePath-prefix drift in client-side fetch URLs across 6 sites (mended in commit `a1f4557`).** Step 6 surfaced what looked like a Google Calendar sync issue: the "Google Calendar Connected" pill was green but the Calendar widget rendered no external GCal events. Tracing the client-side fetch path identified the crack at `apps/fast/components/CalendarMeetingSection.tsx:125` — the events URL was `let url = ` followed by a backtick-quoted `/api/google-calendar?action=events…` with no `/fast` prefix. Under `basePath: '/fast'`, Next.js does not auto-prepend basePath to client-side `fetch()` calls; the request hit `https://aha-coms.web.app/api/google-calendar?...` (a 404 path). A grep audit surfaced **five more sites** with identical drift: `CalendarMeetingSection.tsx:170` (fast meetings read), `orbit/RoutineTemplateForm.tsx:200` (template save), `orbit/milestones/page.tsx:107` (milestone save), `team-inbox/page.tsx:215` (inbox list), `changelog/page.tsx:98` (changelog publish). Each silently returned empty / no-op so Step 4's load-path walk came back green — the pages rendered without 500-ing, but the underlying list / save paths were broken. The shape of the drift is consistent: URL built via a `let url = ` or `const url = … ? : …` conditional construction; fixed-string fetches were caught during the Phase-4 basePath migration. **Mend:** six one-line edits, each prepending `/fast` to the path string. Build green; deploy `25862630270` carried the fix to prod; the Calendar widget now renders external GCal events end-to-end across the month grid (verified live by the operator post-deploy). Same Phase-4 root cause as F4 — together F4 + F8 define the basePath-drift class in `<Link href>` + client fetches; F9 below extends the class into `history.replaceState` URLs.
    - **Finding 9 — `history.replaceState` basePath + wrong-path drift in CalendarMeetingSection (deferred).** Sibling drift to F8 at `apps/fast/components/CalendarMeetingSection.tsx:158`: `window.history.replaceState({}, '', '/tasks')` lacks basePath (would set the URL bar to `/tasks` rather than `/fast/tasks`) AND points at the wrong path entirely. The CalendarMeetingSection widget moved from `/tasks` to the dashboard in an earlier sweep but this clear-the-params handler kept the original target as a hardcoded string; after a meeting-notification deep-link consumes its `?date=` / `?meetingId=` params, the URL bar would flip to `https://aha-coms.web.app/tasks` (which 404s if the user reloads). **Why deferred:** low-impact (only fires when a meeting notification deep-link is consumed) and the right target is its own decision — `window.location.pathname` minus query, or an explicit `/fast/dashboard`. Mend it alongside the broader basePath-drift sweep that F4 + F8 only touched at the surface level. Likely the third leg of the same migration class; logged together for whoever picks up the sweep.
    - **Finding 10 — Lighthouse 12 retired the `--only-categories=pwa` flag (mended docs).** When Step 8's Lighthouse command ran against `lighthouse@latest`, the audit failed with `Runtime error encountered: unrecognized category in 'onlyCategories': pwa`. Lighthouse 12 (released 2024) removed the bundled PWA category score — the individual audits (installable-manifest, service-worker, viewport, themed-omnibox, content-width, apple-touch-icon, maskable-icon, splash-screen) still exist but are no longer aggregated. **Mid-walk workaround:** pin to `lighthouse@11` (the last major with the PWA category bundle); `npx -y lighthouse@11 ...` succeeded and produced the 100% score on `/fast/track`. **Smoke checklist updated** in this seal commit: Step 8's command now reads `lighthouse@11` and the comment names the long-term migration option (Lighthouse 12's per-audit invocation via `--only-audits=installable-manifest,service-worker,viewport,themed-omnibox,content-width,apple-touch-icon,maskable-icon,splash-screen,offline-start-url`). The pin is intentional and named in-comment — future ops know they're on `@11` and why.
    - **Finding 11 — `/fast/request` form mobile-viewport overflow (deferred).** Lighthouse audit on `/fast/request` scored 88% PWA with one failing audit: `content-width` reporting "viewport size 439px vs window size 412px" — a 27px horizontal overflow on mobile. A separate audit run against `/fast/track` (the other public surface) returned 100% PWA with `content-width=PASS`, so the overflow is specific to `/fast/request`'s form layout (1586 lines; likely culprits inside `whitespace-nowrap` spans, fixed-width form elements, or absolute-positioned tooltips/popovers). **Why deferred:** cosmetic, single-page issue, not a PWA infrastructure break. The canonical Lighthouse artifact at `apps/fast/docs/t86-lighthouse.report.html` reflects the 100% `/track` baseline; `apps/fast/docs/t86-lighthouse-request.report.html` keeps the F11 evidence on disk for the future mend window. The mend will need DevTools mobile emulation to find the overflowing element.
    - **Finding 14 — portal-web lacks PWA installability (deferred).** During Step 8's on-device three-PWA install on Android Chrome, fast and heroes both offered the full "Install app" option but portal only got "Add shortcut" (a regular bookmark, not a PWA install). Portal-web (SvelteKit) is likely missing one of: a manifest with all required PWA fields at the served path (`name`, `short_name`, `start_url`, `scope`, icons sized 192 + 512, `display: standalone`), a registered service worker, or HTTPS serving (almost certainly the first or second since portal serves over HTTPS). **Impact on T86:** the FU-10 three-tiles-one-device proof's spirit still holds — three distinct tiles on the home screen with three distinct icons + names — but portal's tile is a shortcut, not a PWA, so it doesn't share fast's standalone scope semantics. **Why deferred:** CP21 is Spec 05 (fast onboarding), not portal cleanup. Track separately as portal-web Phase-7-or-later work so the three-app suite gets full PWA install symmetry. The smoke checklist's "Step 8 should install all three as PWAs" expectation needs a soft caveat noting portal's pending status — the docs update belongs alongside the portal-web mend.
  - **Operator walk 2026-05-14 — eight-step outcomes:**
    - **Step 1 (Sign-in via portal, §1):** PASS post-F1 mend. Browser issued `GET /fast/dashboard` → 307 to `/portal/login?redirect=...` → portal login rendered after F1's Identity Platform authorized-domains PATCH; "Continue with Google" reached the consent screen, sign-in completed, browser landed at `/fast?portal_code=…` (briefly, before the F3 redirect cleaned it post-deploy). `__session` cookie verified: `HttpOnly=true`, `Secure=true`, `SameSite=Lax`, `Path=/`, `HostOnly=true`, no `coms_session` / `better-auth.session` / app-local cookies. GAESA cookie observed (F7, informational). The redirect chain `/fast/dashboard → 307 → /portal/...` (unauthenticated) confirmed live on curl probe.
    - **Step 2 (Chrome render, §3):** PASS. Desktop layout (ServiceBar 36px / TopNav 64px / Sidebar collapsed 64px at `top:[100px]`) renders correctly across both themes. AccountWidget popover verified with full shape (name, email, `ADMIN` badge, Manage account, three-entry app launcher with `FAST` marked `HERE`, Sign out). Mobile (390×844 viewport) drops the ServiceBar and surfaces TopNav + BottomNav. Post-Finding-4-strip TopNav right cluster shows only the notification bell. Three T75 closer screenshots captured + saved to `apps/fast/docs/t75-screenshots/`.
    - **Step 3 (Cross-app navigation + sign-out, §3, §5):** PASS. ServiceBar tab cycle Fast → COMS → Heroes → Fast preserved `__session` across all three; no re-auth. Sign-out via AccountWidget cleared `__session`; the landing was `/heroes/logged-out` (heroes' app-specific page) rather than the bare-domain `/` the checklist named — heroes-specific UX rather than a corridor-wide redirect, accepted as PASS; the checklist's expected destination should grow a soft caveat ("originating app's logged-out page, or `/` if no app-specific page is configured"). Re-auth gate verified on second `/fast/dashboard` visit.
    - **Step 4 (Admin operations, §7):** PASS after F6 docs rewrite. Five admin-equivalent surfaces (`/fast/users`, `/fast/users?tab=teams`, `/fast/users?tab=roles`, `/fast/changelog`, `/fast/activity-log`) loaded clean with data + no console errors + no 5xx. Write path verified by toggling a user's role member ↔ leader; change persisted on reload. The heroes-T47-Finding-1 loopback-fetch trap did NOT surface — fast's admin pages are client-component-driven (fetch `/fast/api/...` from the browser), not Server Components doing loopback. **Caveat:** Step 4's load-path test only checks for 500s; F8's silent-failure paths (team-inbox empty, orbit save broken, changelog publish broken) didn't 500, they just returned empty — visible only when actually exercised. Surfaced in Step 6 instead.
    - **Step 5 (Public surfaces `/request` + `/track`, §1 escape hatches):** PASS. `/fast/request` rendered without portal redirect (middleware allowlist at `apps/fast/middleware.ts:19` honoured), submission persisted with a reference code, `/fast/track` surfaced the status by code, admin team-inbox surfaced the submitted task. End-to-end public-anonymous flow + admin-side handoff verified.
    - **Step 6 (OAuth round-trip Google Calendar, §5):** PASS post-F8 mend. OAuth init from a disconnected state generated a chooser URL with the correct `redirect_uri=https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/auth/google/callback` — T67's registration held. The consent screen requested scopes `calendar + chat.spaces.readonly + chat.messages + chat.memberships.readonly` (bundled rather than incremental — observation, not a finding). External GCal events did NOT render in fast's calendar widget initially despite the green "Connected" pill — traced to F8 (basePath drift in 6 client-side fetches). F8 mended in commit `a1f4557`; deploy `25862630270` carried to prod; post-deploy verification showed the widget renders the operator's real GCal events across the month grid (FBI: Update Issue, Cek Barang Baru, Weekly Meeting PR - FBI, FBI/CIA Laboratory, FBI: Bottom Partner Focus, Briefing Tim, CIA/FBI Projects). Round-trip contract satisfied.
    - **Step 7 (Portal webhook delivery, §11):** PASS all three sub-steps. **7a (portal DB):** `app_webhook_endpoints` JOIN `app_registry` WHERE `slug='fast'` returned `status=active, last_failure_reason=NULL, failure_count=0`. **7b (smoketest):** curl POST to `https://aha-coms.web.app/api/v1/apps/fast/smoketest` with an impersonated ID token (Bearer JWT minted via `gcloud auth print-identity-token --include-email --impersonate-service-account=coms-fast-web-sa@…`) returned `{"ok":true,"endpoints":[{"endpointId":"ca0886c5-...","url":"https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/webhooks/portal","status":200,"latencyMs":576}]}` with HTTP 200. The endpoint URL correctly carries `/fast/api/webhooks/portal`; `SELF_PUBLIC_URL` env on fast's Cloud Run service is correctly the bare origin (FU-24 lesson held). **7c (fast DB):** `portal_webhook_events` returned `events_ever=2, most_recent=2026-05-14 13:33:04+00` (the 2nd row was the smoketest just fired — dedup chain alive); `taxonomy_cache` returned one row for `teams` with 13 entries, matching portal's `org_taxonomies` seed.

Brave repeat skipped per operator triage (same browser engine class as Chrome; coverage sufficient for CP21).

- [x] **T88: Performance check — p50/p95 against pre-migration baseline — sealed 2026-05-14 (becomes the new baseline)**
  - **Prerequisites:** T87, **operator-led**
  - **What:** Capture cold + warm p50/p95 for the fast dashboard load (sign-in → /fast/dashboard render). Compare against a pre-migration baseline captured before T56's subtree merge (if no baseline exists, T87's measurement IS the baseline going forward). Expectation per the integration contract: flat-or-faster vs Better Auth's session-row lookup since `__session` introspection is approximately the same wire cost as the previous DB roundtrip.
  - **Acceptance:** post-migration p50/p95 within ±15% of baseline (or faster). Outside that band, the gap gets diagnosed — per-route breakdown identifies whether the regression lives in `loadFastAuthUser`'s `/api/userinfo` introspection, the React chrome SSR overhead, or fast-internal query changes.
  - **Outcome — baseline captured during T87 walk (2026-05-14):** 20 back-to-back curl samples against each of two URLs from `handers.the@ahacommerce.net`'s gcloud-authenticated session, measuring `time_total` + `time_starttransfer` (TTFB) + `time_connect` (TCP+TLS handshake). **`/fast/track`** (public surface, full HTML render — proxy for authenticated dashboard render speed): p50=**252ms**, p95=**479ms**, min=189ms, max=494ms; TCP+TLS handshake stable at p50=22ms. **`/fast/dashboard`** (auth-redirect first hop, middleware path): p50=**264ms**, p95=**549ms**, min=188ms, max=565ms — middleware adds ~12ms at p50, ~70ms at p95 vs `/track`. First sample of each batch (potentially cold): 210ms and 205ms respectively — no cold-start blip because earlier Lighthouse runs had warmed the Cloud Run instances. **Pre-migration baseline did not exist** (per this entry's "if no baseline exists, T87's measurement IS the baseline going forward" clause). These numbers become the new baseline; CP22+ regression checks compare against them. **Caveat:** curl measures server-side TTFB only — the full user-perceived "sign-in → dashboard render" includes React hydration + client-side data fetches (`/fast/api/dashboard/widgets`, `/fast/api/google-calendar`, `/fast/api/team-inbox`, `/fast/api/messages`, `/fast/api/changelog`) which curl can't capture. Raw sample data saved at `apps/fast/docs/t88-perf-baseline/track-samples.txt` + `dashboard-samples.txt`. A DevTools Performance recording is the next-level measurement when the next perf window opens.
