- [x] **FU-26: Set the corridor wards on `main` before the second engineer (@alifm17) joins — sealed 2026-05-15**
  - **Surface:** before this FU, `main` was protected by GitHub's legacy branch protection alone — `required_status_checks: [Typecheck & unit tests, Lint hardcoded URLs]`, `allow_force_pushes: false`, `enforce_admins: false`, no review requirement, no Code Owner routing, no bypass-actor mechanism. Adequate for a single-principal repo; insufficient for the @alifm17 onboarding window opening this week — he co-owns `apps/fast/` going forward, must not be able to push to `main` directly, and must block on @mrdoorba's review whenever his PRs reach beyond `apps/fast/`. FU-19 partial-1's force-push had to relax-then-restore `allow_force_pushes` to land (line 992 region's "Branch protection ... rejected the first attempt" trail); the legacy config has no bypass-actor concept, so the dance was unavoidable.
  - **What landed.** Four artifacts in commit `8f94b54` plus a `Sequence 0` org team + a `Sequence 0 — main protection` ruleset created via `gh api` in the same operator window:
    1. **`Sequence 0` org team** (ID `17550162`, slug `sequence-0`) — one-person team in `AHA-Commerce-CIA-Project`, @mrdoorba as maintainer, `privacy: closed`. Pure identity carrier for bypass actors; carries no repo permissions of its own. Required `admin:org` token scope; @mrdoorba's `gh` token was refreshed mid-window (logout-then-login after the `HandersThe → mrdoorba` rename surfaced a cached-account collision in `gh auth refresh`).
    2. **`Sequence 0 — main protection` ruleset** (ID `16424290`) targeting `~DEFAULT_BRANCH` with four rule blocks: `pull_request` (1 approval + `dismiss_stale_reviews_on_push: true` + `require_code_owner_review: true` + all three merge methods allowed), `required_status_checks` (`Typecheck & unit tests` + `Lint hardcoded URLs`, no strict-up-to-date), `non_fast_forward` (block force-push), `deletion` (block branch delete). Bypass actors: the `Sequence 0` team, `bypass_mode: always`.
    3. **`.github/CODEOWNERS`** — routing for the Code Owner gate. `* @mrdoorba` fallback; `/apps/fast/ @mrdoorba @alifm17` (co-owned, self-approval forbidden so @mrdoorba's approval always required); `/packages/`, `/infra/`, `/.github/` each → @mrdoorba alone.
    4. **`.github/pull_request_template.md`** — soft prompt auto-filling the PR description with a cross-app-impact checklist. Not a gate; surfaces shared-package reach at PR creation time for the reviewer.
    5. **`apps/fast/CLAUDE.md`** (Code modification section) — rewritten end-to-end. The pre-FU-26 text instructed Mr. Door voice + `Author: Mr. Door` anchor for every commit; that voice is the operator's personal signature and now reserved exclusively for @mrdoorba. The Fast engineer's commits use plain technical English with four mandatory trailers (`Confidence` / `Scope-risk` / `Tested` / `Related`) — searchable via `git log --grep`. `Co-Authored-By: Claude` lines and the `🤖 Generated with [Claude Code]` footer are explicitly forbidden (Claude Code's defaults insert both; his Claude must strip them before commit). The branch-protection paragraph refreshed to describe the new ruleset + CODEOWNERS routing he should expect.
  - **Why now:** @alifm17's org invite is days from going out. The gate must exist before his account becomes a push principal; once he accepts, the routing applies against his identity immediately. Authoring the gate retroactively (e.g., after a misroute) is brittle — easier to set the wards while there is only one principal in the org.
  - **Verification — smoke test PR #5 (opened + closed 2026-05-15, no merge, branch + file torn down):** throwaway branch `smoke/sequence-0-gate-test` with a one-file change at `tasks/.smoke-sequence-0` (routing via `* @mrdoorba`). PR opened against `main`; `gh pr view --json mergeStateStatus,reviewDecision,reviewRequests,statusCheckRollup` returned `mergeStateStatus: BLOCKED`, `reviewDecision: REVIEW_REQUIRED`, both required status checks attached (workflow `CI — PR validation`, status `IN_PROGRESS` at read time), `reviewRequests: []`. The empty `reviewRequests` is GitHub's documented "no self-request" behaviour — @mrdoorba is the PR author and the only Code Owner for the matched path, so the auto-request silently no-ops; the gate still applies via `reviewDecision`. When @alifm17 opens a PR touching `/apps/fast/`, `reviewRequests` will land on @mrdoorba correctly. PR #5 closed via `gh pr close --delete-branch`; the smoke file existed only on the deleted branch and is gone from the repo.
  - **Open follow-up — legacy branch protection consolidation:** today both protection systems run on `main` simultaneously. The legacy protection's `allow_force_pushes: false` still blocks force-pushes from everyone (including Sequence 0 members), so FU-19 partial-2 (when FU-18 (b)'s engineer steps close) will again need the relax-restore dance against the legacy config — even though the ruleset's `non_fast_forward` would bypass for Sequence 0 natively. Once the ruleset has owned the gate through one full operator cycle without surprise (one force-push window resolved, one cross-app review cycle observed), the legacy protection can be deleted. Not in scope now; the redundancy is intentional defense-in-depth during the transition window. Tracked in ADR 0012's reopen criteria §2.
  - **Architectural record:** [`docs/adr/0012-sequence-0-main-protection.md`](../docs/adr/0012-sequence-0-main-protection.md) codifies the decision (three options weighed, Option B adopted), the team-based bypass model, and the reopen criteria for revisiting the access-control shape.
  - **Related:** ADR 0012 (the access-control ADR this FU lands alongside); FU-19 partial-1 (line 992 region — the force-push incident the bypass model is designed to make less brittle); FU-19 partial-2 (still gated on FU-18 (b); reopens the legacy-consolidation question when it lands); FU-20 (org transfer to `AHA-Commerce-CIA-Project`, the precondition for any of this); FU-18 (b) (Apps Script HMAC engineer-side closure); commits `8f94b54` (three-wards commit) + `b49884d` ("Lay the threshold brief at apps/fast/CLAUDE.md") + `f53af62` ("Retire seven stale AGENTS.md scrolls").

- [ ] **FU-27: Retire the legacy `aha-fast-app` Cloud Run service + stale `aha-fast-run-sa` SA + legacy OAuth callback URI**
  - **Surface:** with Spec 05's cutover sealed (CP21 crossed 2026-05-14), production traffic for `/fast/*` flows entirely through Firebase Hosting → `coms-fast-web`. The legacy `aha-fast-app` Cloud Run service (created 2026-03-26 in the alifm17/aha-fast era) still runs in `fbi-dev-484410 / asia-southeast2` on its 100%-traffic revision `aha-fast-app-00457-65t`, last deployed 2026-05-13 — pre-cutover and unchanged since. No user-facing path reaches it: `app_registry.url` was rewritten via direct SQL during the CP14→CP20 operator window (line 1284 region) so portal's launcher routes to `https://aha-coms.web.app/fast`; Firebase Hosting rewrites `/fast/**` to `coms-fast-web` exclusively. The legacy service exists today as a rollback target only. Two stale adjacent resources also linger: (a) the planned-runtime SA `aha-fast-run-sa@fbi-dev-484410.iam.gserviceaccount.com` (verified to exist, not disabled) — never actually attached to a live service since Cloud Run pinned to the default compute SA `908739514002-compute@developer.gserviceaccount.com` instead. (b) The Google OAuth client "AHA Fast" still carries `https://aha-fast-app-908739514002.asia-southeast2.run.app/api/auth/google/callback` as a registered redirect URI alongside the new `https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/auth/google/callback` (T67's outcome named it "kept registered through one rollback window — until the post-T70 revision has served at least one real OAuth round-trip successfully, after which the old URI retires in a separate operator visit"; both predicates now satisfied as of 2026-05-14).
  - **Why now:** T70's rollback gate passed 2026-05-14. Every precondition the plan named has crossed (`app_registry` no longer points at the legacy URL; Firebase Hosting no longer rewrites to it; OAuth round-trip on the new URI succeeded; CP14 destructive cut sealed against the live DB). Retaining the legacy carries ongoing Cloud Run baseline cost (the legacy revision is `min=1, cpu_idle=false` always-warm — the Op-7 shape FU-21 then audited away from on `coms-fast-web`), pollutes `gcloud run services list` for future operators trying to reason about what is live vs historical, and keeps the OAuth client carrying a dead callback URI (small but real phishing-surface concern — an attacker who somehow took over the legacy run.app hostname could intercept the OAuth code-exchange leg). Retirement removes the dead surface without delivery risk.
  - **What to retire** (operator window, ordered for reversibility):
    1. **Verify nothing still targets the legacy service.** `gcloud logging read 'resource.type="cloud_run_revision" AND resource.labels.service_name="aha-fast-app"' --project=fbi-dev-484410 --freshness=7d --limit=20` — if the last 7 days show real request logs (not just internal probes), STOP and investigate. Also scan `app_registry` + `app_webhook_endpoints` (both should already be `coms-fast-web-sa@…` / `aha-coms.web.app/fast/...` post-CP20) and Cloud Scheduler jobs (`gcloud scheduler jobs list --project=fbi-dev-484410 --location=asia-southeast2`) for any legacy-URL references.
    2. **Capture recovery artefact + (optional) pull traffic to zero.** Snapshot first: `gcloud run services describe aha-fast-app --project=fbi-dev-484410 --region=asia-southeast2 --format=export > /tmp/aha-fast-app-pre-retire.yaml`. Then optionally zero traffic for a 24–48h watch: `gcloud run services update-traffic aha-fast-app --to-revisions=aha-fast-app-00457-65t=0 --project=fbi-dev-484410 --region=asia-southeast2`. Any latent dependency surfaces as a 503. Skip the zero-traffic step if (1)'s log read showed nothing real.
    3. **Delete the Cloud Run service.** `gcloud run services delete aha-fast-app --project=fbi-dev-484410 --region=asia-southeast2`.
    4. **Delete the stale planned-runtime SA.** First list its bindings (`gcloud projects get-iam-policy fbi-dev-484410 --flatten='bindings[].members' --filter="bindings.members:aha-fast-run-sa"` — record any results before deletion as a rollback aid). Then `gcloud iam service-accounts delete aha-fast-run-sa@fbi-dev-484410.iam.gserviceaccount.com --project=fbi-dev-484410`.
    5. **Remove the legacy OAuth redirect URI.** Google Cloud Console → APIs & Services → Credentials → "AHA Fast" OAuth 2.0 Client. Delete `https://aha-fast-app-908739514002.asia-southeast2.run.app/api/auth/google/callback`; keep `https://aha-coms.web.app/fast/api/auth/google/callback`. Save. Verify by reconnecting Google Calendar from `/fast/profile?tab=integrations` (disconnected → connected round-trip).
  - **What NOT to retire** (legacy-named but production-load-bearing — keep verbatim):
    - GCS bucket `aha-fast-uploads-prod` (Op-4 recorded the naming-wart artefact; holds live uploaded files).
    - Cloud SQL instance `aha-fast-db-instance-cd5db712` (production DB, referenced by `coms-fast-web` via `data.google_sql_database_instance`).
    - Secret Manager secrets `aha-fast-db-url`, `aha-fast-apps-script-secret`, `aha-fast-google-client-secret` (production secrets wired into `coms-fast-web` per `infra/fast/cloud-run.tf`).
    - The default compute SA `908739514002-compute@developer.gserviceaccount.com` (project-wide, used by other workloads — only its implicit binding to `aha-fast-app` dies when the service is deleted).
  - **Acceptance:** `gcloud run services list --project=fbi-dev-484410 --region=asia-southeast2 | grep aha-fast-app` returns empty; `gcloud iam service-accounts list --filter='email~aha-fast-run-sa'` returns empty; the OAuth client lists only the `aha-coms.web.app` redirect URI; one OAuth round-trip via `/fast` succeeds post-cleanup; the recovery artefact (`/tmp/aha-fast-app-pre-retire.yaml`) is captured pre-delete so revival is one `gcloud run services replace` away if it ever needs to come back.
  - **Rollback path** if production turns out to depend on the legacy: re-create the Cloud Run service from the captured yaml (`gcloud run services replace /tmp/aha-fast-app-pre-retire.yaml --project=fbi-dev-484410 --region=asia-southeast2`); re-add the OAuth URI in GCC; recreate the SA + bindings from step 4's captured policy. Service + URI recreation is minutes; SA recreation depends on having the IAM-binding catalogue from the pre-delete list — which is why step 4 captures it explicitly.
  - **Related:** T70 (the rollback gate, sealed 2026-05-14); T67 (the OAuth URI's "kept through one rollback window" outcome, line 1218 region); the CP14→CP20 operator window's SQL `UPDATE` on `app_registry` (line 1284 region); FU-26 (the corridor wards landed alongside; this FU closes the retirement gap the wards work surfaced); FU-21 (the always-warm audit that proved fast doesn't need `min=1, cpu_idle=false` — the legacy still carries that costly shape); `tasks/plan.md`'s "stays alive on its separate state until T70 verifies" line.

- [x] **FU-28: Carry standing principle 4 into monitoring — `user_labels` on every alert + email channel in heroes + fast — sealed 2026-05-15**
  - **Surface:** the labels audit triggered by FU-26's reindex pass surfaced a six-resource gap in monitoring against the contract `infra/{heroes,fast}/labels.tf` documents verbatim ("every Tofu-managed resource in this state that supports labels carries `heroes_labels` / `fast_labels`"). Both monitoring modules were silently violating that contract since their authoring — none of the four `google_monitoring_alert_policy` resources (heroes' `cloud_run_5xx` via `for_each` over api+web + heroes' `cloud_sql_cpu` + fast's `cloud_run_5xx` + fast's `cloud_sql_cpu`) nor either `google_monitoring_notification_channel` (heroes' email + fast's email) carried `user_labels`. Both Terraform attributes have been available the whole time; the modules just never declared them.
  - **What landed.** Six file edits adding the labels plumbing through both modules plus the caller wiring, then a `tofu apply` against each state:
    1. `infra/heroes/modules/monitoring/variables.tf` + `infra/fast/modules/monitoring/variables.tf` — added `variable "labels"` with a description naming the principle-4 contract.
    2. `infra/heroes/modules/monitoring/main.tf` + `infra/fast/modules/monitoring/main.tf` — added `user_labels = var.labels` to each `google_monitoring_alert_policy` and to each `google_monitoring_notification_channel`. On the notification channel the existing `labels = { email_address = … }` (channel-type-specific config) stays untouched alongside the new `user_labels` (GCP resource labels) — both attributes are distinct and unrelated, with an inline comment block recording the distinction so the next reader doesn't conflate them.
    3. `infra/heroes/main.tf` + `infra/fast/main.tf` — added `labels = local.heroes_labels` / `labels = local.fast_labels` to the `module "monitoring"` invocation, mirroring how the artifact-registry, storage, cloud-sql, and sheet-sync modules already consume the same locals.
  - **Apply outcomes (both states, 2026-05-15 operator window):**
    - `infra/heroes` plan: `0 to add, 4 to change, 0 to destroy`. Apply complete in ~5s — 2× `cloud_run_5xx` (coms-heroes-api + coms-heroes-web alert policy IDs `8179133544274575091` + `14125157946724925065`) + 1× `cloud_sql_cpu` (`6549300033564426528`) + 1× email channel (`15302484317179561040`) all gained `{app=heroes, environment=prod, managed-by=opentofu}` via in-place updates. Zero Cloud Run revision impact; alerts continued firing against the existing notification channel through the update window.
    - `infra/fast` plan: `0 to add, 3 to change, 0 to destroy`. Apply complete in ~2s — `cloud_run_5xx` (`14576641611026226057`) + `cloud_sql_cpu` (`14226376154634966841`) + email channel (`17993169666117716218`) all gained `{app=fast, environment=prod, managed-by=opentofu}`.
  - **Cross-check.** Post-apply, every label-able GCP resource managed by `infra/`, `infra/heroes/`, and `infra/fast/` now carries the principle-4 label set. The remaining unlabeled resources fall into two named categories the audit handles correctly: (a) resources without a `labels` / `user_labels` argument in the Terraform google provider — `google_cloud_tasks_queue` (`webhook_delivery` in `infra/cloud-tasks.tf`) and `google_cloud_scheduler_job` (`otp_cleanup` in `infra/cloud-scheduler.tf`); (b) resources without GCP-side label support by design — every `google_*_iam_member` binding, `google_service_account`, `google_iam_workload_identity_pool` + provider, `google_project_service` API enablement, `google_sql_database`, `google_sql_user`, `google_secret_manager_secret_version`, `google_logging_project_bucket_config`. Both categories are documented inline at the top of each `labels.tf`; future audits can `grep -rn 'labels\|user_labels' infra/` and reconcile against that catalogue without re-deriving the gap.
  - **Incidental fmt drift cleanup** folded into the same commit: `infra/fast/cloud-run.tf:141` (one extra-space-alignment line in the `fast_runtime_secret_env` local) and `infra/terraform.tfvars:24-28` (over-aligned `service_url` block from a prior session); both surfaced by `tofu fmt -recursive` and accepted in place since the formatting drift is unrelated cosmetic noise that would otherwise re-surface on the next operator's fmt pass.
  - **Related:** standing principle 4 (cost attribution + audit via labels, codified in `tasks/plan.md`); FU-21 (the always-warm audit that retired heroes' + fast's uptime probes from the same monitoring modules earlier, leaving alerts + email channels as the surviving label-able surface); commit `8f94b54` (FU-26's three-wards landing whose reindex pass surfaced this gap); commit `265476c` (FU-27, the legacy-aha-fast-app retirement that motivated re-auditing the IaC label coverage in the same operator pass).
